Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
12 min
Compensation for Child's Eye, Penis, Tongue When Health Unknown
Inter-madhhab dispute with expansion on proof and method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling of government adl for organs with uncertain health, identify the Shafi'i objection, and apply the principle that presumption cannot impose liability.

Core Idea
Uncertainty in an organ's health prevents full diyah; only government adl is due.

This lesson examines a key disagreement between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding compensation for injury to a child's eye, penis, or tongue when the health of the organ is unknown. The Hanafi school holds that only government adl (hukumat adl) is obligatory, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues that full diyah is due based on the presumption of health. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi usul approaches liability when facts are uncertain.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: when the health of a child's eye, penis, or tongue is unknown, only government adl is due, not full diyah.
Government adl is compensation assessed by experts based on the loss, not a fixed amount.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that full diyah is obligatory because health is the predominant condition in these organs, analogizing to the soft part of the nose and the ear where full diyah is due.
The Shafi'i analogy relies on qiyas: the nose and ear have full diyah because beauty is their purpose; similarly, health is the purpose here.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis reject the analogy: the purpose of the eye, penis, and tongue is benefit (manfah), not beauty, and since benefit is uncertain when health is unknown, full compensation cannot be imposed. The presumption of health (ghalabat al-sihha) is not sufficient to impose liability.
Hanafi usul principle: al-zann la yughni 'an al-haqq – presumption does not establish certainty for imposing obligations.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If health is uncertain, Hanafis award less compensation (adl), while Shafi'is award full diyah. Once health is proven, both schools agree on full diyah or qisas.
The difference arises only during the period of uncertainty.
5
Apply the method of establishing health
The passage explains how health is determined: tongue health through speech, penis through movement, eye through signs of sight. Crying at birth is not speech; mere crying does not prove the tongue's health.
Once health is established, the ruling matches that of an adult: qisas for intentional, diyah for erroneous.

تشریح پیدائش کے وقت اگر بچہ رویا اور اس کے علاوہ دیگر ذرائع سے اس کی زبان کی صحت معلوم نہ ہوسکی تو صرف حکومت عدل واجب ہے کیونکہ یہ رونا کچھ کلام نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ تو محض ایک آواز ہے بلکہ زبان کی صحت کلام سے اور ذکر کی حرکت جنبش سے اور آنکھ کی ایسی چیز سے جس سے دیکھنے پر استدلال ہو سکے معلوم ہوگی۔

اور جب اس کے اعضاء مذکورہ کی سلامتی معلوم ہوگئی پھر اس کا حکم بالغ کا حکم ہو گا لہذا عمد ا کاٹنے کی صورت میں قصاص اور خطاء میں دیت واجب ہوگی۔
And concerning the eye of a child, his penis, and his tongue when health is not known, it is government adl. Al-Shafi'i said: Full diyah is obligatory therein because health is predominant, so it resembles cutting the soft part of the nose and the ear. Our proof: The purpose of these organs is benefit, so when their health is not known, full arsh is not obligatory due to doubt, and the apparent (presumption) is not valid as proof for imposition, unlike the soft part of the nose and the protruding ear because the purpose is beauty, and he has completely destroyed that beauty. Commentary: When it is known regarding a child that he sees, speaks, and his penis moves, that is a sign of soundness of those organs, so in that case full diyah is obligatory by consensus. But if their soundness and health had not yet become known and someone cut them, then there is a difference between Imam Shafi'i and us. He said: Since the overwhelming presumption is that these organs are sound, on that basis, just as diyah is obligatory for the soft part of the nose and the ear, similarly diyah will be obligatory for the mentioned organs. We said: Diyah will not be obligatory; rather, government adl (is due). And we answered his proof by saying: The overwhelming presumption and the apparent (evidence) are proof, but by reason of them, a ruling cannot be imposed upon another, i.e., they are not proof for imposition. As for Imam Shafi'i's analogy of them to the soft part of the nose and the ear, this analogy is with a difference because the purpose of the two is different. The purpose of the mentioned organs is benefit, and their benefit is not yet known because their health itself is not yet known. As for the soft part of the nose and the protruding part of the ear, their purpose is beauty, and beauty exists in the child because of them, and the cutter has destroyed that beauty, so diyah is obligatory upon him. The child's crying is not speech, method of knowing health of organs. And the error. Similarly, if the child cries at birth, (it is government adl) because it is not speech; rather, it is a mere sound. Knowledge of health in the tongue is through speech, in the penis through movement, and in the eye through that which indicates sight. Then after that, his ruling is the ruling of an adult in intentional and erroneous cases. Commentary: At the time of birth, if the child cried and from other means the health of his tongue could not be known, then only government adl is obligatory because this crying is not speech; rather, it is a mere sound. Rather, health of the tongue is known through speech, of the penis through movement, and of the eye through something from which sight can be inferred. And when the soundness of these organs becomes known, then his ruling is the ruling of an adult. Therefore, in the case of intentional cutting, qisas is obligatory; in error, diyah.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding compensation for injury to a child's eye, penis, or tongue when the health of the organ is unknown. The Hanafi ruling is that only 'government adl' (hukumat adl) is due, not full diyah. The basis is that the primary purpose of these organs is benefit (manfah), and when their health is uncertain, we cannot assume full function, so imposing full compensation would be unjust. The Shafi'i argument relies on the predominance of health (ghalabat al-sihha) and analogizes to the soft part of the nose and the protruding ear, where full diyah is due because beauty is the purpose, and it is completely lost. The Hanafi response distinguishes that in the case of the nose and ear, the purpose is aesthetic and known to be present, while in the child's organs, the benefit is unknown. The passage further clarifies that crying at birth is not speech, so it does not indicate the health of the tongue. Health is determined by actual proof: speech for tongue, movement for penis, and clear signs of sight for the eye. Once health is established, the ruling is the same as for an adult: intentional cutting leads to qisas; erroneous cutting leads to diyah.

Key Terms
حكومة عدل (hukumat adl): Compensation determined by expert assessment of the value of the lost function, not a fixed amount.
دية كاملة (diyat kamilah): Full blood money, equivalent to 100 camels or monetary value for a limb with a fixed diyah.
مارن (marin): The soft, fleshy part of the nose (the tip and surrounding area).
الاذن الشاخصة (al-udhun al-shakhisah): The protruding part of the ear (the pinna).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for cutting a child's tongue when the health of the tongue is unknown?
A) Full diyah is wajib.
B) Government adl is wajib.
C) No compensation is due.
D) Qisas is wajib.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires proof of an organ's health before imposing full diyah; otherwise, only government adl is due.

Diyat — Blood Money

Inclusion of Lesser Arsh in Greater Diyah for Head Wound
Ruling on tadakhul in diyat for head wound leading to loss of reason and scalp wound

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tadakhul (inclusion) of arsh al-mudihah in diyah, identify the qiyas argument used, and explain why Imam Zufar opposes inclusion.

Core Idea
When a single blow causes both a scalp wound and loss of reason, the compensation for the wound is included in the diyah for the loss.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses a critical question in diyat law: if one act produces two harms, must the perpetrator pay separate compensations? The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, applies the principle of tadakhul (interference): the lesser arsh for the scalp wound is subsumed within the greater diyah for loss of reason or all hair. Imam Zufar dissents, arguing for separate payments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario and the legal question
The scenario: a single blow to the head causes two distinct harms—a scalp wound (mudihah) and loss of reason (or all hair). The question: is the arsh for the wound included in the diyah for the loss, or must both be paid separately?
2
State the majority Hanafi position and its proof
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold inclusion. Their proof: a qiyas (analogy) on the case of cutting a finger that paralyzes the hand—the compensation for the finger enters into that for the hand. The common illa (effective cause) is a single act causing two harms to the same site.
The illa is jaliyy (apparent): one act, one locus.
3
Analyze Imam Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that each harm is a separate injury 'within less than life' (fi ma dun al-nafs), so they should not interfere, just as separate injuries to different parts of the body do not interfere.
Zufar's objection challenges the applicability of the illa.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response and the practical consequence (thamarah)
The Hanafi response distinguishes Zufar's analogy: separate injuries involve separate acts or sites, but here one act on one site produces both harms. The thamarah is financial: under the majority, only diyah is paid; under Zufar, arsh and diyah separately.
5
Note the additional intra-Hanafi detail about qisas
The commentary adds that if the act was intentional, Imam Abu Hanifah drops qisas due to uncertainty, while the Sahibayn permit qisas if possible. This does not affect the diyat ruling of inclusion.
This nuance is peripheral but shows the range of opinion within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن شج رجلا فذهب عقله او شعر راسه دخل ارش الموضحة فى الدية لان بفوات العقل تبطل منفعة جميع الاعضاء فصار كما اذا اوضحه فمات وارش الموضحة يجب بفوات جزء من الشعر حتى لو بنت يسقط والدية بفوات كل الشعر وقد تعلقا بسبب واحد فدخل الجزء فى الجملة كما اذا قطع اصبع رجل فشلت يده وقال زفر لا يدخل لان كل واحد جناية فيما دون النفس فلا يتداخلان كسائر الجنايات وجوابه ما ذكرنا

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی کا سر پھوڑ دیا پس اس کی عقل ختم ہوگئی یا اس کے سر کے بال تو موضحہ کا ارش دیت میں داخل ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ عقل کے فوات کی وجہ سے تمام اعضاء کی منفعت باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اس کو زخم موضحہ لگایا پس وہ مر گیا اور موضحہ کا ارش بالوں کا کچھ جزو فوت ہونے سے واجب ہوتا ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر بال جم گئے تو ارش ساقط ہو جائے گا اور دیت پورے بالوں کے فوات سے واجب ہوتی ہے اور یہ دونوں (ارش اور دیت) متعلق ہیں ایک سبب کے ساتھ تو جز کل میں داخل ہو جائے گا جیسے کسی شخص کی ایک انگلی کاٹی پس اس کا ہاتھ شل ہو گیا اور زفر نے فرمایا کہ (موضحہ کا ارش دیت میں) داخل نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک مادون النفس میں جنایت ہے پس ان دونوں میں تداخل نہ ہو گا جیسے تمام جنایت اور اس کا جواب وہی ہے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔

تشریح یہاں مصنف حقیقت میں یہ بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ زید نے ایک جنایت کی جس کا وقوع ایک عضو پر ہوا لیکن اس نے دو چیزوں کو ضائع کر دیا اور ان میں سے ایک کا ارش کم ہے اور دوسرے کا زیادہ ہے تو یہاں اقل اکثر میں داخل ہو جائے گا خواہ جنایت عمدہ ہو یا خطأ اور اگر جنایت کا وقوع الگ الگ دو حصوں پر ہو تو تداخل نہ ہوگا بلکہ ہر ایک کا ارش الگ الگ واجب ہوگا خواہ عمدہ ہو جنایت یا خطا ہو یہ تفصیل امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک ایسی صورت میں قصاص ساقط ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اگر اول عمدہ ہو اور قصاص وصول کرنا ممکن ہو تو قصاص ہوگا ورنہ پھر ان کا وہی مسلک ہے جو امام صاحب کا مسلک ہے۔

اور امام زفر کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ یہاں تداخل نہ ہوگا بلکہ ہر جنایت کا ارش الگ الگ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ ہر جنایت کا تعلق مادون النفس
He (al-Quduri) said: And whoever strikes a person's head so that his reason goes or the hair of his head (falls), the arsh of the scalp wound enters into the diyah because with the loss of reason the benefit of all organs is nullified, so it becomes as if he gave him a scalp wound and he died. And the arsh of the scalp wound is obligatory for the loss of a part of the hair, to the extent that if the hair grows back, the arsh falls. And the diyah is obligatory for the loss of all the hair. And they both relate to one cause, so the part enters into the whole, as when a man's finger is cut and his hand becomes paralyzed. And Zufar said: It does not enter, because each one is an injury within less than life, so they do not interfere with each other like other injuries. And its answer is what we have mentioned. Commentary: Here the author intends to explain that Zayd committed one injury that occurred on one limb but destroyed two things, and the arsh of one is less and the other is more. In this case, the lesser enters into the greater, whether the injury is intentional or erroneous. And if the injury occurs on two separate parts, then interference does not occur; rather, the arsh of each is obligatory separately, whether intentional or erroneous. This detail is according to Imam Abu Hanifah, because according to him, in such a case qisas is dropped. According to the Sahibayn, if the first is intentional and it is possible to exact qisas, then qisas (is applicable); otherwise, their madhhab is the same as Imam Abu Hanifah's. And Imam Zufar's madhhab is that interference does not occur; rather, the arsh of each injury is obligatory separately because each injury relates to less than life.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage discusses a case where a single act (a head wound) causes two consequences: loss of reason (or loss of all hair) and a scalp wound. The ruling is that the arsh (compensation) for the scalp wound (mudihah) is included within the greater diyah for the loss of reason or full hair, because both harms stem from the same cause. The analogy is like cutting a finger that causes the whole hand to become paralyzed: the compensation for the finger is included in that for the hand. Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that each injury is independent and should not interfere, just as separate injuries to different parts of the body do not interfere. The Hanafi response is that here the two effects arise from one act on one site, so the lesser is subsumed. The commentary adds that Imam Abu Hanifah holds that in such a case qisas is not applicable due to uncertainty, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say if the act was intentional and qisas is possible, then qisas applies; otherwise, they agree with Abu Hanifah. This intra-Hanafi dispute revolves around the principle of tadakhul (interference) in diyat.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadakhul): The legal principle that when multiple compensations arise from one act, the lesser is included in the greater (interference).
ارش الموضحة (arsh al-mudihah): Compensation for a scalp wound that bares the bone (mudihah); it is one-twentieth of the full diyah.
دية (diyah): Full blood money (100 camels) payable for loss of life or complete loss of a major function like reason or all hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man strikes another causing both a scalp wound (mudihah) and loss of reason from the same blow, what is the compensation?
A) Arsh al-mudihah only
B) Diyah only (including arsh al-mudihah)
C) Both arsh al-mudihah and diyah separately
D) No compensation

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when a single act on a single site produces two compensable harms, the lesser compensation is included in the greater (tadakhul), and only the greater is due.

Compensation for Newborn Injury: Cry vs. Speech
Ruling on compensation for a crying newborn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a newborn's cry does not prove speech ability and apply the correct initial compensation (hukumat al-adl) versus the later adult ruling (qisas/diyah).

Core Idea
A newborn's cry is not speech; only hukumat al-adl applies until faculties are proven.

This lesson examines a specific Hanafi ruling from al-Hidayah regarding injuries to a newborn who only cries. The text clarifies that crying is merely a sound, not speech, and therefore the default compensation is a fair assessment (hukumat al-adl) until the child's ability to speak, move, and see is established. Once proven, the newborn is treated as an adult for compensation purposes: qisas for intentional injury and diyah for unintentional. Understanding this distinction prevents premature application of severe penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial compensation
Read the passage and note that when a newborn only cries and no other evidence of speech exists, the obligatory compensation is hukumat al-adl (fair assessment by a judge).
This is the default because crying is not considered valid speech.
2
Recognize that crying is not speech
The text explicitly states that crying is merely a sound, not speech. Speech requires articulated words, not just vocalization.
This is the core legal principle.
3
List the ways to prove faculties
The health of the tongue is proven through speech; movement through motion; vision through the ability to see. These are the indicators that the child is like an adult.
These faculties must be established through external evidence.
4
State the consequences once proven
When speech, movement, and vision are confirmed, the newborn's legal ruling becomes that of an adult: for intentional cutting, qisas (retaliation) applies; for unintentional, diyah (blood money) applies.
The ruling transitions from default hukumat al-adl to the full adult compensation scheme.
5
Differentiate between intentional and unintentional
Note the distinction: intentional injury leads to qisas (if possible), while unintentional injury leads to diyah. This mirrors the standard Hanafi classification for injuries to adults.
This distinction only applies after faculties are proven.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالغ کا حکم ہو گا عمد اور خطاء دونوں صورتوں میں )۔ تشریح پیدائش کے وقت اگر بچہ رویا اور اس کے علاوہ دیگر ذرائع سے اس کی زبان کی صحت معلوم نہ ہوسکی تو صرف حکومت عدل واجب ہے کیونکہ یہ رونا کچھ کلام نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ تو محض ایک آواز ہے بلکہ زبان کی صحت کلام سے اور ذکر کی حرکت جنبش سے اور آنکھ کی ایسی چیز سے جس سے دیکھنے پر استدلال ہو سکے معلوم ہوگی ۔ اور جب اس کے اعضاء مذکورہ کی سلامتی معلوم ہوگئی پھر اس کا حکم بالغ کا حکم ہو گا لہذا عمدا کاٹنے کی صورت میں قصاص اور خطاء میں دیت واجب ہوگی۔
The ruling of an adult will apply in both intentional and unintentional cases. Explanation: At the time of birth if the child cried and the health of his tongue could not be known through other means, then only hukumat al-adl is obligatory because this crying is not speech; rather it is just a sound. Rather the health of the tongue will be known through speech, the movement of the organ through motion, and the eye through something by which vision can be inferred. And when the health of the mentioned organs is known, then his ruling will be the ruling of an adult. Hence in the case of cutting intentionally, qisas is obligatory, and in unintentional, diyah.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the classical Hanafi text al-Hidayah, as commented upon in Ashraf al-Hidayah. It addresses the legal capacity and compensation for injuries to a newborn who cannot speak but cries. The key point is that crying alone does not prove the child can speak; it is merely a sound. Therefore, when determining compensation for an inflicted injury, only hukumat al-adl (fair assessment by a judge) is initially mandatory. Once the child's ability to speak, move, and see is established through other means, the child is treated like an adult: intentional injury warrants qisas (retaliation in kind) and unintentional injury warrants diyah (blood money). The ruling is clear and axiomatic, intended for memorization.

Key Terms
حکومت عدل (hukumat al-adl): Fair compensation assessed by a judge when the exact amount of diyah is not prescribed
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment equivalent to the injury, applicable in intentional cases
دیت (diyah): Monetary compensation paid for homicide or bodily injury, also known as blood money

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a newborn is injured and only cries, what compensation is due initially according to this passage?
A) Full diyah
B) Qisas
C) Hukumat al-adl
D) No compensation

Key Takeaway
A newborn's cry is not speech; therefore only hukumat al-adl is initially wajib, and only after proving faculties does the ruling become like an adult, triggering qisas or diyah.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Inclusion of Lesser Compensation in Greater: Single Blow Causing Dual Harm
Intra-Hanafi dispute on inclusion of lesser compensation in greater from a single injury

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether arsh al-mudihah merges into diyah when a single blow causes loss of sanity or hair, explain the qiyas used, and identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, and Zufar.

Core Idea
When a single blow causes multiple harms on one locus, the greater diyah absorbs the lesser arsh—unless the act is intentional and qisas applies.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: if a head wound causes both loss of sanity and hair, does the compensation for the wound (arsh) merge into the full diyah? The majority holds inclusion based on qiyas to a finger cut causing hand paralysis. We will unpack the reasoning, the objections of Imam Zufar, and the practical ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two harms
Consider a single blow to the head that results in loss of sanity (all limb benefits nullified) and either partial or full hair loss. Determine what compensations are potentially due: arsh for the head wound (mudihah) and diyah for loss of sanity or full hair.
The passage distinguishes loss of sanity (destroys all limb benefit) from mere hair loss.
2
State the ruling from Quduri's matn
The matn declares: 'arsh al-mudihah enters into the diyah' when both arise from one cause on one locus. This means only full diyah is wajib; the arsh is not added separately.
The matn uses 'mudihah' loosely to mean a wound causing hair destruction, not the technical bone-exposing wound.
3
Understand the qiyas to the finger-hand case
The ruling is supported by analogy: if cutting a finger paralyses the entire hand, the arsh for the finger is included in the diyah for the hand. The illa (effective cause) is unity of cause (one blow) and locus (one limb). Apply the same illa to the head case.
The qiyas is jaliy (clear) because the illa is directly observed.
4
Contrast Zufar's objection
Imam Zufar argues that each jinaayah below the soul is independent, so compensations should not merge. He cites the general rule that separate jinaayaat on different limbs do not interpenetrate.
Zufar's view would require both arsh and diyah to be paid separately, increasing total compensation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its qualification
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn: inclusion applies when cause and locus are unified. However, the Sahibayn add that if the act is intentional and qisas is possible, qisas takes precedence over diyah, and then inclusion may not apply.
This qualification prevents double compensation while allowing retribution.

Source Text

ایک شخص کو ایسی چوٹ لگائی جس سے اس کی عقل ماری گئی یا اس کے بال گر گئے تو کتنی دیت واجب ہوگی

قال ومن شج رجلا فذهب عقله او شعر راسه دخل ارش الموضحة فى الدية لان بفوات العقل تبطل منفعة جميع الاعضاء فصار كما اذا اوضحه فمات وارش الموضحة يجب بفوات جزء من الشعر حتى لوبنت يسقط والدية بفوات كل الشعر وقد تعلقا بسبب واحد فدخل الجزء فى الجملة كما اذا قطع اصبع رجل فشلت يده وقال زفر لا يدخل لان كل واحد جناية فيما دون النفس فلا يتداخلان كسائر الجنايات وجوابه ما ذكرنا

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی کا سر پھوڑ دیا پس اس کی عقل ختم ہوگئی یا اس کے سر کے بال تو موضحہ کا ارش دیت میں داخل ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ عقل کے فوات کی وجہ سے تمام اعضاء کی منفعت باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اس کو زخم موضحہ لگایا پس وہ مر گیا اور موضحہ کا ارش بالوں کا کچھ جزو فوت ہونے سے واجب ہوتا ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر بال جم گئے تو ارش ساقط ہو جائے گا اور دیت پورے بالوں کے فوات سے واجب ہوتی ہے اور یہ دونوں (ارش اور دیت ) متعلق ہیں ایک سبب کے ساتھ تو جز کل میں داخل ہو جائے گا جیسے کسی شخص کی ایک انگلی کاٹی پس اس کا ہاتھ شل ہو گیا اور زفر نے فرمایا کہ (موضحہ کا ارش دیت میں ) داخل نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک مادون النفس میں جنایت ہے پس ان دونوں میں تداخل نہ ہو گا جیسے تمام جنایت اور اس کا جواب وہی ہے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔

تشریح یہاں مصنف محقیقت میں یہ بیان کرنا چاہتے ہیں کہ زید نے ایک جنایت کی جس کا وقوع ایک عضو پر ہوا لیکن اس نے دو چیزوں کو ضائع کر دیا اور ان میں سے ایک کا ارش کم ہے اور دوسرے کا زیادہ ہے تو یہاں اقل اکثر میں داخل ہو جائے گا خواہ جنایت عمدا ہو یا خطأ اور اگر جنایت کا وقوع الگ الگ دو حصوں پر ہو تو تداخل نہ ہوگا بلکہ ہر ایک کا ارش الگ الگ واجب ہوگا خواہ عمد ہو جنایت یا خطا ہو یہ تفصیل امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک ایسی صورت میں قصاص ساقط ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اگر اول عمد ہو اور قصاص وصول کرنا ممکن ہو تو قصاص ہوگا ورنہ پھر ان کا وہی مسلک ہے جو امام صاحب کا مسلک ہے۔

اور امام زفر کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ یہاں تداخل نہ ہوگا بلکہ ہر جنایت کا ارش الگ الگ واجب ہوگا کیونکہ ہر جنایت کا تعلق مادون النفس سے ہے جہاں تداخل نہیں ہوا کرتا۔

لیکن ہماری طرف سے ان کو یہ جواب دیا گیا کہ جب سب متحد ہے اور محل متحد ہے تو اکثر اقل کو شامل ہو جائے گا یہ اس پوری تفصیل کا حاصل ہے جو مصنف نے بیان فرمائی ہے۔ اور ماقبل میں گزر چکا ہے کہ پورے سر کے بال مونڈنے میں جب کہ پھر وہ دوبارہ نہ آ گئیں پوری دیت ہے،

اور داڑھی میں پوری دیت ہے اور اگر اگ جائے تو کچھ واجب نہیں مگر تعزیر، اور اگر سر کے کچھ بال ختم کئے تو اس میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے لہذا اس نے اگر سر کو زخمی کیا جس سے زخم موضحہ ہو گیا اور بال بھی ختم ہو گئے (یعنی کچھ بال ) تو اب دیکھا جائے تو موضحہ کا ارش زیادہ ہے یا بالوں کی حکومت عدل زیادہ ہے جو نسا زیادہ ہو اسی کو واجب کیا جائے گا، اور قلیل کو کثیر میں داخل کر دیا جائے گا لہذا اگر حکومت عدل زیادہ ہو تو وہی واجب ہے اور ارش موضحہ کو حکومت عدل میں داخل مانا جائے گا تو یہ ایک جگہ ہے جہاں موضحہ کے ارش کو داخل فی الکثیر کیا گیا ہے۔ اور دوسری جگہ یہ ہے کہ زخم موضحہ کیا گیا لیکن مجروح اس کی وجہ سے مر گیا تو یہاں دیت کاملہ واجب ہوگی اور ارش موضحہ کو اس میں داخل کر دیا جائے گا مصنف کی عبارت میں کچھ انتشار سا ہے اس کی تفصیل سے سارا مسئلہ منقطع ہو جائے گا۔ لہذا مصنف نے فرمایا کہ سر پھوڑنے سے اگر عقل زائل ہوگئی تو پوری دیت واجب ہے اور جب پوری دیت واجب ہوگئی تو موضحہ کا ارش کچھ نہ ہو گا۔

اسی طرح اگر زخمی کیا جس کی وجہ سے پورے بال ختم ہو گئے تو پوری دیت واجب ہو گی اب موضحہ کا کچھ ارش واجب نہ ہوگا۔ وارش الموضحه.... الخ - یہاں موضحہ سے مراد اصطلاحی موضحہ نہیں ہو سکتا ورنہ اس کے ارش کا مدار بالوں پر نہیں ہے (کمامر ) اور اسی طرح بال اُگنے سے یا زخم بھر جانے سے اس کا ارش ختم نہیں ہوتا ہے ( کما مر ) بلکہ یہاں ضروری ہے کہ موضحہ سے مراد ان بالوں کا ختم ہونا لیا جائے جو کچھ ختم ہوں اور نہ اُگے جس میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے اور اگر اگ جائیں تو کچھ بھی واجب نہیں ہوتا ، اور دیت سے مراد پورے بالوں کی دیت ہے اب مسئلہ صاف ہے کہ زخم کی وجہ سے ہاتھوں ہاتھ کچھ بال ختم ہو گئے پھر اس کے اثر سے سارے بال ختم ہو گئے تو اب اس پر پوری دیت واجب ہے اور پہلے بال ختم ہونے کی وجہ سے جو حکومت عدل واجب تھی وہ چونکہ قلیل ہے لہذاوہ کثیر میں داخل ہو جائے گی۔

اور یہ بھی ممکن ہے کہ موضحہ سے وہ زخم مراد لیا جائے جو مادون الموضحہ ہیں جن میں کچھ خراش وغیرہ ہوگئی ہو اور کچھ بال وغیرہ اڑ گئے ہوں اور پھر اس کے اثر سے سارے بال اُڑ گئے ہوں۔ تو چونکہ اول میں حکومت عدل واجب تھی اور ثانی میں دیت تو جب دیت واجب کر دی گئی تو حکومت عدل اسی میں داخل ہو جائے گی اس تاویل کے بغیر مسئلہ حل نہیں ہوتا اور صاحب نتائج نے اگر چہ یہاں طویل گفتگو کی ہے مگر سب لا حاصل ہے۔
A person inflicted such a blow on someone that his sanity was lost or his scalp hair fell; how much diyah is wajib? He said: And whoever wounds the head of a man, and his sanity or hair of the head is lost, the arsh of the mudihah enters into the diyah, because by loss of sanity the benefit of all limbs is nullified; so it is as if he gave him a mudihah wound and he died. And arsh al-mudihah is wajib by loss of a part of the hair, so if it grows back it is cancelled, and diyah is wajib by loss of all the hair. And both are related to a single cause, so the part enters into the whole, like a man's finger is cut and his hand becomes paralyzed. And Zufar said: It does not enter, because each is a jinaayah below the soul, so they do not interpenetrate, like other jinaayaat. And its answer is what we mentioned. Translation: Quduri said: And whoever breaks someone's head, and his sanity ends or the hair of his head (falls), then the arsh of the mudihah enters into the diyah, because by loss of sanity the benefit of all limbs becomes void. So it is as if he gave him a mudihah wound and he died. And arsh of mudihah is wajib by loss of a part of the hair, such that if the hair grows back the arsh is dropped, and diyah is wajib by loss of all the hair. And these two (arsh and diyah) are attached to a single cause, so the part enters into the whole, like a man's finger is cut and his hand becomes paralyzed. And Zufar said: It does not enter, because each of them is a jinaayah below the soul, so they do not interpenetrate, like all jinaayaat. And its answer is what we have mentioned. Explanation: Here the author intends to state that Zaid committed one injury that occurred on one limb, but it destroyed two things, and the arsh of one is less and of the other is more. So here the lesser enters into the greater, whether the injury is intentional or unintentional. And if the injury occurs on two separate parts, then interpenetration does not occur; rather each one's arsh is wajib separately, whether the injury is intentional or unintentional. This detail is according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because according to him in such a case qisas is dropped. And according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if it is initially intentional and qisas is possible, then qisas; otherwise their position is the same as Imam's. And Imam Zufar's position is that here interpenetration does not occur; rather each jinaayah's arsh is wajib separately, because each jinaayah relates to that below the soul, where interpenetration does not occur. But from our side it was answered that when both the cause and the locus are unified, the greater includes the lesser. This is the summary of the full detail that the author has explained. And it has passed before that in shaving all the hair of the head, when they do not grow back, full diyah is wajib; and in the beard full diyah, and if it grows back, nothing is wajib except ta'zeer (discretionary punishment). And if some hair of the head is destroyed, then in that hukumat al-adl is wajib. Hence if he injured the head such that a mudihah wound occurred and hair also fell (some hair), then it is seen whether the arsh of mudihah is greater or the hukumat al-adl of the hair is greater; whichever is greater is made wajib, and the lesser is included in the greater. So if hukumat al-adl is greater, it is wajib and arsh al-mudihah is considered included in hukumat al-adl. This is one place where arsh al-mudihah is included in the greater. And the other place is that a mudihah wound was given but the wounded person died from it; here full diyah is wajib and arsh al-mudihah is included in it. There is some disorder in the author's expression; detailing it would break the issue. So the author said: If from breaking the head sanity was lost, full diyah is wajib, and when full diyah is wajib, arsh of mudihah is nothing. Similarly, if he injured him and all hair was lost, full diyah is wajib, and now no arsh of mudihah is wajib. 'Wa arsh al-mudihah...' Here 'mudihah' cannot be the technical mudihah, otherwise its arsh does not depend on hair (as before), and also from hair growing back or wound healing its arsh is not dropped (as before). Rather here it is necessary that by 'mudihah' is meant the destruction of some hair that do not grow back, in which hukumat al-adl is wajib, and if they grow back then nothing is wajib. And by 'diyah' is meant the diyah of all hair. Now the matter is clear: due to the wound some hair were destroyed immediately, then from its effect all hair were destroyed, so full diyah is wajib, and the hukumat al-adl that was wajib earlier due to initial hair loss is lesser, so it enters into the greater. And it is also possible that by 'mudihah' is meant the wound that is less than a mudihah, in which some scratches etc. occurred and some hair etc. fell, and then from its effect all hair fell. So since in the first hukumat al-adl was wajib and in the second diyah, when diyah is made wajib, hukumat al-adl enters into it. Without this interpretation the issue is not resolved, and the author of Nata'ij has made lengthy discussion but it is all fruitless.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and expansion of a ruling from al-Hidayah. The core issue: when a single blow (one jinaayah on one limb) causes two distinct harms—loss of sanity (which nullifies all limb functions) and loss of hair—does the compensation for the lesser harm (arsh) merge into the greater (diyah) or must each be paid separately? The text quotes the matn of Quduri stating that arsh al-mudihah (wound exposing bone) enters into the full diyah because the loss of sanity destroys the benefit of all limbs, analogous to a fatal wound where arsh merges into diyah. The argument is that since both harms arise from one cause on one locus, the part (arsh for partial hair loss) is absorbed into the whole (diyah for total hair loss or sanity loss). This is compared to cutting a finger causing the entire hand to be paralyzed: the arsh for the finger enters into the diyah for the hand. Imam Zufar opposes, arguing each jinaayah below the soul is independent and no interpenetration occurs, like separate jinaayaat. The commentary then explains that Imam Abu Hanifa holds the inclusion view (lesser enters greater) regardless of intent, but if the injury is intentional and qisas is possible, qisas is the primary claim and diyah is subsidiary. The Sahibayn differentiate: if the initial act is intentional and qisas can be executed, qisas takes precedence; otherwise they agree with Abu Hanifa. Zufar insists on separate compensation. The Hanafi response solidifies the inclusion principle: unification of cause and locus necessitates the greater including the lesser. Practical applications: full head hair loss (if non-regrowing) warrants full diyah, beard similarly; partial non-regrowing hair loss triggers hukumat al-adl (fair assessment). The passage ends with a methodological note about interpreting 'mudihah' in the matn to avoid contradiction: here it refers to partial hair loss requiring hukumat al-adl, not the technical mudihah wound, because the arsh of a technical mudihah does not depend on regrowth. The discussion concludes that the inclusion principle holds, dismissing lengthy debates as fruitless.

Key Terms
ارش (arsh): Fixed compensation for a specific bodily injury, e.g., arsh al-mudihah (wound exposing bone)
دیت (diyah): Full blood money for loss of a faculty (e.g., sanity) or complete loss of hair
موضحہ (mudihah): A head wound that exposes the bone; in this passage it is reinterpreted as destruction of hair that does not grow back
حکومت عدل (hukumat al-adl): Fair compensation assessed by a judge when no specific arsh is prescribed
تداخل (tadaakhul): Interpenetration or merging of compensations when multiple harms arise from a single cause on one locus

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn), if a single head wound causes loss of both sanity and some hair, how is compensation calculated?
A) Full diyah for sanity plus arsh for hair are both paid separately.
B) Only full diyah for sanity is paid, and arsh for hair is included in it.
C) Only hukumat al-adl for hair is paid, and no diyah for sanity.
D) Qisas is applied for both harms.

Key Takeaway
When cause and locus are unified, the greater diyah absorbs the lesser arsh; this is the relied-upon Hanafi position despite Zufar's objection.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Tadakhul of Arsh al-Mudihah in Full Diyah for Hair Loss
Explaining when compensation for head wound merges into full blood money for hair loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tadakhul to determine the wajib compensation when a head wound causes both a mudihah and hair loss.

Core Idea
When cause and locus unite, the greater compensation includes the lesser — avoiding double payment for a single injury.

In diyat, when a single act causes multiple compensable injuries, the Hanafi school uses the principle of tadakhul to prevent double counting. This lesson examines a specific case: a head wound that causes both a mudihah (exposing bone) and hair loss. By understanding the unity of cause and locus, you will learn how to determine the correct wajib compensation — whether total or partial hair loss is involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a head wound (jirah) that results in two harms: a mudihah wound and hair loss. The ruling involves determining wajib compensation (diyah or hukuma adl).
The mudihah has a fixed arsh (1/20 of diyah). Hair loss is compensated by full diyah if permanent and total, or hukuma adl if partial.
2
Locate the principle
The key principle is tadakhul: when two compensable injuries arise from a single act and affect the same bodily locus, the greater compensation includes the lesser.
This is based on istihsan; the dalil is the maxim 'when the cause and locus are united, the greater includes the lesser.'
3
Distinguish total vs partial hair loss
If hair loss is total and permanent, full diyah is wajib. If partial, a discretionary hukuma adl is assessed. The presence of a mudihah adds another fixed arsh.
The mudihah's arsh does not depend on hair regrowth; it is fixed once bone is exposed.
4
Apply the rule: greater includes lesser
For total hair loss: full diyah is greater than arsh mudihah, so only full diyah is wajib. For partial: compare hukuma adl and arsh mudihah; the larger is wajib, the smaller is included. If the wound also causes death, full diyah subsumes the arsh.
This prevents double compensation and is called tadakhul.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Other schools may treat each injury separately, leading to separate payments. The Hanafi view simplifies liability and is considered more just.
The commentary criticizes Sahib al-Nata'ij for an unproductive lengthy discussion on this point.

سے ہے جہاں تداخل نہیں ہوا کرتا۔ لیکن ہماری طرف سے ان کو یہ جواب دیا گیا کہ جب سب متحد ہے اور محل متحد ہے تو اکثر اقل کو شامل ہو جائے گا یہ اس پوری تفصیل کا حاصل ہے جو مصنف نے بیان فرمائی ہے۔ اور ماقبل میں گزر چکا ہے کہ پورے سر کے بال مونڈنے میں جب کہ پھر وہ دوبارہ نہ آ گئیں پوری دیت ہے، اور داڑھی میں پوری دیت ہے اور اگر اگ جائے تو کچھ واجب نہیں مگر تعزیر، اور اگر سر کے کچھ بال ختم کئے تو اس میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے لہذا اس نے اگر سر کو زخمی کیا جس سے زخم موضحہ ہو گیا اور بال بھی ختم ہو گئے (یعنی کچھ بال ) تو اب دیکھا جائے تو موضحہ کا ارش زیادہ ہے یا بالوں کی حکومت عدل زیادہ ہے جو نسا زیادہ ہو اسی کو واجب کیا جائے گا، اور قلیل کو کثیر میں داخل کر دیا جائے گا لہذا اگر حکومت عدل زیادہ ہو تو وہی واجب ہے اور ارش موضحہ کو حکومت عدل میں داخل مانا جائے گا تو یہ ایک جگہ ہے جہاں موضحہ کے ارش کو داخل فی الکثیر کیا گیا ہے۔ اور دوسری جگہ یہ ہے کہ زخم موضحہ کیا گیا لیکن مجروح اس کی وجہ سے مر گیا تو یہاں دیت کاملہ واجب ہوگی اور ارش موضحہ کو اس میں داخل کر دیا جائے گا مصنف کی عبارت میں کچھ انتشار سا ہے اس کی تفصیل سے سارا مسئلہ منقطع ہو جائے گا۔ لہذا مصنف نے فرمایا کہ سر پھوڑنے سے اگر عقل زائل ہوگئی تو پوری دیت واجب ہے اور جب پوری دیت واجب ہوگئی تو موضحہ کا ارش کچھ نہ ہو گا۔ اسی طرح اگر زخمی کیا جس کی وجہ سے پورے بال ختم ہو گئے تو پوری دیت واجب ہو گی اب موضحہ کا کچھ ارش واجب نہ ہوگا۔ وارش الموضحه.... الخ - یہاں موضحہ سے مراد اصطلاحی ، موضحہ نہیں ہو سکتا ورنہ اس کے ارش کا مدار بالوں پر نہیں ہے (کمامر ) اور اسی طرح بال اُگنے سے یا زخم بھر جانے سے اس کا ارش ختم نہیں ہوتا ہے ( کما مر ) بلکہ یہاں ضروری ہے کہ موضحہ سے مراد ان بالوں کا ختم ہونا لیا جائے جو کچھ ختم ہوں اور نہ اُگے جس میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے اور اگر اگ جائیں تو کچھ بھی واجب نہیں ہوتا ، اور دیت سے مراد پورے بالوں کی دیت ہے اب مسئلہ صاف ہے کہ زخم کی وجہ سے ہاتھوں ہاتھ کچھ بال ختم ہو گئے پھر اس کے اثر سے سارے بال ختم ہو گئے تو اب اس پر پوری دیت واجب ہے اور پہلے بال ختم ہونے کی وجہ سے جو حکومت عدل واجب تھی وہ چونکہ قلیل ہے لہذاوہ کثیر میں داخل ہو جائے گی۔ اور یہ بھی ممکن ہے کہ موضحہ سے وہ زخم مراد لیا جائے جو مادون الموضحہ ہیں جن میں کچھ خراش وغیرہ ہوگئی ہو اور کچھ بال وغیرہ اڑ گئے ہوں اور پھر اس کے اثر سے سارے بال اُڑ گئے ہوں۔ تو چونکہ اول میں حکومت عدل واجب تھی اور ثانی میں دیت تو جب دیت واجب کر دی گئی تو حکومت عدل اسی میں داخل ہو جائے گی اس تاویل کے بغیر مسئلہ حل نہیں ہوتا اور صاحب نتائج نے اگر چہ یہاں طویل گفتگو کی سے مگر سب لا حاصل ہے۔
From the Book of Blood Money. It is where tadakhul (inclusion) does not occur. But from our side, this answer was given to them: when both are united and the locus is united, then the greater includes the lesser. This is the summary of the complete detail that the author has explained. And it has passed previously that in shaving all the hair of the head, when they do not grow back, full diyah is due; and for the beard, full diyah; and if they grow back, nothing is wajib except ta'zir. And if some hair of the head are removed, then hukuma adl is wajib. So if he wounded the head such that a mudihah wound occurred and hair also were lost, then it is seen: is the arsh of the mudihah greater or the hukuma adl for the hair greater? Whichever is greater, it is made wajib, and the lesser is included in the greater. So if hukuma adl is greater, it is wajib, and arsh al-mudihah is considered included in the hukuma adl. So this is one place where arsh al-mudihah is included in the greater. And the second place is: a mudihah wound was inflicted but the injured died due to it, so here full diyah (diyat kamilah) is wajib and arsh al-mudihah will be included in it. There is some disorder in the author's wording; its detail would break the issue. So the author said: if from cracking the head, intellect is lost, then full diyah is wajib; and when full diyah becomes wajib, arsh of mudihah is nothing. Similarly, if he wounded such that all hair were lost, then full diyah is wajib; now no arsh of mudihah is wajib. 'Wa arsh al-mudihah... etc.' Here 'mudihah' cannot mean the terminological mudihah; otherwise its arsh does not depend on hair (as before). And similarly, from hair growing back or wound healing, its arsh is not removed (as before). Rather, here it is necessary that by 'mudihah' is meant the removal of those hair that are partially removed and do not grow back, for which hukuma adl is wajib; and if they grow back, nothing is wajib. And 'diyah' means the diyah for all hair. Now the issue is clear: due to the wound, some hair were lost immediately, then from its effect all hair were lost. Now full diyah is wajib on him, and the hukuma adl that was wajib for the initial hair loss, because it is lesser, it will be included in the greater. And it is also possible that by 'mudihah' is meant those wounds that are below mudihah (madoon al-mudihah) in which some scratch etc. occurred and some hair etc. fell out, and then from its effect all hair fell out. Since in the first case hukuma adl was wajib and in the second case diyah, when diyah is made wajib, the hukuma adl will be included in it. Without this interpretation the issue is not resolved, and Sahib al-Nata'ij, although he has a lengthy discussion here, all is fruitless.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah discusses the principle of tadakhul (inclusion of one compensation into another) when a single act causes two compensable injuries. The author explains that when a head wound (shajjah) causes both a mudihah and hair loss, the applicable compensation depends on whether the hair loss is total or partial. If total and hair does not regrow, full diyah for hair is due and the arsh of the mudihah is included (tadahul). If partial, the greater of the hukuma adl for hair and arsh of mudihah is taken, with the lesser included. This ruling is based on the principle that when both the cause (jinaayah) and the locus (mahall) are unified, the greater subsumes the lesser. The author also addresses a possible interpretation that 'mudihah' here might not refer to the technical term but to any wound causing hair loss, clarifying that the arsh of a true mudihah does not depend on hair growth. The passage ends by criticizing Sahib al-Nata'ij for an unproductive lengthy discussion.

Key Terms
موضحہ (mūḍiḥah): A head wound that exposes the bone; in this passage, also interpreted as any wound causing hair loss.
حکومت عدل (ḥukūmat ʿadl): Discretionary compensation assessed by expert for injury to a part without fixed arsh.
تداخل (tadākhul): Merging of lesser compensation into greater when both stem from a single act on a single locus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a single head wound causes a mudihah (arsh 50 dinars) and partial hair loss (hukuma adl 80 dinars), what is the wajib compensation according to the Hanafi position in this passage?
A) 130 dinars (both separately)
B) 80 dinars (only the greater, the lesser is included)
C) 50 dinars (only the mudihah arsh)
D) 80 dinars plus ta'zir

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of tadakhul ensures that when a single act on a single locus gives rise to multiple compensations, the greater subsumes the lesser, preventing double liability.

Diyat — Blood Money

Dispute on Tadakhul of Arsh al-Mudihah with Diyah for Lost Senses
Intra-Hanafi dispute on merging arsh into diyah for lost senses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on tadakhul when a mudihah causes loss of hearing, sight, or speech, and compare the two narrations from Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When a mudihah causes loss of a specific sense, the arsh is separate from diyah—each sense is like a distinct limb, unlike the all-pervading intellect.

The question of whether compensation for a head wound merges with blood money for a lost sense arises when one act causes two injuries. The Hanafi school has an internal difference: Abu Hanifa holds that no merging occurs, while Abu Yusuf offers two narrations. Understanding their reasoning—centered on analogy to separate limbs versus the hidden intellect—is key to applying diyat rulings correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two compensations
Recognize that the same injury (mudihah) causes two harms: the wound itself and the loss of a sense (hearing, sight, or speech). The offender owes arsh for the wound and diyah for the sense.
The dispute is whether these two payments merge (tadakhul).
2
State the two intra-Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and one narration from Abu Yusuf: no tadakhul—pay both separately. Second narration from Abu Yusuf: tadakhul for hearing and speech, but not for sight.
3
Analyze the underlying qiyas for each position
The first position analogizes each sense to a separate limb because its benefit is localized to its organ; thus, like injuries to different limbs, no merging. The second position analogizes hearing and speech to intellect (hidden, general benefit) so tadakhul applies; sight is external so it remains separate.
The key distinguishing factor is whether the benefit is specific or general.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
If no tadakhul: offender pays full diyah (100 camels) + arsh (5 camels) = 105 camels. If tadakhul applies: only diyah (100 camels) is paid; arsh is merged.
The mufta bihi is the first position (no tadakhul).

موضحہ زخم کے ساتھ ساتھ قوت سماعت یا قوت بصارت یا گویائی ختم ہوگئی دیت کے ساتھ موضحہ کا ارش بھی واجب ہے اقوال فقہاء

ال وان ذهب سمعه او بصره او كلامه فعليه ارش الموضحة مع الدية قالوا هذا قول أبي حنيفة وابي يوسف حمهم الله وعن أبي يوسف ان الشجة تدخل فى دية السمع والكلام ولاتدخل فى دية البصر وجه الاول ان كلامنها جناية فيمادون النفس والمنفعة مختصة به فاشبه الاعضاء المختلفة بخلاف العقل لان منفعة عائدة ی جميع الاعضاء على مابينا وجه الثانى ان السمع والكلام مبطن فيعتبر بالعقل والبصر ظاهر فلا يلحق به

زجمعہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر (محجہ موضحہ کی وجہ سے ) اس کی قوت سماعت یا اس کی بصر یا اس کی گویائی ختم ہو گئی تو اس پر دیت کے ساتھ ساتھ موضحہ کا ارش ہے ، مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ یہ تیخین کا قول ہے اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ شجہ سماعت اور گویائی کی دیت میں تو اخل ہوگا اور بھر کی دیت میں داخل نہ ہوگا ، اول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک ایسی جنایت ہے جو مادون النفس میں ہے اور منفعت ن میں سے ہر ایک کے ساتھ مختص ہے تو یہ اعضاء مختلفہ کے مشابہ ہو گئے ۔ بخلاف عقل کہ اس لئے کہ اس کی منفعت تمام اعضاء کی جانب وتی ہے جیسا کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ ثانی قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ سمع اور کلام باطنی چیزیں ہیں تو ان کو عقل پر قیاس کیا جائے گا اور بصر ظاہری چیز ہے تو اس کو عقل کے ساتھ احق نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح زید نے خالد کا سر پھوڑ دیا جس کی وجہ سے فحجہ موضحہ ہو گیا اور ساتھ ہی ساتھ قوت سماعت یا بینائی یا گویا کی بھی جاتی رہی تو اب کیا حکم ہے تداخل ہوگا یا نہیں تو اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول عدم تداخل کا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف سے دور روایتیں ہیں ایک کے اندر تو وہ مام صاحب کے ساتھ ہیں اور دوسری میں ان کے یہاں تفصیل ہے یعنی مذکورہ تین قوتوں میں سے ایک میں یعنی بھر میں وہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں اور سمع اور کلام میں وہ تداخل کے قائل ہیں۔ اب دونوں روایتوں کی دلیل دیکھئے۔ عدم تداخل کی دلیل ... ان تینوں قوتوں میں سے ہر ایک میں جو جنایت ہے یہ جنایت فیمادون النفس ہے اور ان میں سے ہر ایک کی منفعت اسی کے ساتھ مختص ہے یعنی بولنا صرف زبان کا کام ہے اور سننا سماعت کا اور دیکھنا آنکھ کا لہذا یہ اعضاء مختلفہ کے مشابہ ہوئے اور اعضاء مختلفہ میں تداخل نہیں ہوا کرتا لہذا یہاں بھی تداخل نہ ہوگا ۔ بلکہ ان کے ختم ہونے کی دیت دینی ہوگی اور موضحہ کا ارش الگ دینا ہو گا۔ اور عقل کی صورت میں تداخل کا قول اس لئے اختیار کیا تھا کہ عقل کی منفعت پورے بدن کی جانب راجع ہے اور یہاں ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ ہر قوت اپنے مخصوص دائرے میں کام کرتی ہے۔ دوسری روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قوت سماعت اور گویائی باطنی او مخفی چیزیں ہیں جیسے عقل مخفی اور باطنی چیز ہے تو ان دونوں کو عقل پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے وہی حکم دیا گیا جو عقل کی صورت میں ہے، اور بھر ایک ظاہری قوت ہے تو اس کو عقل پر قیاس کیا گیا اور عدم مداخل
Along with the mudihah wound, if hearing, sight, or speech is lost, the arsh of the mudihah is also wajib along with the diyah. The sayings of the jurists: 'And if his hearing, sight, or speech goes, then he owes the arsh of the mudihah along with the diyah.' They said: This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the shajjah (head wound) is included in the diyah for hearing and speech, and is not included in the diyah for sight. The reason for the first: each one of them is a jinayah below the soul (below murder), and the benefit is specific to it, so it resembles separate limbs, unlike intellect because its benefit returns to all limbs as we have explained. The reason for the second: hearing and speech are hidden (batin), so they are analogized to intellect; and sight is apparent (zahir), so it is not attached to intellect. Imam al-Quduri said: 'And if (due to the mudihah) his hearing, his sight, or his speech is lost, then he owes the arsh of the mudihah along with the diyah.' The mashayikh said: This is the qawl of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And from Abu Yusuf it is narrated that the shajjah is included in the diyah for hearing and speech, and is not included in the diyah for sight. The reason for the first: each of them is a jinayah below the soul, and the benefit of each is specific to it, so they resemble separate limbs. Unlike intellect because its benefit goes to all limbs. The reason for the second saying: hearing and speech are internal things, so they will be analogized to intellect; and sight is an external thing, so it will not be attached to intellect. Explanation: Zaid cracked Khalid's head, causing a mudihah, and at the same time hearing, sight, or speech ceased. What is the ruling? Will tadakhul occur or not? In this, Imam Abu Hanifa's saying is no tadakhul. And from Imam Abu Yusuf there are two narrations: in one, he is with Imam Abu Hanifa; in the second, he has a detail—among the three faculties, in one, i.e., sight, he is with Imam Abu Hanifa, and regarding hearing and speech, he holds tadakhul. Now see the proof of both narrations. Proof of no tadakhul: each of these three faculties is a jinayah below the soul, and the benefit of each is specific to it—speech is only the work of the tongue, hearing is of the ear, seeing of the eye—so they resemble different limbs, and in different limbs, tadakhul does not occur. Therefore here too tadakhul will not occur; rather, the diyah for their loss must be paid and the arsh of mudihah must be given separately. And the saying of tadakhul in the case of intellect was adopted because the benefit of intellect returns to the entire body, and here it is not like that; rather, each faculty works in its own specific sphere. The proof of the second narration: hearing and speech are internal and hidden things, like intellect is hidden and internal; so by analogizing these two to intellect, the same ruling is given as in the case of intellect. And sight is an external faculty, so it is not analogized to intellect; therefore no tadakhul.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the application of tadakhul when a head wound (mudihah) causes loss of hearing, sight, or speech. The primary position (Abu Hanifa and one narration from Abu Yusuf) is that there is no tadakhul: the offender must pay both the full diyah for the lost sense and the arsh for the mudihah separately. This is because each sense (hearing, sight, speech) is a specific benefit (manfa'ah) localized to its organ, making it analogous to separate limbs (a'da' mukhtalifah), where tadakhul is not applied. Intellect is different because its benefit pervades the whole body. Abu Yusuf's second narration distinguishes between internal and external senses: hearing and speech are hidden (batin) like intellect, so they analogize to intellect and tadakhul applies (the arsh is included in the diyah); but sight is apparent (zahir) so it does not analogize and tadakhul does not apply. The commentary provides the reasoning for both positions, emphasizing that the analogy to different limbs (a'da' mukhtalifah) is the basis for the majority view.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Fixed blood money for loss of life, limb, or faculty; here, full diyah for loss of hearing, sight, or speech.
ارش (arsh): Fixed compensation for specific injuries; here, arsh al-mudihah (1/20 of full diyah).
شجہ (shajjah): A head wound; here used generally for the mudihah wound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second narration of Abu Yusuf, which lost sense(s) allow tadakhul (inclusion of arsh into diyah) when combined with a mudihah?
A) Hearing and sight
B) Speech and sight
C) Hearing and speech
D) Sight only

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi diyat, tadakhul does not apply to lost senses (hearing, sight, speech) when combined with a mudihah, because each sense has a specific localized benefit, making it analogous to separate limbs.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Does Arsh of Muwaddiha Merge with Diya for Sensory Loss?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on merging arsh of muwaddiha with diya for sensory loss

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether the arsh of a muwaddiha wound merges with diya for loss of hearing, speech, or sight, and explain the reasoning (qiyas) behind each position.

Core Idea
The arsh of a head wound merges or remains separate depending on whether the lost faculty is hidden or apparent.

This passage examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement over compensating multiple injuries from a single blow. When a muwaddiha wound causes loss of a sensory faculty, should the wound's fixed compensation (arsh) be paid separately, or does it merge into the full diya? The answer hinges on whether the lost faculty is considered 'hidden' (batin) like sanity, or 'apparent' (zahir) like sight. We will explore the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the two narrations from Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa (and one narration of Abu Yusuf) that no merger occurs for any of the three faculties, and the second narration of Abu Yusuf that merger occurs for hearing and speech but not for sight.
The first position treats all three faculties equally; the second distinguishes based on hiddenness.
2
Analyze the proof of the first position
Understand that each faculty (hearing, speech, sight) has a benefit specific to its organ, like different limbs. Since tadaakhul does not apply to different limbs, it does not apply here. This is a qiyas on limbs.
The benefit of each faculty is localized, unlike sanity which benefits all limbs.
3
Analyze the proof of the second position
Hearing and speech are hidden faculties (batin), analogous to sanity (aql). Since the wound's arsh merges into diya for loss of sanity, it also merges for hearing and speech. Sight is apparent (zahir), so no merger.
The analogy (qiyas) is on hiddenness, not on specificity of benefit.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under the first position, the victim receives both arsh (wound) and full diya (faculty) for each lost faculty. Under the second, for hearing/speech only diya is paid; for sight both are paid.
The practical difference is significant: double compensation vs. single compensation for hidden faculties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ال وان ذهب سمعه او بصره او كلامه فعليه ارش الموضحة مع الدية قالوا هذا قول أبي حنيفة وابي يوسف [؟] الله وعن أبي يوسف ان الشجة تدخل فى دية السمع والكلام ولاتدخل فى دية البصر وجه الاول ان كلامنها جناية فيمادون النفس والمنفعة مختصة به فاشبه الاعضاء المختلفة بخلاف العقل لان منفعة عائدة [؟] جميع الاعضاء على مابينا وجه الثانى ان السمع والكلام مبطن فيعتبر بالعقل والبصر ظاهر فلا يلحق به
ثم جمعہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر (موضحہ کی وجہ سے) اس کی قوت سماعت یا اس کی بصر یا اس کی گویائی ختم ہو گئی تو اس پر دیت کے ساتھ ساتھ موضحہ کا ارش ہے، مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ یہ [؟] کا قول ہے اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ شجہ سماعت اور گویائی کی دیت میں تو داخل ہوگا اور بصر کی دیت میں داخل نہ ہوگا، اول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک ایسی جنایت ہے جو مادون النفس میں ہے اور منفعت ان میں سے ہر ایک کے ساتھ مختص ہے تو یہ اعضاء مختلفہ کے مشابہ ہو گئے۔ بخلاف عقل کہ اس لئے کہ اس کی منفعت تمام اعضاء کی جانب راجع ہے جیسا کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ ثانی قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ سمع اور کلام باطنی چیزیں ہیں تو ان کو عقل پر قیاس کیا جائے گا اور بصر ظاہری چیز ہے تو اس کو عقل کے ساتھ الحاق نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ تشریح: زید نے خالد کا سر پھوڑ دیا جس کی وجہ سے موضحہ ہو گیا اور ساتھ ہی ساتھ قوت سماعت یا بینائی یا گویائی بھی جاتی رہی تو اب کیا حکم ہے تداخل ہوگا یا نہیں؟ تو اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول عدم تداخل کا ہے اور امام ابو یوسف سے دو روایتیں ہیں ایک میں وہ امام صاحب کے ساتھ ہیں اور دوسری میں ان کے یہاں تفصیل ہے یعنی مذکورہ تین قوتوں میں سے ایک یعنی بصر میں وہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے ساتھ ہیں اور سمع اور کلام میں وہ تداخل کے قائل ہیں۔ اب دونوں روایتوں کی دلیل دیکھئے۔ عدم تداخل کی دلیل: ان تینوں قوتوں میں سے ہر ایک میں جو جنایت ہے یہ جنایت فیمادون النفس ہے اور ان میں سے ہر ایک کی منفعت اسی کے ساتھ مختص ہے یعنی بولنا صرف زبان کا کام ہے اور سننا سماعت کا اور دیکھنا آنکھ کا، لہذا یہ اعضاء مختلفہ کے مشابہ ہوئے اور اعضاء مختلفہ میں تداخل نہیں ہوا کرتا، لہذا یہاں بھی تداخل نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ ان کے ختم ہونے کی دیت دینی ہوگی اور موضحہ کا ارش الگ دینا ہوگا۔ اور عقل کی صورت میں تداخل کا قول اس لئے اختیار کیا تھا کہ عقل کی منفعت پورے بدن کی جانب راجع ہے اور یہاں ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ ہر قوت اپنے مخصوص دائرے میں کام کرتی ہے۔ دوسری روایت کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قوت سماعت اور گویائی باطنی اور مخفی چیزیں ہیں جیسے عقل مخفی اور باطنی چیز ہے تو ان دونوں کو عقل پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے وہی حکم دیا گیا جو عقل کی صورت میں ہے، اور بصر ایک ظاہری قوت ہے تو اس کو عقل پر قیاس نہیں کیا گیا اور عدم تداخل کے قول کو اختیار کیا گیا۔
And if his hearing, sight, or speech is lost, then upon him is the arsh of the muwaddiha along with the full diya. They said: This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them). And from Abu Yusuf [it is narrated] that the head wound enters into the diya of hearing and speech and does not enter into the diya of sight. The justification of the first: that each of them is an injury below the soul and the benefit is specific to it, so it resembles different limbs, unlike the mind because its benefit returns to all limbs as we explained. The justification of the second: that hearing and speech are hidden, so they are measured by analogy to the mind, and sight is apparent, so it is not attached to it.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the compensation (arsh) for a muwaddiha wound merges with the diya for losing a sensory faculty. The first opinion, attributed to Abu Hanifa and one narration from Abu Yusuf, holds that they do not merge because each loss is a separate injury below the soul, and the benefit of each faculty is specific to that part, similar to different limbs. The second opinion, from another narration of Abu Yusuf, distinguishes between latent faculties (hearing and speech) and the apparent faculty (sight). For hearing and speech, the wound's arsh merges into the diya, analogous to the case of sanity, while for sight it does not merge. The commentator explains the reasoning: the first opinion views each faculty as a distinct benefit, so no merger; the second opinion analogizes hidden faculties to sanity, which is a hidden condition affecting the whole body. The practical outcome is that in the first view, the victim receives both the arsh for the wound and the diya for the lost faculty, while in the second view, for hearing and speech, only the diya is due, but for sight, both are due.

Key Terms
موضحہ (muwaddiha): A head wound that exposes the bone
ارش (arsh): Fixed compensation for wounds, less than full diya
دیت (diya): Blood money paid for loss of life or faculties
تداخل (tadakhul): Merging of compensations where one injury is subsumed under another
باطن (batin): Hidden or internal faculties

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Sight only
B) Hearing and speech
C) All three faculties
D) None of the three

Key Takeaway
Whether arsh merges with diya depends on whether the lost faculty is considered hidden (like sanity) or apparent (like sight); the school's relied-upon position is the non-merger view.

Qisas and Diya for Muwaddiha with Loss of Both Eyes
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas and diya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn) on qisas and diya for a muwaddiha that also causes loss of both eyes and apply the ruling to a similar compound injury scenario.

Core Idea
A muwaddiha that blinds both eyes triggers two compensations: the wound and the eyes, with a dispute on qisas for the wound.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), regarding a compound injury: a head wound (muwaddiha) that also destroys both eyes. The key issue is whether qisas (retaliation) applies to the wound itself and what compensation is due for each injury component.

Guided Path
1
Identify the injury components
The scenario involves two separate injuries: a muwaddiha wound (exposing the bone) and the loss of both eyes. Understand that each injury may have its own ruling and compensation.
2
State Abu Hanifa’s position
Abu Hanifa holds that there is no qisas for the muwaddiha wound because it is a type of wound where precise equivalence is difficult. Instead, the assailant must pay diya for the eyes and arsh (fixed compensation) for the wound.
Abu Hanifa’s view is based on the principle that qisas is limited to wounds where exact retaliation is possible.
3
State the Sahibayn’s position
The Sahibayn hold that qisas is due for the muwaddiha wound, analogizing it to other wounds where qisas is possible. Additionally, they agree that diya is due for the loss of both eyes.
The Sahibayn’s analogy extends qisas to this wound despite the difficulty in exact equivalence.
4
Note the textual omission and supplementation
The text of al-Jami' al-Saghir (quoted in the lesson) only mentions the dispute over qisas for the wound but does not explicitly state that diya for the eyes is due in both views. The mashayikh (later scholars) supplement the text by clarifying that diya for the eyes is agreed upon.
This teaches an important principle: later commentaries often complete what the original matn left implied.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Abu Hanifa: the victim receives diya for both eyes (full diya, e.g., 100 camels) plus arsh for the wound. Under the Sahibayn: the assailant suffers qisas for the wound (the same wound inflicted on him) and also pays diya for the eyes.
The practical difference is whether the attacker faces physical retaliation or only financial penalty for the wound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وفى الجامع الصغير ومن شج رجلا موضحة فذهبت عيناه فلا قصاص فى ذلك عند ابي حنيفة قالوا وينبغي ان تجب الدية فيهما وقالا في الموضحة القصاص قالوا وينبغى أن تجب الدية في العينين
ترجمہ مصنف نے فرمایا اور جامع صغیر میں ہے اور جس نے کسی شخص کو شجة موضحہ لگایا پس اس کی دونوں آنکھیں ختم ہو گئیں تو اس میں ابی حنیفہ کے نزدیک قصاص نہیں ہے مشائخ نے فرمایا اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں دیت واجب ہو، اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ موضحہ میں قصاص ہے مشائخ نے فرمایا اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ دونوں آنکھوں میں دیت واجب ہو۔ تشریح اگر کسی نے زید کا سر پھوڑا جس سے زخم موضحہ ہو گیا اور زید کی دونوں آنکھوں کی روشنی ختم ہوگئی تو ایسی صورت میں امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک دونوں آنکھوں کی دیت اور موضحہ کا ارش واجب ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک موضحہ میں قصاص اور آنکھوں میں دیت واجب ہے یہ ہے اصل مسئلہ اب صاحب ہدایہ جامع صغیر کی عبارت جو اس مسئلہ کے بارے میں ہے اس کو نقل کر کے اس کی کمی کو ظاہر کرتے ہیں تو جامع صغیر کی عبارت یہ ہے " و من شج رجلا موضحةً فذهبت عيناه فلا قصاص فى ذلك عندا بى حنيفة، وقالا في الموضحة القصاص " تو اس میں صرف یہ کہا گیا ہے کہ ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک قصاص نہیں ہے مگر دیت اور ارش واجب ہے جس کو بیان نہیں کیا گیا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک موضحہ میں قصاص واجب ہے لیکن آنکھوں کی دیت کو بیان نہیں کیا گیا ہے۔
He said: And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: Whoever wounds a person with a muwaddiha and his eyes are lost, then there is no qisas in that according to Abu Hanifa. They said: It is appropriate that the diya is due in the two eyes. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: In the muwaddiha, qisas is due. They said: It is appropriate that the diya is due in the two eyes.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage discusses the case where a muwaddiha wound causes loss of both eyes. According to Abu Hanifa, there is no qisas for the wound itself because it is a wound that does not entail qisas according to his view, but the diya for the eyes is due along with the arsh for the muwaddiha. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that qisas is applicable for the muwaddiha wound, and additionally, diya is due for the loss of both eyes. The commentator notes that the text of al-Jami' al-Saghir only mentions the difference regarding qisas but omits to state the diya for the eyes, which is mentioned by the mashayikh (later scholars) supplementing the text. The practical effect is that in Abu Hanifa's view, the victim gets diya for eyes plus arsh for wound; in the Sahibayn's view, the assailant faces qisas for the wound plus diya for the eyes.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retributive justice; exacting a similar injury upon the assailant
جامع صغیر (al-Jami' al-Saghir): One of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
موضحة (muwaddiha): A wound that exposes the bone
دية (diya): Financial compensation for manslaughter or injury to limbs/senses

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, what is the ruling for a muwaddiha that causes loss of both eyes?
A) No qisas for wound; only diya for eyes
B) Qisas for wound and diya for eyes
C) Only diya for eyes, no arsh
D) No compensation at all

Key Takeaway
In a muwaddiha causing loss of both eyes, both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree that diya is due for the eyes; they differ on whether qisas applies to the wound.

Compensation for Finger Joint Cutting with Paralysis and Tooth Breaking with Blackening
Hanafi ruling on diya and hukumat for partial injury with after-effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for a cut finger joint that causes paralysis, and distinguish between diya for the direct injury and hukumat 'adl for the consequential loss.

Core Idea
When an injury causes additional functional loss, fixed diya for the direct injury is supplemented by hukumat for the consequential loss.

This lesson examines two specific injury scenarios from the Hanafi school: cutting a finger joint that leads to paralysis of the remaining part, and breaking part of a tooth that causes the remainder to turn black. The rulings clarify that no qisas applies to the after-effects, but financial compensation—diya and hukumat 'adl—must be paid. The passage, transmitted by Imam Muhammad without recorded disagreement, demonstrates how the Hanafi school balances fixed penalties with equitable assessment for losses not covered by fixed arsh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the act is (cutting a finger joint, breaking part of a tooth) and the initial consequence (paralysis, blackening). The ruling: no qisas for the after-effect; only financial compensation.
Focus on the shift from qisas to diya/hukumat.
2
Classify the types of compensation
Distinguish between diya (fixed blood money for the severed joint or whole tooth) and hukumat 'adl (equitable compensation for the loss of function in the paralyzed part or blackened tooth). Diya is fixed; hukumat is assessed by a judge.
Diya for the finger joint is one-third of the finger's diya.
3
Understand the basis for no qisas
Qisas is not applicable because the paralysis or blackening is an indirect result (not a direct amputation). In Hanafi law, qisas is only for direct intentional injury to a limb or joint where retaliation is possible.
This prevents excessive punishment for consequential damage.
4
Apply the same principle to the tooth case
Breaking part of a tooth that turns black means the whole tooth is effectively lost. Therefore, diya for the whole tooth is due, not just for the broken part. This parallels the finger case where the after-effect entails additional compensation.
The blackening indicates the tooth is no longer functional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وان قطع اصبع رجل من المفصل الاعلى فشل مابقى من الاصبع او اليد كلها لا قصاص عليه في شئ من ذلك وينبغى ان تجب الدية فى المفصل الاعلى وفيما بقى حكومة عدل وكذالك لو كسر بعض سن رجل فاسود ما بقى ولم يحك خلافا وينبغى ان تجب الدية في السن كله
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور اگر کسی مرد کی انگلی کو اوپر کے پورے سے کاٹ دیا پس باقی انگلی یا باقی ہاتھ شل ہو گیا تو اس پر ان میں سے کسی شئی کا قصاص نہ ہوگا اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ پہلے پورے میں دیت اور مابقی میں حکومت عدل واجب ہو اور ایسے ہی (قصاص نہیں ہے)۔ اگر کسی شخص کے دانت کا کچھ حصہ توڑ دیا پس مابقی سیاہ ہو گیا اور محمد نے اختلاف نقل نہیں کیا اور مناسب یہ ہے کہ پورے دانت میں دیت واجب ہو جائے۔
He said: And if a person cuts a man's finger from the upper joint and the remaining part of the finger or the whole hand becomes paralyzed, then there is no qisas upon him in any of that. And it is appropriate that the diya is due for the upper joint and for what remains a hukumat 'adl. Likewise, if he breaks part of a tooth and the remainder turns black, and no disagreement is reported, and it is appropriate that the diya is due for the whole tooth.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage gives two rulings without recorded disagreement among the Hanafi school. First, if a person cuts off the upper joint of a finger and the remaining part of the finger or the entire hand becomes paralyzed (shalla), then no qisas is due for the paralysis because it is an indirect result. Instead, the assailant must pay diya for the cut joint (which is a fixed amount, one-third of the diya of the whole finger) and for the paralyzed part, a hukumat 'adl (equitable compensation assessed by a judge based on the loss). Second, if a person breaks part of a tooth and the remaining part turns black (indicating death of the tooth), then diya for the whole tooth is due, even though only part was broken, because the blackening renders the entire tooth useless. The commentator notes that Imam Muhammad did not report any disagreement on these rulings, indicating consensus among the Hanafi masters.

Key Terms
شل (shalla): Paralysis or loss of function in the remaining part
حکومت عدل (hukumat 'adl): Equitable compensation assessed by the judge based on the value of the lost function
دیت (diya): Fixed blood money for specific body parts or losses

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person cuts off the upper joint of another's finger and the rest of the finger becomes paralyzed?
A) Qisas for the joint and hukumat for the paralysis
B) No compensation at all
C) Diya for the cut joint and hukumat for the paralyzed part
D) Only diya for the whole finger

Key Takeaway
For injuries causing after-effects like paralysis or blackening, the Hanafi school requires diya for the direct damage and hukumat for the consequential functional loss, with no qisas for indirect results.

Mawdihah Causing Blindness: Qisas or Diyah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas and diyah for mawdihah causing blindness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on qisas for a mawdihah that causes blindness, and state the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Transitivity of a wound can block qisas: if the act's effect spreads uncontrollably, only financial compensation is due.

In this passage, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute: when a deliberate head wound (mawdihah) unintentionally causes blindness, should qisas apply? The Sahibayn argue for qisas on the head plus diyah for the eyes; Imam Abu Hanifa holds that transitivity of the wound makes qisas impossible, so only monetary penalties are due.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario and the disputed ruling
What is the exact case? A striker inflicts a mawdihah (head wound exposing bone) and the victim loses eyesight. The dispute: does qisas apply on the head?
2
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that two separate penalties are due: qisas for the head and diyah for the eyes. Their proof: multiplicity of loci (head vs. eyes), and analogy to an arrow that passes through and kills two persons.
The arrow analogy: qisas for first, diyah for second.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds only financial compensation: arsh for the wound and diyah for the eyes, no qisas. His proof: the wound is transitive (sariyah), qisas requires exact equivalence which is impossible since transitivity is uncontrollable; the act and place are one; doubt at the end creates doubt in the beginning.
Unity of act and place due to strong connection between head and eyes.
4
Analyze the responses to analogies
How does Abu Hanifa refute the arrow and knife analogies? The arrow case: two deaths are not connected by transitivity; they are separate hits. The knife case: the second cut is a separate act, not a completion of the first. Here the eye loss is a direct transitive effect of the first wound.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
Practical difference: under Sahibayn, the striker faces both qisas and diyah; under Abu Hanifa, only financial compensation. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's because doubt removes qisas.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah adopts this view.
