Diyat for Tooth Discoloration: When Qisas Is Impossible
Lists diyat and qisas consequences for tooth discoloration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyat and qisas when a tooth changes color after a blow and explain the proof based on impossibility of exact retaliation.

Core Idea
If a tooth discolours but does not fall, diyat is due; qisas is impossible and thus not wajib.

This passage addresses a specific injury: a tooth that changes colour to black, red, or green after a blow, without falling out. The Hanafi school rules that the striker must pay diyat (blood money) in both accidental and intentional cases, but qisas (retaliation in kind) is not applicable. The reason is that exact retaliation cannot be achieved—no one can strike a blow that produces precisely the same discolouration. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a blow that discolours a tooth without causing it to fall. The ruling is that diyat is wajib on the striker or his aqilah, and qisas is not wajib.
Distinguish between khata (accidental) and amd (intentional) for who pays the diyat.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a rational argument (qiyas): retaliation is impossible because one cannot replicate the exact discolouration.
This is a 'dalil aqli' (rational evidence) based on the concept of mumathala (equivalence) in qisas.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The impossibility of exact retaliation means that the condition for qisas—equal retaliation—cannot be met. Therefore, the law shifts to monetary compensation (diyat).
The same reasoning applies regardless of the colour (black, red, green).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that if the tooth does not change colour at all, Hukumat al-Adl (equitable compensation) may be due. But for discolouration, all three Hanafi imams agree on diyat and no qisas.
This intra-madhhab difference does not affect the present ruling.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that diyat is due and qisas is not. This is based on the consensus of the three imams for this specific scenario.
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن ابى يوسف انه تجب حكومة الأوسنبين الوجهين بعد هذا ان شاء تعالى ولولم تسقط ولكهنا اسودت يجب الا رش في الخطا على العاقلة وفى العمد في ماله ولا يجب القصاص لانه لا يمكنه ان يضربه ضربا تسود منه وكذا اذا كسر بعضه واسود الباقى لا قصاص لما ذكرنا وكذام حمر او اخضر ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ تکلیف میں حکومت عدل ہے اور ہم اس کے بعد انشاء اللہ تعالیٰ دونوں وجہوں کو بیان کریں گے اور اگر دانت گرانہ ہو بلکہ سیاہ پڑ گیا ہو تو خطاء کی صورت میں عاقلہ پر دیت واجب ہے۔ اور عمد کی صورت میں اس کے ان میں اور قصاص واجب نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ مضروب کو مکن نہیں کہ ضارب کو ایسی چوٹ مارے جس سے دانت سیاہ پڑ جائے اور ایسے ہی جب کہ دانت کا کچھ حصہ تو ڑا اور باقی سیاہ ہو گیا تو قصاص نہ ہوگا اسی وجہ سے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ اور ایسے ہی اگر سرخ ہو جائے یا پیلا ہو جائے۔ تشریح اگر دانت گرا نہ ہو تو کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا لیکن امام ابو یوسف اس صورت میں حکومت عدل کو واجب کرتے ہیں جس کی وجہ اگلے مسئلہ میں آرہی اور اسی کا مصنف نے حوالہ دیا ہے۔ اور اگر دانت گرا تو نہ ہولیکن سیاہ پڑ گیا ہوتو اگر یہ قتل خطا ہوا تو عاقلہ پر دیت واجب ہوگی۔ اور اگر عمد ہوا ہوتو مارنے والے کے مال میں دیت واجب ہوگی اور قصاص اس لئے واجب نہ ہوگا کہ یہ غیر ممکن ہے کہ مضروب اس طرح ضارب کو مارے جس سے اس کا دانت سیاہ پڑ جائے۔ اور اسی طرح اگر دانت کا کچھ حصہ تو ڑ دیا جس کی وجہ سے باقی سیاہ پڑ گیا اب بھی قصاص نہ ہو گا اسی دلیل مذکور کی وجہ سے اور اگر سرخ یا سبز پڑ گیا ہوتب بھی قصاص نہ ہوگا بدلیل مذکور بالا ۔
And from Abu Yusuf that Hukumat al-Adl is obligatory between the two aspects after this, God willing. And if it does not fall but turns black, then diyat in case of khata is upon the aqilah, and in case of amd upon his wealth, and qisas is not obligatory because it is impossible for him to strike him a blow that would turn his tooth black. Similarly, if part is broken and the rest turns black, no qisas for what we mentioned. Similarly, if it turns red or green. Translation: And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that in difficulty Hukumat al-Adl is obligatory, and we will explain both aspects after this, God willing. And if the tooth does not fall but becomes black, then in case of khata, diyat is upon the aqilah; in case of amd, upon his wealth, and qisas is not obligatory because it is impossible for the victim to strike the striker such that his tooth blackens. Similarly, if part is broken and the rest becomes black, then no qisas for the same reason. Similarly, if it becomes red or green. Commentary: If the tooth does not fall, nothing is obligatory, but Imam Abu Yusuf makes Hukumat al-Adl obligatory in this case, which will be explained in the next issue. And if the tooth does not fall but turns black, then if it was khata, diyat is upon the aqilah; if amd, diyat from the striker's wealth, and qisas is not obligatory because it is impossible. Similarly, if part is broken and rest turns black, also no qisas. And if red or green, also no qisas due to the mentioned proof.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage deals with scenarios where a tooth is struck but does not fall; instead it changes color. The Hanafi ruling: if the tooth turns black (or red/green), the striker is liable for diyat (full blood money) in cases of both accidental (khata) and intentional (amd) injury. However, qisas (retaliation in kind) is not applicable because it is impossible to inflict a blow that produces exactly the same discoloration. In khata, the diyat is paid by the aqilah (the striker's clan), and in amd, from the striker's own wealth. The passage also references Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion about Hukumat al-Adl (equitable compensation) in some cases, which is a separate issue. The key principle is that any injury that cannot be exactly reciprocated due to its specific nature is subject to monetary compensation rather than qisas.

Key Terms
اسوداد (iswidād): Blackening of the tooth due to the blow.
حكومة عدل (ḥukūmat al-ʿadl): Equitable compensation assessed by a judge for injuries without fixed diyat.
عاقلة (ʿāqilah): The clan or tribe responsible for paying diyat in cases of accidental killing or injury.
دية (diyah): Blood money: monetary compensation for killing or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because tooth injuries are always subject to diyat only.
B) Because exact retaliation is impossible.
C) Because the victim must forgive.
D) Because the tooth did not fall out.

Key Takeaway
When a tooth discolours without falling, diyat is due and qisas is not applicable due to the impossibility of exact retaliation.

Compensation for Healing Head Wound: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on arsh for healed head wound.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding compensation for a head wound that heals without a trace, and explain the legal cause (illah) for their disagreement.

Core Idea
No blemish, no arsh: Abu Hanifa; pain compensable: Abu Yusuf.

This passage from Kitab al-Diyat presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the founder and his chief disciple. At stake is the very basis of compensation for injuries: is it the visible blemish (shayn) or the experience of pain (alam)? Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping the Hanafi theory of damages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The case: a head wound (shajjah) heals completely, leaving no trace, and hair regrows. Determine the legal question.
The question is whether any compensation (arsh) is due.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Ruling and Reasoning
Abu Hanifa rules no arsh because the blemish (shayn) that necessitated compensation has disappeared.
The illah is the existence of a visible defect.
3
State Abu Yusuf's Ruling and Reasoning
Abu Yusuf rules that arsh for pain (alam) is due, assessed via hukumat al-adl, because pain remains even after the blemish disappears.
The illah for him includes the experience of pain.
4
Extract the Legal Cause (Illah) Disagreement
Abu Hanifa: shayn is the sole cause. Abu Yusuf: alam is also a compensable harm. Identify how each defines the effective cause.
This is a difference in tahqiq al-manat.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf and Mufta Bihi
Under Abu Hanifa, no payment; under Abu Yusuf, payment for pain. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's.
The matn indicates Abu Hanifa's view as the default.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن شج رجلا فالتحمت ولم يبق لها اثرو نبت الشعر سقط الارش عند ابي حنيفة لزوال الشين الموجب وقال ابو يوسف يجب عليه ارش الا لم وهو حكومة عدل لان الشين ان زال فالا لم الحاصل مازال فيجب تقويمه ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی کا سر پھوڑ دیا پس زخم بھر گیا اور اس کا کوئی نشان باقی نہیں رہا اور بال جم گئے تو ابوحنیفہ کے
He said: And who wounded a person's head, and it healed and left no trace, and hair grew, then the arsh falls according to Abu Hanifa due to disappearance of the blemish that necessitates compensation. And Abu Yusuf said: He must pay arsh of the pain, which is hukumat al-adl, because even if the blemish is gone, the pain experienced has not disappeared, so it must be evaluated. Translation: Quduri said: And who wounded a person's head, then the wound healed and no trace remained, and hair grew, then according to Abu Hanifa ('s view...) [incomplete].
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute from Kitab al-Diyat. The scenario: a head wound (shajjah) heals completely without any scar or disfigurement, and hair regrows. Abu Hanifa rules that no compensation (arsh) is due because the blemish (shayn) that warranted compensation has been removed. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, stating that even if the blemish disappeared, the victim experienced pain (alam) during the injury and its treatment, and that harm remains. He holds that Hukumat al-Adl (an equitable assessment of damages) must be paid for the pain. This difference is based on the legal cause (illah) for compensation: according to Abu Hanifa, the blemish itself is the cause; for Abu Yusuf, both blemish and pain are compensable. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa, as indicated by the matn. However, the text is incomplete; it only gives the beginning of the Urdu translation, but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
شجہ (shajjah): A head wound.
التحمت (iltaḥamat): The wound healed and closed up.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for injuries less than those with fixed diyat.
شین (shayn): Blemish; disfigurement or defect that warrants compensation.
ألم (alam): Pain experienced by the victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Depends on the victim's pain

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi diyat, arsh is only due if a blemish (shayn) remains; pain alone does not justify compensation according to the relied-upon view.

Ruling on Tooth Turning Black: Dispute of Abu Yusuf on Hukumat al-Adl
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for tooth discoloration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Abu Yusuf regarding compensation for a tooth that changes color without falling, and distinguish it from Abu Hanifa's position.

Core Idea
A tooth that discolors without falling may still require compensation (hukumat al-adl) under Abu Yusuf, even though no fixed arsh is due.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning compensation (arsh/hukumat al-adl) when a tooth changes color but does not fall. The base ruling of Zahir al-Riwayah (Abu Hanifa) holds that no arsh is due since the tooth remains physically present. However, Imam Abu Yusuf introduces a nuanced view: the pain and functional impairment justify equitable compensation called hukumat al-adl. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurists balance fixed rules against actual harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Recognize that the default Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) holds no arsh for a tooth that discolors without falling.
This is derived from Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
State Abu Yusuf's exception
Imam Abu Yusuf rules that hukumat al-adl (equitable compensation) is wajib for the harm caused by discoloration.
The amount is assessed by the judge.
3
Differentiate between 'amd and khata'
If the act was intentional ('amd), compensation is from the offender's wealth; if by mistake (khata'), it is on the 'aqila.
This affects who pays.
4
Explain why qisas is inapplicable
Qisas (retaliation) is impossible because one cannot strike the offender to cause the exact same discoloration.
Thus monetary compensation is substituted.
5
Apply the ruling to similar cases
The same rule applies if part of the tooth is broken and the rest discolored, or if it turns red or green.
Consistency in the legal principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعن أبي يوسف أنه تجب حكومة العدل بين الوجهين بعد هذا إن شاء تعالى. ولو لم تسقط ولكنها اسودت يجب الأرش في الخطأ على العاقلة وفي العمد في ماله ولا يجب القصاص لأنه لا يمكنه أن يضربه ضربًا تسود منه. وكذا إذا كسر بعضه واسود الباقي لا قصاص لما ذكرنا. وكذا إذا احمر أو اخضر.
And from Abu Yusuf: Hukumat al-Adl is obligatory between the two aspects, after this if Allah wills. And if it did not fall but became black, the arsh is obligatory in the case of error upon the 'aqila, and in the case of intentional upon his wealth, and qisas is not obligatory because it is not possible for him to strike him a blow that makes it black. Similarly, if he broke part of it and the rest became black, no qisas due to what we mentioned. Similarly, if it became red or green.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding compensation for a tooth that does not fall but changes color. The base ruling (Imam Abu Hanifa's view, implied) is that if the tooth does not fall, no arsh is due. However, Imam Abu Yusuf argues that hukumat al-adl (equitable compensation) is wajib for the harm caused, as the tooth has lost its function and appearance. He also specifies that if the act was khata' (unintentional), the diyah is on the 'aqila (tribal guarantors), and if 'amd (intentional), it is on the offender's own wealth (since it's not subject to qisas due to difficulty in exact retaliation). The reason qisas is not applicable is that it is impossible to strike the offender in exactly the same manner to cause discoloration. The same ruling applies if part of the tooth is broken and the rest discolored, or if it turns red or green.

Key Terms
حكومة العدل (hukumat al-adl): Equitable compensation assessed by the judge for harm that does not have a fixed diyah or arsh.
أرش (arsh): Fixed compensation for injuries causing loss of a body part or its function.
عاقلة ('aqila): The paternal relatives (asabah) who bear the diyah in cases of accidental homicide or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full diyah
B) Nothing
C) Hukumat al-Adl
D) Qisas

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Yusuf's view that hukumat al-adl is due for tooth discoloration without fall introduces an equitable compensation principle within the Hanafi school, distinct from the default no-arsh rule.

Ruling on Wound Healing Completely: Dispute on Arsh for Pain
Intra-Hanafi dispute over compensation for a fully healed head wound.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on compensation for a fully healed head wound and explain the principle that the mufta bihi is based on.

Core Idea
A wound that heals without trace yields no compensation: benefits (manafi') are not compensable without contract.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a head wound (shajjah) that heals completely with no trace. Abu Hanifa holds that no arsh is due because the defect is gone. Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad differ, but the relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa’s, grounded in the usul principle that benefits (manafi’) are not compensable except by contract or its equivalent.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the common scenario: a head wound that heals completely with no trace and hair regrows.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Abu Hanifa: no compensation (arsh) because the defect (shayn) that warranted arsh is removed.
3
Identify Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf: arsh al-alam (pain) is wajib, assessed as hukumat al-adl.
4
Identify Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad: also wajib to pay doctor's fee and medicine cost, as direct financial loss caused by the offender.
5
Analyse Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
Abu Hanifa counters: manafi' (benefits) are not compensable without contract or its equivalent; medical costs are benefits consumed, not property.
This rebuttal relies on a key Hanafi usul principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: ومن شج رجلا فالتحمت ولم يبق لها أثر ونبت الشعر سقط الأرش عند أبي حنيفة لزوال الشين الموجب. وقال أبو يوسف: يجب عليه أرش الألم وهو حكومة عدل. وقال محمد: عليه أجرة الطبيب وثمن الدواء لأنه إنما لزمه أجرة الطبيب وثمن الدواء بفعله فصار كأنه أخذ ذلك من ماله. إلا أن أبا حنيفة يقول: إن المنافع على أصلنا لا تتقوم إلا بعقد أو بشبهة ولم يوجد في حق الجاني فلا يغرم شيئًا.
He said: And whoever wounds a person in the head (shajjah), and it heals and no trace remains, and hair grows, the arsh drops according to Abu Hanifa due to removal of the defect that necessitates it. And Abu Yusuf said: He owes arsh for the pain, which is hukumat al-adl. And Muhammad said: He owes the doctor's fee and the cost of medicine, because he incurred the doctor's fee and medicine cost by his action, so it is as if he took that from his wealth. Except that Abu Hanifa says: Benefits (manafi') according to our principle are not compensable except by contract or its equivalent, and none exists in the case of the offender, so he guarantees nothing.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage addresses a complete shajjah (head wound) that heals with no visible trace and regrows hair. The dispute is intra-Hanafi.
- Abu Hanifa: No arsh is due because the defect (shayn) that would warrant compensation has been fully eliminated; the wound no longer exists.
- Abu Yusuf: Arsh for the pain (alam) is wajib, assessed as hukumat al-adl, because the pain and suffering that occurred during the injury remain a compensable harm even after the wound heals.
- Imam Muhammad: The offender must also pay the doctor's fee and medicine costs incurred by the victim, as these are direct financial losses caused by his action.
- Abu Hanifa counters that, according to usul, benefits (manafi') are not compensable except via a contract or a quasi-contract (shubhat al-'aqd). Since there is no such contract between the offender and victim, he is not liable for these amounts. The doctor's fee and medicine are considered benefits consumed by the victim, not direct property loss.

Key Terms
شج (shajj): A head wound that reaches the bone; a specific type of injury with its own rulings.
شين (shayn): A defect or disfigurement that warrants compensation; its removal eliminates arsh.
ألم (alam): Pain suffered due to injury; Abu Yusuf considers it compensable even after healing.
منافع (manafi'): Benefits or utilities; according to Hanafi usul, they are not compensable without contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On what basis does Imam Muhammad hold the offender liable for the doctor's fee?
A) Contract between the parties
B) The offender's act caused the victim to incur the expense
C) It is a fixed arsh amount
D) The victim's consent

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a wound that heals completely with no trace negates compensation because the defect is gone and benefits (manafi') are not compensable without contract.

Compensation for Beating with Whip: When Trace Remains or Heals
Short ruling on compensation for beating that leaves no trace

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios of compensation for beating with a whip and identify which ruling applies based on whether a trace remains.

Core Idea
If a beating leaves a trace, arsh al-darb is due; if no trace, the ruling follows the dispute on healed head wounds.

This lesson clarifies a specific ruling from the matn regarding a person who is beaten with a whip, sustains wounds, and later recovers. The key factor is whether a trace (athar) of the beating remains after recovery. If it does, a fixed compensation called arsh al-darb is payable. If the skin heals completely without any trace, the case falls under the earlier dispute on shajjah multahimah (a healed head wound). Understanding this distinction is important for correctly assessing compensation in cases of physical harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two possibilities: (1) a trace of the beating remains after recovery, or (2) no trace remains. The ruling differs between these.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
If a trace remains, arsh al-darb (compensation for beating) is wajib. If no trace remains, the ruling is not fixed here; it references a previous dispute on shajjah multahimah.
The arsh al-darb is a fixed amount determined by the severity of the beating.
3
Connect to the earlier dispute
The 'difference that has preceded' refers to the ikhtilaf among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding a head wound that heals without scarring. That dispute applies here by analogy.
Refer to the earlier lesson on shajjah multahimah for the details of that dispute.
4
Apply the condition
Test a case: if a victim is beaten, wounds heal but a scar remains → arsh al-darb due. If no scar, then evaluate according to the shajjah multahimah dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: ومن ضرب رجلا مائة سوط فجرحه فبرأ منها فعليه أرش الضرب. معناه إذا بقي أثر الضرب. فأما إذا لم يبق أثره فهو على اختلاف قد مضى في الشجة الملتحمة.
He said: And whoever strikes a man a hundred lashes, and wounds him, and he recovers from them, then he owes the arsh of the beating. Its meaning: if there remains a trace of the beating. However, if no trace remains, then it is subject to the difference that has preceded regarding the healed head wound.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from the matn regarding a case where a person is beaten with a whip (hundred lashes) and sustains wounds but later recovers fully. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios:
1. If a trace (athar) of the beating remains (e.g., scarring), then arsh al-darb (compensation for beating) is due. This arsh is likely a fixed amount depending on the severity.
2. If no trace remains, the ruling follows the ikhtilaf previously discussed regarding the shajjah mul'tahima (head wound that healed). So, the opinions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad apply analogously: Abu Hanifa says no compensation, Abu Yusuf says hukumat al-adl for pain, and Muhammad adds medical expenses.
The passage does not resolve the dispute; it simply references the earlier discussion.

Key Terms
أرش الضرب (arsh al-darb): Fixed compensation due for beating that leaves a trace, assessed based on the severity of the beating.
شجة ملتحمة (shajjah multahimah): A head wound that has healed and closed up; referenced for analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The obligation of arsh al-darb depends on the presence of a trace after healing; otherwise, the case is referred to the ikhtilaf on healed head wounds.

Compensation for a Healed Wound: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on arsh for healed wound

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on compensation for a wound that heals completely and explain the underlying principle that manafi' are not compensable without a contract or its semblance.

Core Idea
A healed wound removes arsh, but pain (manafi') may require just assessment or medical costs, depending on the imam.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether compensation is due when a wound heals without leaving any trace. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that no arsh is due because the defect that triggered the arsh no longer exists. Imam Abu Yusuf argues for a just assessment (hukumat al-adl) for the pain and loss of health, while Imam Muhammad requires the offender to pay the doctor's fee and medicine cost. The disagreement hinges on whether benefits (manafi') like pain are compensable in tort without a contractual basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the central question
Consider: a person wounds another on the head; the wound heals completely with no trace. Is any compensation due from the offender? The passage presents three answers from the founding Hanafi imams.
The scenario is specific: complete healing, no residual defect.
2
State Abu Hanifa's ruling and its basis
Imam Abu Hanifa says no arsh is due because the defect that required the arsh has ceased. His principle: manafi' (benefits such as pain) are not compensable in tort except through a valid or defective contract.
The key term 'manafi'' is critical.
3
State Abu Yusuf's ruling and its basis
Abu Yusuf says a just assessment (hukumat al-adl) is obligatory for the pain that was experienced, even though the defect vanished. He treats pain as a compensable loss independent of the defect.
He differentiates between the defect and the pain.
4
State Muhammad's ruling and its basis
Imam Muhammad says the offender must pay the doctor's fee and medicine cost, because these are direct financial losses caused by the offender's act, similar to taking the victim's property.
He focuses on actual monetary expenditure.
5
Analyse the underlying principle
All three agree on the general Hanafi rule that manafi' are not compensable without a contract (ijarah) or its semblance (e.g., invalid ijarah). Abu Hanifa applies it strictly; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad find exceptions based on additional considerations (pain as a separate harm, direct financial loss).
The dispute tests the boundaries of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نزد یک ارش ساقط ہو گیا اس عیب کے زوال کی وجہ سے جو موجب ارش تھا اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ اس کہ اوپر الم (درد) کا ارش واجب ہے اور ارش وہ حکومت عدل ہے اس لئے کہ عیب اگر چہ زائل ہو گیا پس وہ درد جو حاصل ہوا تھا وہ زائل نہیں ہوا پس اس کی ( فائت بالالم ) قیمت لگانا واجب ہے۔ تشریح زید نے خالد کو سر میں کوئی زخم لگایا اور وہ بالکل اچھا ہوگیا یہاں تک کہ اس کا کوئی نشان بھی باقی نہیں رہا۔ تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اب اس کا ارش کچھ واجد سے ہوگا کیونکہ جس عیب کی وجہ سے مثل واجب ہوتا ہے وہ عیب ہی ختم ہو گیا ہے۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کا فرمان یہ ہے کہ صورت مذکورہ میں حکومت عدل واجب ہے کیونکہ اگر چہ اس کا زخم اور نشان اور عیب سب ختم ہو گیا لیکن اس تکلیف کی وجہ سے جو اس کو ہوئی تھی اور اس کی جو صحت اس سے متاثر ہوئی تھی۔ اس کا کوئی بدل نہیں ہوا۔ لہذا اس کا بدل حکومت عدل ہے۔
امام محمد کا مسلک
وقال محمد عليه اجرة الطبيب وثمن الدواء لانه انما لزمه اجرة الطبيب وثمن الدواء بفعله فصار كانه اخذ ذالك من ماله الا ان ابا حنيفة يقول ان المنافع على اصلنا لا تتقوم الا بعقد او بشبهة ولم يوجد في حق الجاني فلا يغرم شيئا
ترجمہ امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ اس پر طبیب کی اجرت اور دواء کی قیمت ہے اس لئے کہ اس کو (مضروب کو ) طبیب کی اجرت اور دواء کی قیمت ضارب کے فعل کی وجہ سے لازم ہوئی ہے پس ایسا ہو گیا گویا کہ ضارب نے یہ مضروب کے مال سے لیا ہے، مگر ابوحنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ منافع ہماری اصل پر منتقوم نہیں ہوتے مگر عقد یا شبہ عقد سے اور جانی کے حق میں ان سے کوئی نہیں پایا گیا ہے تو جانی کسی چیز کا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح یہ امام محمد کا مسلک ہے کہ صورت مذکورہ میں ضارب کے اوپر ڈاکٹر کی فیس اور دوا کی قیمت واجب ہوگی اس لئے کہ یہ سارا خسارا مضروب کو ضارب کے فعل کی وجہ سے برداشت کرنا پڑا ہے۔ تو ایسا ہو گیا گویا اتنا مال مضروب سے مضارب نے لیا ہے جس کی واپسی ضارب پر ضروری ہے۔ لیکن امام صاحب فرماتے ہیں کہ صورت مذکورہ میں الم اور درد کا حمل از قبیل منافع ہے اور منافع کچھ ان پر متقوم نہیں اور منافع کے اندر تقوم عقد اجارہ سے حاصل ہوتا ہے یا شبہ عقد سے جیسے اجارہ فاسدہ اور مضاربت فاسدہ کے اندر۔ اور یہاں نہ کوئی عقد ہے اور نہ شبہ عقد ہے لہذا ضارب اور جانی پر یہاں کچھ بھی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔
Near him (Abu Hanifa) the arsh becomes dropped due to the removal of the defect which necessitated the arsh. Abu Yusuf said that upon him (the offender) the arsh of pain is obligatory, and arsh is the just assessment, because even though the defect has disappeared, the pain that occurred has not disappeared, so its valuation (lost due to pain) is obligatory. Explanation: Zayd inflicted a wound on Khalid's head and it completely healed, leaving no trace. So according to Imam Abu Hanifa, no arsh is due because the defect that necessitated the arsh has gone. Imam Abu Yusuf says that a just assessment is due because although the wound, trace, and defect are gone, the pain he suffered and the impact on his health have not been compensated, so its compensation is a just assessment. 
The school of Imam Muhammad: Muhammad said: Upon him (the offender) is the doctor's fee and the price of the medicine, because the doctor's fee and medicine price became incumbent upon (the victim) due to his act, so it is as if he took that from his wealth. But Abu Hanifa says: On our principle, benefits (manafi') are not compensable except by contract or by something resembling a contract, and in the case of the offender these are not found, so he does not guarantee anything. Translation: Imam Muhammad said that the doctor's fee and medicine price are on him because these became due to the victim due to the offender's action, so it is as if the offender took this from the victim's property. But Abu Hanifa says that on our principle, benefits are not compensable except by a valid contract or a defective contract (like invalid hire), and here there is no contract or resemblance, so the offender does not guarantee anything. Explanation: This is Imam Muhammad's view: in this case, the offender owes the doctor's fee and medicine cost because the victim incurred this loss due to the offender's action. So it is as if the offender took this amount from the victim and must return it. But Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa) says that the pain is a benefit, and benefits are not compensable; compensation for benefits occurs only through a contract of hire or a defective contract (like invalid hire or invalid mudaraba). Since neither exists here, the offender owes no guarantee.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning compensation for a wound that heals without leaving any trace. The three positions are: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa: no arsh is due because the defect for which arsh was prescribed no longer exists. (2) Imam Abu Yusuf: a just assessment (hukumat al-adl) is obligatory because the pain suffered is a loss independent of the disappearance of the defect. (3) Imam Muhammad: the offender must cover the doctor's fee and medicine cost, as these are direct financial losses caused by his act. Abu Hanifa responds that benefits (manafi') such as pain are not compensable in Islamic law except through a contract (like hire) or a semblance of a contract (like a defective contract). Since the injury involves no contract, no compensation is due. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that manafi' are not considered property (mal) for the purposes of liability in torts without a contractual basis.

Key Terms
أرش (arsh): Fixed compensation for a specific injury or defect, assessed by the law.
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): A just assessment by experts of the value of the part lost or diminished due to injury, used when no fixed arsh is prescribed.
منافع (manafi'): Benefits or usufruct; here specifically the pain and loss of health that are non-material losses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the defect for which arsh was prescribed no longer exists.
C) Because the offender did not intend to cause harm.
D) Because the wound was not inflicted by a weapon.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a wound that heals completely may not require compensation due to the principle that manafi' (benefits like pain) are not compensable without a contract, though the Sahibayn offer exceptions.

When Does Lashing Require Compensation? The Trace Condition
Ruling on compensation for lashing causing injury

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for lashing injuries and identify the condition that determines whether arsh is due or a dispute applies.

Core Idea
Compensation for lashing injury depends on whether a visible trace remains; if no trace, the imams differ.

A person who lashes another with a whip may cause injury, or may not. When injury occurs, the remaining trace determines the obligation of compensation. This passage from Imam Muhammad presents the ruling and also highlights the well-known intra-Hanafi difference when the wound heals completely leaving no mark.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Injury
Start with the act: a person strikes another with a hundred lashes. Determine whether the strike caused a wound. If no wound, by consensus nothing is due.
Consensus: no injury, no compensation.
2
Check if a Trace Remains After Healing
If the wound heals, look for a visible trace. 'Trace' means a scar or mark that indicates the beating occurred.
Trace can be a scar, discoloration, or any lasting physical change.
3
Apply the Ruling Based on Trace
If a trace remains, the offender must pay arsh al-darb (fixed compensation for the beating). If no trace remains, the case becomes disputed among the Hanafi imams.
Arsh is predetermined for the severity and duration of the mark.
4
Recognize the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
When no trace remains: Abu Hanifa says nothing is due; Abu Yusuf says a just assessment (hukumat al-adl) is needed; Muhammad says the actual expenses (doctor's fee and medicine) are owed.
This dispute mirrors the earlier ruling on a wound that heals without leaving a mark (al-shajjah al-multahimah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن ضرب رجلا مائة سوط فجرحه فبرأ منها فعليه أرش الضرب معناه إذا بقى أثر الضرب فإذا لم يبق أثره فهو على اختلاف قد مضى في الشجة الملتحمة
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی شخص کو سو کوڑے مارے پس اس کو زخمی کر دیا پس وہ اس سے اچھا ہو گیا تو اس کے اوپر ضرب کا ارش ہے اس کے معنی یہ ہیں جب کہ ضرب کا نشان باقی رہے پس بہر حال جب کہ اس کا نشان باقی نہ رہے تو یہ اسی اختلاف پر ہے جو گزر گیا ہے بھر جانے والے زخم میں۔
تشریح زید نے عمر کو سو کوڑے مارے جس سے وہ زخمی نہیں ہوا تو بالا تفاق کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر زخمی ہو گیا تو اب دو صورتیں ہیں اچھا ہو کر نشان وغیرہ مٹ گئے یا باقی ہیں اگر باقی ہیں تو ضارب پرارش واجب ہے۔ اور اگر باقی نہ ہوں تو یہ وہی اختلافی مسئلہ ہے جیسے اس سے پہلا مسئلہ تھا یعنی امام صاحب کے نزدیک کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک حکومت عدل واجب ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ڈاکٹر کی فیس اور دوا کی قیمت واجب ہے۔
He (Muhammad) said: And whoever strikes a man a hundred lashes, causing him to become wounded, then he heals from it, then upon him is the arsh of the beating. Its meaning: when the trace of the beating remains; but if its trace does not remain, then it falls under the difference (of opinion) that has passed concerning the wound that heals completely. Translation: Muhammad said that if someone strikes a person with a hundred lashes and wounds him, then he heals, the offender owes the arsh of the beating. The meaning is when the trace of the beating remains; if no trace remains, then it is the same disputed issue as passed earlier in the wound that heals. Explanation: Zayd struck Umar with a hundred lashes without wounding him, then nothing is due by consensus. If he did wound him, there are two scenarios: the wound heals leaving no trace, or it leaves a trace. If trace remains, arsh is due. If no trace, then it is the same disputed issue as before: Imam Sahib (Abu Hanifa) says nothing, Imam Abu Yusuf says hukumat al-adl, Imam Muhammad says doctor's fee and medicine cost.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This is a ruling from Imam Muhammad regarding compensation for lashing that causes wounds. The ruling is that if the wound leaves a visible trace, the offender must pay the fixed arsh for that beating. However, if the wound heals completely without any trace, then the case is governed by the earlier dispute among the three imams: Abu Hanifa says no compensation, Abu Yusuf says a just assessment, and Muhammad says the actual expenses (doctor and medicine). The passage also notes that if the beating does not even cause a wound, there is complete agreement that nothing is owed.

Key Terms
أرش الضرب (arsh al-darb): The fixed compensation for injuries caused by beating, assessed based on the severity and remaining trace.
الشجة الملتحمة (al-shajjah al-multahimah): A head wound that heals completely leaving no scar; used as the analogous case for the dispute on trace.
حكومة عدل (hukumat al-adl): Just assessment of compensation by a qualified expert when no fixed amount is prescribed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nothing is due because the wound healed.
B) Arsh al-darb is wajib.
C) Hukumat al-adl is due.
D) Only doctor's fee is due.

Key Takeaway
Compensation for lashing injury (arsh) is only wajib if a visible trace remains after healing; otherwise, the Hanafi imams differ (nothing, hukumat, or expenses).

Diyah When a Hand is Cut and Then the Victim is Killed Before Healing
Ruling on merging both compensations into one diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that only the full diyah is due and the arsh for the hand falls, and explain the legal reasoning (talil) that the diyah for life subsumes the compensation for limbs.

Core Idea
The diyah for life includes all body parts, so a prior injury compensation merges into the full diyah.

This ruling from al-Quduri addresses a case where a person first cuts off someone's hand by mistake, then before the wound heals, kills the same person by mistake. The Hanafi school rules that only the full diyah (blood money for life) is payable; the arsh (compensation for the hand) is dropped. The reasoning is that both acts are of the same type (khata) and both obligate the same kind of compensation, which is diyah. Since diyah compensates the entire person, it already covers the limb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
There are two consecutive accidental injuries: first a hand is cut off, then before the wound heals, the same person is killed. Both acts are khata (mistake).
The key condition is that the death occurs before the hand heals.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that only the full diyah (100 camels or equivalent) is wajib; the arsh for the hand is dropped (sāqiṭ). No separate compensation is added for the hand.
This is the position of the Hanafi school, based on the text of al-Quduri.
3
Locate the legal cause (ʿilla)
The ʿilla for merging is that both injuries are of the same type (jins wāḥid) and both obligate the same wajib (diyah). Since diyah is the substitute for the entire person (badal an-nafs bi jamīʿ ajzāʾihā), it includes all body parts.
The ʿilla is that the greater compensation (diyah) subsumes the lesser (arsh) when both arise from the same category of injury.
4
Understand the talīl (reasoning)
The diyah is compensation for the whole life, so the hand is already compensated within it. It is as if the killer killed him from the beginning (ka-annahu qatalahu ibtidāʾan), meaning only one diyah is due.
This is a form of qiyās: the case of two-step injury is analogized to immediate killing.
5
Note the practical consequence
The victim's heirs receive only one diyah. The hand's arsh is not added. This avoids double compensation for the same person.
If the hand had healed before death, the arsh would be due separately because the two injuries would be independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن قطع يد رجل خطأ ثم قتله قبل البرء فعليه الدية وسقط أرش اليد لان الجناية من جنس واحد والموجب واحد وهو الدية وانها بدل النفس بجميع اجزائها فدخل الطرف النفس كانه قتله ابتداء
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کاٹ دیا خطاء کسی شخص کا ہاتھ پھر اس کو اچھا ہونے سے پہلے خطا قتل کر دیا تو اس کے اوپر دیت واجب ہے اور ہاتھ کا ارش ساقط ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ جنایت ایک جنس کی ہے اور موجب ایک ہے اور وہ دیت ہے اور دیت پورے نفس کا بدل ہے نفس کے تمام اجزاء کے ساتھ تو طرف نفس میں داخل ہو جائے گا گویا کہ اس نے ابتدا ہی سے اس کو قتل کر دیا ہے۔
تشریح زید نے عمرہ کا خطاء ہاتھ کاٹ دیا وہ ابھی اچھا نہیں ہو پایا تھا کہ پھر خطاء اس کو قتل کر دیا تو اب ہاتھ کی دیت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور نفس کی دیت یعنی سو اونٹ واجب ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ دونوں جنایت خطاء ہونے کی وجہ سے جنس واحد ہے اور دونوں کا موجب بھی ایک ہے یعنی دیت۔ اور دیت حقیقت میں بدن کے تمام اجزاء کا عوض ہے تو ہاتھ کا بھی عوض ہے۔ اس لئے ہاتھ کا عوض دوبارہ نہیں لیا جائے گا بلکہ تر اضل ہو جائے گا اور یوں شمار کیا جائے گا گویا کہ زید نے عمرہ کو ابتداء ہی سے قتل کیا ہے اور خطا قتل کی سزادیت ہے جو واجب ہوگئی ہے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: And whoever cuts off a man's hand by mistake, then kills him before healing, then upon him is the diyah, and the arsh for the hand falls. Because the injury is of one type, and the obligatory is one, which is the diyah, and it is the substitute for the life with all its parts, so the limb enters into the life, as if he killed him initially. Translation: Al-Quduri said: If someone mistakenly cuts off a person's hand, then before it heals, mistakenly kills him, then the full diyah is due, and the arsh for the hand is dropped. Explanation: Zayd mistakenly cut off Umar's hand; before it healed, he mistakenly killed him. So the hand's compensation falls, and the full diyah (100 camels) is due because both acts are of the same type (khata) and the same obligation (diyah) applies. Since diyah is the substitute for the whole body, including all parts, the hand is included in the life; it is as if he killed him from the start.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This ruling deals with consecutive injuries by mistake: first cutting a hand, then killing the same person before the hand heals. The ruling is that only the full diyah for the life is payable; the arsh for the hand is not added separately. The reasoning is that both injuries are of the same category (khata) and both demand the same type of compensation (diyah). Since diyah is compensation for the entire person, including all body parts, the hand is already covered by the diyah for the life. This is analogous to killing from the outset, where only diyah is due.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Full blood money for killing by mistake, set at 100 camels or equivalent.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for injury to a limb or body part short of death.
بدل النفس (badal an-nafs): Substitute for the life; the diyah is the price of the entire person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the arsh for the hand fall when the victim is later killed by mistake before the hand heals?
A) Because the hand healed before death.
B) Because the diyah for the life includes all body parts.
C) Because the offender paid for the hand already.
D) Because the killing was intentional.

Key Takeaway
When accidental injuries lead to death, the full diyah for life subsumes any previous limb compensation, as if the death occurred from the start.

When to Execute Qisas for Wounds: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on immediate vs delayed qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on delaying qisas for wounds, identify the Hanafi proofs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
Qisas for wounds is delayed because the outcome is uncertain – it may heal or kill.

When someone inflicts a non-fatal wound, should the perpetrator face immediate retaliation or must we wait until the victim either heals or dies? This lesson unpacks a key Hanafi ruling and its reasoning against the Shafi'i view. We'll examine the prophetic directive and the logical basis that makes the Hanafi position the relied-upon stance in the school.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the exact ruling: qisas for a wound is not executed immediately; it is postponed until the victim either recovers fully or dies from the wound.
2
State the Shafi'i Position
Recognize the opposing view: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that qisas for wounds is immediate, analogizing it to qisas for homicide.
3
Examine the Hanafi Proof
Analyze the two Hanafi proofs: (1) the hadith 'Wait in wounds' (direct Sunnah), and (2) rational reasoning: the wound's outcome is unknown and may spread (sirayah) to cause death, changing the crime's nature.
The hadith provides explicit textual authority; the rational reasoning explains why the delay is necessary.
4
Examine the Shafi'i Proof
Identify the Shafi'i proof: qiyas (analogy) to qisas for life, where the harm is certain and execution is immediate.
They argue that since the cause for qisas exists (the act of wounding), it should not be suspended.
5
Understand the Hanafi Response and Practical Difference
See how the Hanafi school refutes the analogy: in homicide, death is certain; in wounds, the ultimate outcome is unknown. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Hanafi, qisas for wounds is delayed, while under Shafi'i it is immediate.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ومن جرح رجلا جراحة لم يقتص منه حتى يبرأ وقال الشافعى يقتص منه فى الحال اعتبارا بالقصاص في النفس وهذا لان الموجب قد تحقق فلا يعطل ولنا قوله عليه السلام يستاني في الجراحات، سنة ولان الجراحات يعتبر فيها مالها لا حالها لان حكمها فى الحال غير معلوم قلعلها تسرى الى النفس فيظهر انه قتل وانما يستقر الأمر بالبرء .
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی کو زخم لگایا تو فی الحال اس سے قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا یہاں تک کہ وہ ٹھیک ہو جائے۔ اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اس سے فی الحال قصاص لیا جائے گا نفس کے قصاص پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہ اس لئے کہ موجب قصاص متحقق ہو پر چھکا
He (al-Quduri) said: And whoever wounds a man with a wound, qisas will not be taken from him until he heals. Al-Shafi'i said: Qisas will be taken from him immediately, by analogy with qisas for life. And this is because the cause for qisas is established, so it should not be suspended. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Wait in wounds' – a Sunnah. And because for wounds, what is considered is their outcome, not their current state, because their ruling at present is unknown; perhaps it may spread to the soul, so it becomes clear that it is killing, and the matter is settled only by healing.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage addresses a disagreement between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the timing of qisas (retaliatory punishment) for wounds. The Hanafi position is that qisas is not to be executed immediately upon inflicting a wound; rather, one must wait until the victim either heals or dies. This is based on two proofs: (1) The prophetic hadith commanding delay in cases of wounds. (2) Rational reasoning: the ultimate outcome of the wound is unknown—it may heal, or it may spread and cause death. If it causes death, the crime becomes murder, not mere wounding, and the penalty changes to qisas for life or diyah. Therefore, immediate qisas could be unjust if the wound escalates. The Shafi'i view analogizes wounds to intentional killing, where qisas is immediate, but the Hanafi response is that the cause for qisas in wounds is not fully established until the outcome is known.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retributive punishment: life for life, limb for limb.
سراية (sirayah): The spreading of a wound to the soul (i.e., causing death).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why must qisas for a wound be delayed until healing or death?
A) Because the wound may spread and cause death, changing the nature of the crime.
B) Because the offender might repent.
C) Because the victim might forgive.
D) Because the court is busy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school delays qisas for wounds due to the uncertainty of the outcome, supported by a direct hadith and rational reasoning.

Ruling on Lashing Causing Injury and Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for lashing injury.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) on compensation for lashing where injury heals without a mark, and explain the practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
When lashing injury heals without a trace, the Hanafi school is divided on whether any compensation is due.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning compensation (arsh) for lashing that causes an injury which later heals without any permanent mark. The text first establishes the rule when the mark remains, then explains three distinct positions of the founding imams when the mark disappears. Understanding this dispute deepens your appreciation of how the Hanafi masters derived rulings from principles of injury compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between lashing that leaves a mark and lashing where injury heals without a mark. First, determine the ruling when the mark remains.
2
Understand the consensus scenario
If the lashing causes no injury at all, nothing is due by agreement. Then focus on the disputed case.
3
State the position of Imam Abu Hanifa
He holds that nothing is due when the mark disappears, likely because compensation is tied to visible harm.
4
State the position of Imam Abu Yusuf
He requires an equitable assessment (hukumat adl) by a judge.
5
State the position of Imam Muhammad
He requires reimbursement of actual expenses (doctor's fee and medicine cost).
6
Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects how much the striker must pay: nothing, a judge-determined amount, or actual costs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی شخص کو سو کوڑے مارے پس اس کو زخمی کر دیا پس وہ اس سے اچھا ہو گیا تو اس کے اوپر ضرب کا ارش ہے اس کے معنی یہ ہیں جب کہ ضرب کا نشان باقی رہے پس بہر حال جب کہ اس کا نشان باقی نہ رہے تو یہ اسی اختلاف پر ہے جو گزر گیا ہے بھر جانے والے زخم میں۔
تشریح زید نے عمر کو سو کوڑے مارے جس سے وہ زخمی نہیں ہوا تو بالا تفاق کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔
اور اگر زخمی ہو گیا تو اب دو صورتیں ہیں اچھا ہو کر نشان وغیرہ مٹ گئے یا باقی ہیں اگر باقی ہیں تو ضارب پرارش واجب ہے۔ اور اگر باقی نہ ہوں تو یہ وہی اختلافی مسئلہ ہے جیسے اس سے پہلا مسئلہ تھا یعنی امام صاحب کے نزدیک کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا ۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک حکومت عدل واجب ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک ڈاکٹر کی فیس اور دوا کی قیمت واجب ہے۔
Translation of Matn: Muhammad said: And whoever lashes a person one hundred lashes and injures him, then he recovers, then upon him is the 'arsh of lashing, meaning when the mark of the lashing remains. In any case, when no mark remains, it follows the same difference of opinion that has passed regarding a wound that heals. Commentary: Zayd lashes 'Amr one hundred lashes but he was not injured, then by consensus nothing is due. And if injured, then two scenarios: either he recovers and the mark disappears, or the mark remains. If it remains, the 'arsh of lashing is due on the striker. If it does not remain, it is the same disputed issue as the previous one, meaning in the view of Imam Abu Hanifa nothing is due; in the view of Imam Abu Yusuf, an equitable assessment (hukumat adl) is due; and in the view of Imam Muhammad, the doctor's fee and medicine cost are due.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (dispute) regarding compensation for lashing that causes injury which later heals without a trace. The text first states the ruling from Muhammad al-Shaybani's transmission: if the mark of the lashing remains, the fixed compensation ('arsh) for lashing is due. If the mark disappears entirely, the ruling follows the previously mentioned difference of opinion concerning a wound that heals completely. The commentary then clarifies: if no injury occurred at all, there is consensus that nothing is due. If injury occurred, two cases arise: (1) if the mark remains, 'arsh is due; (2) if the mark disappears, the three leading Hanafi imams differ. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that nothing is due. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that an equitable government assessment (hukumat adl) is due. Imam Muhammad holds that the actual expenses—doctor's fee and medicine cost—are due. The text does not specify which view is preferred, but in later Hanafi practice, Imam Abu Hanifa's view is generally relied upon in such cases.

Key Terms
ارش (arsh): Fixed monetary compensation for injury to a body part or for lashing where the mark remains.
حکومت عدل (hukumat adl): An equitable assessment of compensation by a qualified judge when no fixed 'arsh is prescribed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All Hanafi imams agree that 'arsh is due.
B) Imam Abu Hanifa says nothing is due; Imam Abu Yusuf says hukumat adl; Imam Muhammad says doctor's fee and medicine cost.
C) Imam Abu Hanifa says doctor's fee is due; Imam Abu Yusuf says nothing; Imam Muhammad says hukumat adl.
D) The 'arsh for lashing is due by consensus.

Key Takeaway
When lashing injury heals without a trace, the Hanafi school is divided: Abu Hanifa says nothing, Abu Yusuf says equitable assessment, Muhammad says actual expenses.

When a Limb Injury is Subsumed by Death: The Rule of Overlapping Diyat
States that diya for accidental killing includes 'arsh of hand if killed before healing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when an accidental injury is followed by accidental death before healing, and explain why the arsh for the limb is dropped.

Core Idea
If an accidental injury leads to death before healing, full diya subsumes separate limb compensation.

This passage from Quduri addresses a specific scenario: two separate accidental acts—cutting a hand and then killing—but because the victim dies before the hand heals, the law treats them as one unified accident. The reasoning is rooted in the nature of diya as compensation for the entire person. Understanding this rule prevents double compensation and clarifies the Hanafi approach to overlapping injuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and their individual rulings
First, note that cutting a hand accidentally (khata') requires 'arsh (fixed compensation for the hand). Killing accidentally requires full diya. Normally, both would be due separately.
2
Note the timing condition
The ruling applies only if death occurs before the hand heals. If the hand healed first, then separate payments would be due.
The condition is explicitly mentioned: 'before it heals'.
3
Understand the talil (legal reasoning)
Both acts are of the same type (khata') and both obligate diya (for life). Diya is compensation for the entire self with all its parts. Therefore, the limb's compensation is already included in the life diya.
The reasoning uses the principle that diya replaces the whole person.
4
Apply the ruling
Thus, only one full diya (100 camels) is due. The 'arsh for the hand is dropped, as if the killing had occurred from the start and the cutting was part of the same incident.
This avoids double payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خطاء ہاتھ کاٹا پھر ٹھیک ہونے سے پہلے قتل کر دیا اس پر دیت ہے ہاتھ کا تاوان ساقط ہے
قال ومن قطع يد رجل خطا ثم قتله قبل البرء فعليه الدية وسقط ارش اليد لان الجناية من جنس واحد والموجب واحد وهو الدية وانها بدل النفس بجميع اجزائها فدخل الطرف النفس كانه قتله ابتداء
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کاٹ دیا خطاء کسی شخص کا ہاتھ پھر اس کو اچھا ہونے سے پہلے خطا قتل کر دیا تو اس کے اوپر دیت واجب ہے اور ہاتھ کا ارش ساقط ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ جنایت ایک جنس کی ہے اور موجب ایک ہے اور وہ دیت ہے اور دیت پورے نفس کا بدل ہے نفس کے تمام اجزاء کے ساتھ تو طرف نفس میں داخل ہو جائے گا گویا کہ اس نے ابتدا ہی سے اس کو قتل کر دیا ہے۔
تشریح زید نے عمرہ کا خطاء ہاتھ کاٹ دیا وہ ابھی اچھا نہیں ہو پایا تھا کہ پھر خطاء اس کو قتل کر دیا تو اب ہاتھ کی دیت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور نفس کی دیت یعنی سو اونٹ واجب ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ دونوں جنایت خطاء ہونے کی وجہ سے جنس واحد ہے اور دونوں کا موجب بھی ایک ہے یعنی دیت۔ اور دیت حقیقت میں بدن کے تمام اجزاء کا عوض ہے تو ہاتھ کا بھی عوض ہے۔ اس لئے ہاتھ کا عوض دوبارہ نہیں لیا جائے گا بلکہ تر اضل ہو جائے گا اور یوں شمار کیا جائے گا گویا کہ زید نے عمرہ کو ابتداء ہی سے قتل کیا ہے اور خطا قتل کی سزادیت ہے جو واجب ہوگئی ہے۔
Heading: Accidental cutting of hand then killing before healing: upon him is diya, compensation for hand is waived. Matn: And whoever cuts off a man's hand by mistake, then kills him before it heals, then upon him is the diya, and the 'arsh of the hand falls, because the injury is of one type and the obligation is one, which is diya, and it is the compensation for the entire self with all its parts, so the limb is included in the self, as if he killed him from the beginning. Translation of Quduri: And whoever accidentally cuts off a person's hand, then accidentally kills him before it heals, then upon him is the diya (full blood money) and the 'arsh of the hand is dropped, because the two crimes are of one type and the obligation is one, which is diya; and diya is compensation for the entire self with all its parts, so the limb enters into the self, as if he killed him initially. Commentary: Zayd accidentally cuts off 'Amr's hand, and before it heals, he accidentally kills him. Then the diya of the hand is dropped and the diya for the life (one hundred camels) becomes wajib. Because both crimes are accidental, they are of the same type, and both are obliged by one thing: diya. Diya is in reality compensation for all parts of the body, so it includes the hand. Therefore, compensation for the hand is not taken twice; rather it is subsumed, and it is as if Zayd killed 'Amr from the beginning, and the punishment for accidental killing is diya which has become wajib.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling from the matn of Quduri and its commentary regarding a combined accidental injury and homicide. The case: Zayd accidentally cuts off 'Amr's hand. Before the wound heals, Zayd accidentally kills 'Amr. The ruling is that only the full diya for the life (one hundred camels or equivalent) is due; the separate fixed compensation ('arsh) for the hand is waived. The reasoning is that both acts are accidental (khata') and thus are of the same legal category. The obligation arising from both is one: diya (blood money). Since diya is the compensation for the entire person, including all body parts, the compensation for the hand is already included within the diya for the life. Therefore, it would be double compensation to pay both. Legally, it is treated as if the killing occurred initially and the cutting was part of the same incident. The commentary illustrates with names and explains that the hand's compensation is subsumed (تر اضل) into the life diya.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Monetary compensation paid for accidental killing or injury, specifically the full blood money for the life (100 camels) in this context.
ارش (arsh): Fixed compensation for injury to a body part; here specifically for the hand.
خطاء (khata'): Accidental; refers to unintentional killing or injury without intent or negligence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only the 'arsh for the hand.
B) Full diya for life plus 'arsh for the hand.
C) Full diya for life only; no separate payment for the hand.
D) Nothing, because both were accidental.

Key Takeaway
When accidental injury is followed by accidental death before healing, only full diya is due; limb compensation is subsumed.

Delaying Qisas for Wounds: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi argues qisas for wounds must wait until healing; Shafi'i says immediate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on delaying qisas for wounds and explain the proof from hadith and reasoning.

Core Idea
Qisas for wounds must wait until healing because the wound's final outcome is unknown — it may turn into murder.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is on whether retaliation for a wound can be inflicted immediately or must be delayed. The Hanafi school, relying on a prophetic hadith and the uncertainty of the wound's outcome, requires waiting until the victim heals or a year passes. The Shafi'i school, using qiyas on murder, argues for immediate qisas. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hadith can override analogy in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and both positions
Read the matn to find the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings. Note that the Hanafi ruling is stated before the objection, and the objection is followed by the Hanafi proof.
The matn says: 'He does not take qisas until he heals.' Then 'al-Shafi'i said: he takes qisas immediately.'
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Identify that al-Shafi'i uses qiyas on qisas for murder. The cause (wujub) is present, so the ruling should be immediate.
Qiyas: murder is immediate in qisas, so wounds should be too.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Note two proofs: (1) The hadith 'yustana fi al-jarahat sanah' commands a delay. (2) Rational argument: the wound's final outcome (mal) is uncertain; it may kill, changing the crime.
The hadith is a specific dalil naqli; the rational argument is istidlal.
4
Determine the practical consequence
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: Under Hanafi, the perpetrator is not punished until the wound heals or a year passes; under Shafi'i, punishment is immediate.
This affects the timing of legal action and the nature of the charge.

قال ومن جرح رجلا جراحة لم يقتص منه حتى يبرأ وقال الشافعى يقتص منه فى الحال اعتبارا بالقصاص في النفس وهذا لان الموجب قد تحقق فلا يعطل ولنا قوله عليه السلام يستاني في الجراحات، سنة ولان الجراحات يعتبر فيها مالها لا حالها لان حكمها فى الحال غير معلوم قلعلها تسرى الى النفس فيظهر انه قتل وانما يستقر الأمر بالبرء .
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جس نے کسی کو زخم لگایا تو فی الحال اس سے قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا یہاں تک کہ وہ ٹھیک ہو جائے ۔ اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اس سے فی الحال قصاص لیا جائے گا نفس کے قصاص پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہ اس لئے کہ موجب قصاص متحقق ہو پر چھکا ہے تو موجب کو معطل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور ہماری دلیل نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے کہ جراحات میں ایک سال کی مہلت دی جائے گی ۔ اور اس لئے کہ جراجات میں ان کا مال معتبر ہے ان کا حال (موجودہ) معتبر نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ فی الحال جراحات کا حکم معلوم نہیں ہے پس شاید کہ جراحات نفس کی طرف سرایت کر جائیں تو یہ بات ظاہر ہو جائے گی کہ یقتل ہے اور بات پختہ ہوگی اچھا ہونے سے۔
تشریح جب کسی شخص کو کوئی زخم لگا دیا گیا تو ہوسکتا ہے کہ وہ اچھا ہو جائے اور ہوسکتا ہے کہ نوبت موت تک پہنچ جائے اس لئے فی الحال قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا بلکہ جب وہ اچھا ہو جائے تب قصاص لیا جائے گا۔ یہ ہمارا مسلک ہے اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ قصاص فی الفور لیا جائے گا کیونکہ اگر کوئی کسی شخص کو قتل کرتا ہے تو وہاں بھی قصاص فی الفور کیا جاتا ہے، لہذا یہاں بھی فی الحال قصاص واجب ہوگا۔
اور اس لئے بھی کہ موجب قصاص جب موجود ہے تو پھر اس کو معطل قرار دینے کے کیا معنی؟
ہماری دلیل ایک تو یہ حدیث ہے کہ زخموں میں ایک سال کی مہلت دی جائے گی اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ زخم کا حال ابھی معلوم نہ ہو سکا کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ وہ سرایت کر کے قتل تک پہنچ جائے تو جراحات میں حال کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مال کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اچھا ہونے تک انتظار کیا جائے تا کہ بات پیٹنٹ طریقہ پر مسلح ہو کر سامنے آجائے۔
Matn: And whoever wounds a man with a wound, qisas is not taken from him until he heals. Al-Shafi'i said: qisas is taken from him immediately, by analogy with qisas for the life. This is because the obligation has been established, so it should not be suspended. Our proof is the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'One should wait for a year in wounds.' And because in wounds, what matters is their ultimate outcome (mal), not their current state (hal), because the ruling at the moment is unknown; perhaps the wound will spread to the soul, making it apparent that it is killing. The matter becomes settled upon healing. Translation: Quduri said: And whoever wounds someone, qisas is not taken from him immediately until he heals. Al-Shafi'i said: qisas is taken from him immediately, by analogy with qisas for the life, and because the cause of qisas is established, so it should not be suspended. Our proof: the Prophet's command that in wounds a delay of one year is given. And also because in wounds, their final outcome (mal) is considered, not their current state, because the ruling at the moment is unknown; perhaps the wound will spread to the soul, then it becomes clear that it is killing, and the matter becomes settled upon healing. Commentary: When a person receives a wound, it may heal or may lead to death. Therefore, qisas is not taken immediately, but after healing. This is our (Hanafi) position. Imam al-Shafi'i says qisas must be taken immediately, because if someone kills, qisas is immediate, so here also qisas is immediate. And also because the cause of qisas is present, so why should it be suspended? Our proof is the hadith that in wounds a one-year delay is given, and also because the state of the wound is unknown; it might spread and cause death, so the current state is not considered, but the final outcome is. Therefore, we wait until healing so that the matter becomes clear and settled.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage presents a classical inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and the Shafi'is regarding the timing of qisas (retaliation) for wounds. The matn of Quduri states the Hanafi position: qisas for a wound cannot be executed immediately; it must be delayed until the victim heals. Imam al-Shafi'i argues for immediate qisas, analogizing it to qisas for murder, where the obligation is immediate once proven, and suspending the cause would be unreasonable. The Hanafi proof is twofold: first, a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that commands a one-year waiting period for wounds (indicating that delays are prescribed). Second, a rational argument: the final outcome of the wound (whether it heals or becomes fatal) is legally decisive, not its current state. If the wound kills, it becomes murder and qisas for life is due; if it heals, only qisas for the wound. Since the outcome is unknown at the time of the wound, qisas must wait. The commentary clarifies that the Hanafi school follows this view, while the Shafi'i school follows immediate qisas. The practical result: in Hanafi law, a person who wounds another cannot be punished until the victim is declared healed or the waiting period ends.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation or retributive punishment for bodily harm, equivalent to the injury inflicted.
جراحت (jarahat): A wound or injury that does not reach the level of killing immediately.
برء (bur'): Healing or full recovery from the wound, after which the final ruling on qisas is determined.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the Hanafi ruling on the timing of qisas for a wound is:
A) Immediate.
B) Delayed until the victim fully heals.
C) Delayed for a maximum of one year.
D) Delayed until the victim heals, up to one year.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires delay in qisas for wounds due to uncertainty of the outcome, supported by a prophetic hadith.

Diya for Intentional Killing with Doubt and by Settlement
States diya for intentional killing with doubt and by settlement are on killer's property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that diya for intentional killing with doubt and compensation by settlement are on the killer's property, and distinguish the payment periods of three years vs. immediate.

Core Idea
When qisas falls due to doubt or is replaced by settlement, the diya is on the killer's property, not the 'aqila.

In Hanafi diyat law, the general principle is that the 'aqila (tribe) bears the blood money for accidental killing. But what happens when the killing is intentional but qisas is dropped due to a doubt (shubha), or when the victim's family settles for a compensation? This passage, from Quduri's matn and its commentary, clarifies that in both scenarios, the financial burden falls squarely on the killer himself, not his tribe. The proof is a prophetic hadith, and the two cases differ only in the payment schedule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Find where the passage discusses: (1) intentional killing where qisas is dropped due to shubha, and (2) any 'arsh (compensation) that becomes obligatory through sulh (settlement). These are the two cases where diya is on the killer's property.
Example: father killing son is a classic shubha.
2
State the common rule
For both scenarios, the diya is in the wealth of the killer (fī māl al-qātil). Not on the 'aqila.
This is the core ruling.
3
Cite the hadith proof
The matn cites: لاتعقل العواقل عمدا ('The 'aqila do not bear intentional killing'). Understand how this serves as evidence that the killer alone is responsible.
The hadith is a proof from Sunnah.
4
Distinguish the payment terms
The first case (diya due to killing with shubha) is payable in three years, like shibh al-'amd. The second (sulh compensation) is payable immediately, like a price in a sale.
Why? The first is based on the killing act; the second is based on a contract.
5
Understand the rationale
The commentary explains that the diya from killing resembles shibh al-'amd (which is also paid over three years), while the sulh payment resembles a contractual debt, due at once.
This analogy (tashbīh) is key to the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قتل عمد میں شبہ سے قصاص ساقط ہے اور دیت قاتل کے مال میں ہے اور ہر وہ ارش جو صلح سے واجب ہو وہ قاتل کے مال میں ہے
قال وكل عمد سقط القصاص فيه بشبهة فالدية في مال القاتل وكل ارش وجب بالصلح فهو في مال القاتل لقوله عليه السلام لاتعقل العواقل عمدا الحديث وهذا عمد غير ان الاول يجب في ثلث سنين لانه مال وجب بالقتل ابتداء فاشبه شبه العمد والثاني يجب حالا لانه مال وجب بالعقد فاشبه الثمن في البيع
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور ہر قتل عمد جس میں شبہ کی وجہ سے قصاص ساقط ہو جائے تو دیت قاتل کے مال میں ہوگی اور ہر وہ ارش جو صلح کی وجہ سے واجب ہو تو وہ قاتل کے مال میں ہے نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ عواقل عمد کا محل نہیں کرتے (الحدیث) اور یہ عمد ہے علاوہ اس بات کے کہ اول تین سال میں واجب ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ایسا مال ہے جو ابتداء قتل کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہے تو یہ شبہ عمد کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور ثانی فی الحال واجب ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہ ایسا مال ہے جو عقد کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہے تو یہ بیع میں شمن کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔
تشریح یہاں سے ایک اصول پیش فرماتے ہیں کہ جہاں قتل عمد میں کسی شبہ کی وجہ سے قصاص ساقط ہو جائے اور دیت واجب ہو جیسے اگر باپ نے بیٹے کو قتل کر دیا ہوتو ایسی دیت قاتل کے مال میں واجب ہوگی عاقلہ پر نہ ہوگی اور ہر مال جر مانہ جو عمد کی صورت میں بر بناء مصالحت واجب ہوا ہے وہ بھی قاتل کے مال میں واجب ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ حدیث میں وارد ہے کہ عاقلہ عمد کا ذمہ دار نہیں ہے اور یہ عمدہی ہے البتہ ان دونوں باتوں میں فرق یہ ہے کہ اول قسطوار تین سالوں میں واجب ہوگا اور مال صلح فی الحال ہوگا۔
Heading: In intentional killing, if qisas is dropped due to doubt, the diya is in the property of the killer. And every 'arsh that becomes obligatory by settlement is in the property of the killer. Matn: And every intentional killing in which qisas falls due to doubt, then the diya is in the wealth of the killer. And every 'arsh that becomes obligatory by settlement, it is in the wealth of the killer. Because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'The 'aqila do not bear intentional killing' (hadith). This is intentional, except that the first (diya due to killing) is obligatory in three years, because it is wealth that became obligatory due to killing from the beginning, so it resembles shibh al-'amd (semi-intentional killing). And the second (compensation by settlement) is obligatory immediately, because it is wealth that became obligatory by contract, so it resembles the price in a sale. Translation by Quduri: And every intentional killing in which qisas is dropped due to doubt, then the diya is in the wealth of the killer. And every 'arsh that becomes obligatory by settlement is in the wealth of the killer, because of the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'The 'aqila do not bear intentional killing' (hadith). This is intentional, except that the first is obligatory in three years, because it is wealth that became obligatory due to the initial killing, so it resembles shibh al-'amd. And the second is obligatory immediately, because it is wealth that became obligatory by contract, so it resembles the price in a sale. Commentary: From here an principle is presented: Where intentional killing has qisas dropped due to doubt (e.g., a father killing his son), the diya is wajib on the killer's property, not on the 'aqila. And every compensation money that becomes wajib in a case of intentional killing based on settlement (sulh) is also wajib on the killer's property. This is because the hadith states that the 'aqila are not responsible for intentional killing, and this is intentional. However, there is a difference: the first (diya due to killing) is payable in installments over three years; the settlement payment is immediately payable.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage discusses a key principle in Hanafi diyat law: when intentional killing (qatl 'amd) occurs in circumstances where qisas (retaliation) is not applicable due to a doubt (shubha) — for example, a father killing his son — then the diya (blood money) is paid from the killer's own wealth, not by his 'aqila (family/ tribe). Similarly, if the case is settled by agreement (sulh), the compensation ('arsh) is also on the killer's wealth. The proof is a hadith: 'The 'aqila do not bear intentional killing.' However, there is a difference in the manner of payment. The diya that becomes due by the killing itself (due to shubha) is payable over three years, because it resembles shibh al-'amd (semi-intentional killing), where the diya is also on the killer in installments. The compensation agreed by settlement (sulh) is payable immediately because it arises from a contract (sulh), and thus resembles the price in a sale, which is due immediately. The commentary illustrates with the example of a father killing his son: qisas is waived due to doubt, so diya is wajib on the father's property, not on the 'aqila.

Key Terms
شبہ (shubha): A doubt that prevents the implementation of hadd or qisas, e.g., in a father killing his son.
عاقلہ ('aqila): The group (usually extended family or tribe) that bears the diya in cases of accidental killing.
صلح (sulh): Amicable settlement between parties, replacing qisas or diya with an agreed compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A father accidentally kills his son (qatl amd with shubha). According to the passage, who must pay the diya?
A) The father's 'aqila (tribe).
B) The father himself from his own property.
C) The state treasury (bayt al-mal).
D) No diya is due because it was intentional.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, diya for intentional killing with doubt and compensation by settlement are both the responsibility of the killer, not his 'aqila.
