Delay in Qisas for Wounds: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute over immediate vs delayed qisas for wounds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school delays qisas for wounds and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A wound's outcome is uncertain; qisas is delayed until recovery or death—this protects against mistaken execution.

When someone inflicts a wound, should the retributive punishment (qisas) be applied immediately or after waiting? This question reveals a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi school, guided by an explicit hadith and the principle of uncertainty, requires a one-year respite. Imam al-Shafi'i argues by analogy to murder that qisas should be immediate. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to handle textual evidence vs. analogical reasoning in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: qisas for wounds is postponed for one year to observe whether the wound heals or leads to death.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that qisas should be executed immediately, just as in cases of intentional killing.
The Shafi'i view relies on qiyas (analogy).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i dalil: the cause (sabab) of qisas exists (the wound), so it should not be invalidated by delay. Analogy to murder where qisas is immediate.
Understand the structure of their analogy.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school refutes the analogy by pointing to an explicit hadith that commands a one-year respite, and by noting the uncertainty of the wound's outcome. The analogy fails because murder is certain, wounds are not.
The hadith is a specific text (takhsis) that overrides the general qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, qisas may be replaced by diyah if death occurs; under Shafi'i, qisas is executed immediately regardless of future outcome.
This shows how a seemingly minor usul difference has major fiqh consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہے تو موجب کو معطل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور ہماری دلیل نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے کہ جراحات میں ایک سال کی مہلت دی جائے گی ۔ اور اس لئے کہ جراجات میں ان کا مال معتبر ہے ان کا حال (موجودہ) معتبر نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ فی الحال جراحات کا حکم معلوم نہیں ہے پس شاید کہ جراحات نفس کی طرف سرایت کر جائیں تو یہ بات ظاہر ہو جائے گی کہ یقتل ہے اور بات پختہ ہوگی اچھا ہونے سے۔ تشریح جب کسی شخص کو کوئی زخم لگا دیا گیا تو ہوسکتا ہے کہ وہ اچھا ہو جائے اور ہوسکتا ہے کہ نوبت موت تک پہنچ جائے اس لئے فی الحال قصاص نہیں لیا جائے گا بلکہ جب وہ اچھا ہو جائے تب قصاص لیا جائے گا۔ یہ ہمارا مسلک ہے اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ قصاص فی الفور لیا جائے گا کیونکہ اگر کوئی کسی شخص کو قتل کرتا ہے تو وہاں بھی قصاص فی الفور کیا جاتا ہے، لہذا یہاں بھی فی الحال قصاص واجب ہوگا۔ اور اس لئے بھی کہ موجب قصاص جب موجود ہے تو پھر اس کو معطل قرار دینے کے کیا معنی؟ ہماری دلیل ایک تو یہ حدیث ہے کہ زخموں میں ایک سال کی مہلت دی جائے گی اور دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ زخم کا حال ابھی معلوم نہ ہو سکا کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ وہ سرایت کر کے قتل تک پہنچ جائے تو جراحات میں حال کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا بلکہ مال کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اچھا ہونے تک انتظار کیا جائے تا کہ بات پیٹنٹ طریقہ پر مسلح ہو کر سامنے آجائے۔
It will not be held that the cause [of qisas] is invalidated. And our proof is the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'In wounds, a respite of one year will be given.' And because in wounds, their [the victim's] wealth is considered, not their current condition, because the ruling on wounds is not known immediately. So perhaps the wounds will spread to the soul, then it will become apparent that it is death, and the matter will be settled upon recovery. Explanation: When a person is inflicted with a wound, it may heal or it may lead to death. Therefore, qisas is not taken immediately, but when he recovers, then qisas will be taken. This is our school. Imam al-Shafi'i says that qisas will be taken immediately, because if someone kills a person, qisas is done immediately, so here too qisas becomes obligatory immediately. And because when the cause of qisas exists, what meaning is there in declaring it invalid? Our proof is the hadith that in wounds, a respite of one year will be given. The second proof is that the condition of the wound is not yet known, because it may spread to death. So in wounds, the current state is not considered, rather wealth is considered. Therefore, one waits until recovery so that the matter becomes settled and clear.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage addresses the dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the timing of qisas for wounds. The Hanafi position, which is the relied-upon view, is that qisas is not executed immediately upon infliction of a wound. Instead, the victim must be given a full year's respite to observe whether the wound heals or leads to death. The reasoning is that the ultimate outcome is uncertain; if the wound proves fatal, the offense becomes murder, which carries a different ruling. The Hanafi proof is a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ commanding a one-year wait for wounds. Additionally, the focus is on the potential monetary compensation (diyah) if death occurs, not on the immediate state. Imam al-Shafi'i argues for immediate qisas by analogy to intentional killing, where qisas is immediate. The Hanafi response refutes this by highlighting the uncertainty inherent in wounds, which distinguishes them from clear-cut murder. The passage is a standard inter-madhhab dispute resolved through textual proof and rational analysis.

Key Terms
جراح (jirah): wound or injury
قصاص (qisas): retributive punishment, specifically for wounds or killing
دیت (diyah): blood money paid for homicide or injury

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when should qisas for a wound be executed?
A) Immediately after the wound is inflicted
B) After a one-year respite to observe the outcome
C) Only if the wound results in death
D) At the discretion of the judge

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school delays qisas for wounds for one year due to uncertainty and an explicit hadith, distinguishing it from immediate qisas for murder.

Diyah in Intentional Killing with Shubha: Payment Modalities
Ruling on diyah with shubha and sulh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah when qisas is dropped due to shubha and distinguish between payment in three annual installments (direct diyah) and immediate payment (sulh-based arsh).

Core Idea
Intentional killing with shubha: diyah on the killer, paid in three years; but if by sulh, immediate.

This lesson examines a nuanced fiqh ruling from al-Quduri's matn: when a person commits intentional killing but qisas is dropped due to a legal doubt (shubha), diyah becomes obligatory. However, the manner of payment depends on the source of the obligation. If the diyah is imposed directly by the killing (e.g., father killing son), it is spread over three years. If the compensation is agreed upon through reconciliation (sulh), it is due immediately. We will explore the textual proof and the analogical reasoning behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the general principle: in every intentional killing where qisas is dropped due to shubha, diyah is wajib on the killer's wealth, not on his 'aqila.
Note the exception: 'aqila are never liable for intentional acts.
2
Locate the textual proof
Recognize the hadith cited: 'La ta'qilu al-'awaqilu 'amdan' (The 'aqila do not bear responsibility for intentional acts). Understand that this negates 'aqila liability and places the burden on the killer.
3
Distinguish the two subcases
Differentiate between diyah directly from killing (first type) and arsh by sulh (second type). Note the difference in payment timeline: first type in three years, second type immediately.
4
Trace the analogical reasoning
Understand why each subcase follows its payment schedule. The first type is analogized to diyah for shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional killing) because both arise from the act of killing without a contract. The second type is analogized to a sale price because it arises from a contract (sulh).
This is a classic Hanafi qiyas applied to payment modality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قتل عمد میں شبہ سے قصاص ساقط ہے اور دیت قاتل کے مال میں ہے اور ہر وہ ارش جو صلح سے واجب ہو وہ قاتل کے مال میں ہے قال وكل عمد سقط القصاص فيه بشبهة فالدية في مال القاتل وكل ارش وجب بالصلح فهو في مال القاتل لقوله عليه السلام لاتعقل العواقل عمدا الحديث وهذا عمد غير ان الاول يجب في ثلث سنين لانه مال وجب بالقتل ابتداء فاشبه شبه العمد والثاني يجب حالا لانه مال وجب بالعقد فاشبه الثمن في البيع ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور ہر قتل عمد جس میں شبہ کی وجہ سے قصاص ساقط ہو جائے تو دیت قاتل کے مال میں ہوگی اور ہر وہ ارش جو صلح کی وجہ سے واجب ہو تو وہ قاتل کے مال میں ہے نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ عواقل عمد کا محل نہیں کرتے (الحدیث) اور یہ عمد ہے علاوہ اس بات کے کہ اول تین سال میں واجب ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ایسا مال ہے جو ابتداء قتل کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہے تو یہ شبہ عمد کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور ثانی فی الحال واجب ہو گا اس لئے کہ یہ ایسا مال ہے جو عقد کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہے تو یہ بیع میں شمن کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ تشریح یہاں سے ایک اصول پیش فرماتے ہیں کہ جہاں قتل عمد میں کسی شبہ کی وجہ سے قصاص ساقط ہو جائے اور دیت واجب ہو جیسے اگر باپ نے بیٹے کو قتل کر دیا ہوتو ایسی دیت قاتل کے مال میں واجب ہوگی عاقلہ پر نہ ہوگی اور ہر مال جر مانہ جو عمد کی صورت میں بر بناء مصالحت واجب ہوا ہے وہ بھی قاتل کے مال میں واجب ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ حدیث میں وارد ہے کہ عاقلہ عمد کا ذمہ دار نہیں ہے اور یہ عمدہی ہے البتہ ان دونوں باتوں میں فرق یہ ہے کہ اول قسطوار تین سالوں میں واجب ہوگا اور مال صلح فی الحال ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اصول یہ مقرر ہے کہ جو مال شروع ہی سے یعنی بغیر مصالحت کے قتل کی وجہ سے واجب ہوگا تو وہ قتل شبہ عمد کے مشابہ ہو گا تو جیسے شبہ عمد میں مال قسطوار واجب ہوتا ہے ایسے ہی اس میں بھی منتطوار واجب ہوگا۔ اور جو مال کسی عقد و معاہدہ کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہو تو وہ فی الحال واجب ہوگا جیسے بیچ میں شمن فی الحال واجب ہوتا ہے۔
In intentional killing, qisas is dropped due to doubt, and diyah is in the wealth of the killer. And every compensation (arsh) that becomes obligatory by reconciliation is in the wealth of the killer. He (al-Quduri) said: And every intentional killing in which qisas is dropped due to a doubt, the diyah is in the wealth of the killer. And every compensation that becomes obligatory by reconciliation is in the wealth of the killer, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'The 'aqila do not bear responsibility for intentional acts' — the hadith. And this is intentional, except that the first is obligatory in three years because it is wealth that became obligatory by killing initially, so it resembles quasi-intentional killing. The second is obligatory immediately because it is wealth that became obligatory by contract, so it resembles the price in a sale. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And every intentional killing in which qisas is dropped due to a doubt, the diyah is in the wealth of the killer. And every compensation that becomes obligatory by reconciliation is in the wealth of the killer, due to the command of the Prophet, peace be upon him, that the 'aqila do not bear responsibility for intentional acts (hadith). And this is intentional, except that the first is obligatory in three years because it is wealth that became obligatory by killing initially, so it resembles quasi-intentional killing. The second is obligatory immediately because it is wealth that became obligatory by contract, so it resembles the price in a sale. Explanation: Here he presents a principle: where in intentional killing qisas is dropped due to some doubt and diyah becomes obligatory, like if a father kills his son, such diyah is obligatory on the wealth of the killer, not on the 'aqila. And every monetary compensation that becomes obligatory in a case of intentional killing by way of reconciliation is also obligatory on the killer's wealth. Because it is narrated in the hadith that the 'aqila are not responsible for intentional acts, and this is intentional. However, the difference between these two is that the first is obligatory in installments over three years, and the wealth of reconciliation is immediate. Because the established principle is that wealth that becomes obligatory from the beginning, i.e., without reconciliation, due to killing, then it resembles quasi-intentional killing. So just as in quasi-intentional killing wealth is obligatory in installments, similarly here it is also obligatory in installments. And wealth that becomes obligatory due to a contract or agreement becomes obligatory immediately, just as in sale the price is obligatory immediately.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational principle from Quduri's matn regarding diyah in cases where qisas is dropped due to shubha (doubt). The key ruling is that in any intentional killing where shubha prevents qisas (e.g., a father killing his son, or a Muslim killing a dhimmi), the diyah is payable from the killer's own wealth, not from his 'aqila. The proof is the hadith 'the 'aqila do not bear responsibility for intentional acts.' The text further distinguishes two subcases: (1) diyah imposed directly due to the killing (without reconciliation) is paid in three annual installments, by analogy to diyah for shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional killing); (2) compensation agreed upon through sulh (reconciliation) is paid immediately, like a sale price, because it arises from a contract. This distinction highlights the Hanafi method of analogical reasoning (qiyas) applied to different types of obligations.

Key Terms
عاقلہ (aakila): the tribal guarantors who pay diyah on behalf of a killer in accidental killing
ارش (arsh): monetary compensation for injuries or killing, especially when set by agreement
صلح (sulh): settlement or reconciliation between parties
شبه العمد (shibh al-amd): quasi-intentional killing, where death is caused by an intentional act without intent to kill

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how is diyah paid when qisas is dropped due to shubha in intentional killing, and no sulh is involved?
A) Immediately as a lump sum
B) In installments over three years
C) In installments over one year
D) The killer's 'aqila pay it immediately

Key Takeaway
In intentional killing with shubha, diyah is wajib on the killer alone, paid in three years if from the killing itself, and immediately if by sulh.

Diyah for Father Killing Son: Immediate or Deferred?
Dispute on whether diyah for father killing son is immediate or deferred

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on diyah for a father who kills his son, explain the Shafi'i counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response using qiyas and the nature of Shari'ah valuation.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, diyah for killing is always deferred—even for an intentional father who kills his son.

When a father intentionally kills his son, qisas is dropped based on the hadith 'No father is executed for his son.' Instead, diyah becomes wajib. But is this diyah payable immediately or over three years? The Hanafi school holds it is deferred by analogy to accidental killing, while Imam al-Shafi'i argues for immediate payment. This lesson unpacks the proofs behind each view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act (father kills son), the consequential hukm (diyah, no qisas), and the specific ruling: payment over three years.
This is the starting point—know what the school actually says.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that diyah is immediate in this case. Distinguish this from the Hanafi view.
The ikhtilaf is on the timing (ta'jeel vs. hall), not on the obligation of diyah itself.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i argument: (1) general principle that liability for damage is immediate; (2) deferment is a concession only for accidental killers; (3) the victim's right is immediate, so compensation must be immediate.
Shafi'i considers this intentional killing, not accidental, so no concession.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafi response: (a) valuation of human life in wealth is a departure from qiyas, established by Shari'ah as deferred; (b) just as the amount cannot be increased for intentionality, the timing cannot be changed to immediate; (c) analogy to diyat of khata and shibh 'amd.
The Hanafi proof relies on the Shari'ah's original ruling for all killing-related diyah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi says three annual installments; Shafi'i says immediate lump sum. This affects how the diyah is collected and when the heirs receive it.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باپ بیٹے کو عمد اقتل کر دے تو دیت کس کے ذمے کتنے دنوں میں واجب ہے، اقوال فقہاء قال واذا قتل الاب ابنه عمدا فالدية فى ماله فى ثلث سنين وقال الشافعى تجب حالة لان الاصل ان ما يجب بالاتلاف يجب حالا والتاجيل للتخفيف فى الخاطى وهذا عامد فلا يستحقه ولان المال وجب جبر لحقه وحقه فى نفسه حال فلا ينجبر بالمؤجل ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کو عمد قتل کر دیا تو دیت قاتل کے مال میں تین سال میں ہوگی ۔ اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ فی الحال واجب ہوگی اس لئے کہ اصل یہ ہے کہ جو مال اختلاف کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے وہ فی الحال واجب ہوگا اور خاطی کے اندرتا جیل ( مہلت) تخفیف کی غرض سے ہوتی ہے اور یہ ہوگا۔ تشریح جب باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کو قتل کر دیا تو قصاص نہیں بلکہ دیت واجب ہے پھر اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ یہ دیت مؤجل ہوگی یا معجل، ہمارا مذ ہب یہ ہے کہ مؤجل ہے جس کی ادائیگی تین سال میں کرنی پڑے گی۔ اور امام شاملی فرماتے ہیں کہ معجل ہے اور فی الحال واجب الادا ہے۔ امام شافعی نے یہ دلیل پیش کی ہے کہ جو مال کسی چیز کو تلف کرنے سے واجب ہوتا ہے وہ فی الحال واجب ہوا کرتا ہے۔ اور قتل خطاء میں بھی مال کا وجوب اتلاف نفس کی وجہ سے ہے لیکن اس کے خاطی ہونے کی وجہ سے اور معذور ہونے کی وجہ سے تخفیفاً تین سال میں ادائیگی کو واجب قراردیا گیا ہے مگر باپ یہاں خاطی نہیں ہے بلکہ عامد ہے لہذا عامد تخفیف کا مستحق یہ اس لئے کہ قیاس انکار کرتا ہے آدمی کے تقوم کا مال کے ساتھ تماثل نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور تقویم شریعت سے ثابت ہوتی ہے اور تحقیق کہ
If the father intentionally kills his son, then the diyah is on his wealth over three years. And al-Shafi'i said: it is obligatory immediately, because the principle is that wealth obligatory due to damage is obligatory immediately, and deferment is a concession for the mistaken (khati'), and this is intentional, so he does not deserve it. And because the wealth became obligatory to compensate his right, and his right is in his soul immediately, so it cannot be compensated by a deferred payment. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And when the father intentionally killed his son, the diyah is on his wealth over three years. And al-Shafi'i said: it is obligatory immediately, because the principle is that wealth obligatory due to damage is obligatory immediately, and deferment is a concession for the mistaken, and this is intentional, so he does not deserve the concession. And because the wealth became obligatory to compensate his right, and his right in his soul is immediate, so this right which is immediate cannot be compensated by a deferred payment. Explanation: When the father killed his son, qisas is not applicable; rather diyah is wajib. Then there is disagreement whether this diyah is deferred or immediate. Our school is that it is deferred, requiring payment over three years. Imam al-Shafi'i says it is immediate and wajib al-ada immediately. Imam al-Shafi'i presented this proof: Wealth that becomes obligatory due to destroying something is normally obligatory immediately. In accidental killing, the obligation is also due to destroying the soul, but due to the killer being mistaken and excused, it is deferred over three years as a concession. But here the father is not mistaken but intentional, so he does not deserve the concession. His second proof: Wealth becomes obligatory to fulfill the right of the victim, and since the father killed him immediately, the payment should also be immediate, otherwise an immediate right cannot be compensated by a deferred payment. The Hanafi proof: And we have that this is wealth obligatory due to killing, so it is deferred like the diyah of accidental and quasi-intentional killing. This is because qiyas rejects the valuation of a human with wealth due to lack of equivalence, and valuation is established by Shari'ah, and it came as deferred, not immediate, so it should not be changed, especially to increase [the burden]. And since increasing [the amount] due to intentionality is not allowed in quantity, it is also not allowed in description (i.e., timing).
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage deals specifically with the case of a father who intentionally kills his son. Since a father cannot be executed for killing his son (based on the hadith 'No father is killed for his son'), qisas is dropped and diyah becomes wajib. The Hanafi school holds that this diyah must be paid over three years, in installments, by analogy to the diyah for accidental (khata) and quasi-intentional (shibh 'amd) killing. Imam al-Shafi'i argues for immediate payment, citing the general principle that liability for damage is immediate, and deferment is only a concession for accidental killers. Shafi'i also argues that the victim's right is immediate, so compensation must be immediate. The Hanafi response is twofold: first, the valuation of a human in monetary terms is a departure from qiyas (since humans are not commodities), and this valuation came from the Shari'ah as deferred; hence it cannot be changed to immediate. Second, just as the amount of diyah cannot be increased due to intentionality (it remains the same as accidental), so too the timing (payment in installments) should not be changed to immediate. This shows the consistency of Hanafi legal reasoning in treating all forms of diyah arising from killing as deferred, regardless of intent.

Key Terms
عامد (aamid): one who acts intentionally
خاطی (khati'): one who acts accidentally or mistakenly
تاجیل (ta'jeel): deferment or postponement of payment

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school rule that diyah for a father killing his son is paid over three years?
A) Because the father is poor and needs time
B) By analogy to diyah for accidental and quasi-intentional killing
C) Because the hadith specifies three years for all diyah
D) Because the son's heirs agreed to a delay

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, diyah for killing is always deferred over three years, whether intentional or accidental, because the Shari'ah's valuation of human life in monetary terms is a concession that cannot be altered in amount or timing.

Diyah of Father Intentionally Killing Son: Mu'ajjal vs Hal
Inter-madhhab dispute on diyah timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing of diyah when a father intentionally kills his son and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Diyah for intentional killing by a father is deferred over three years, just like accidental killing.

When a father kills his son intentionally, qisas is not applied; instead, diyah becomes wajib. But the key dispute is timing: should the payment be immediate or spread over three years? This passage from al-Hidayah pits the Hanafi view (mu'ajjal) against Imam al-Shafi'i's view (hal). The reasoning draws on principles of qiyas, leniency for accidental killing, and the nature of compensation. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to see how a shared source (shari'ah) leads to different rulings through different usul.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: diyah is wajib on the father's wealth, payable over three years (mu'ajjal). No qisas.
The source text explicitly says 'on his wealth in three years'.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that any wealth due for destruction of property is immediate; deferment is only for accidental killers. This father is intentional, so no leniency.
Also: the victim's right is immediate, so compensation must also be immediate.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Hanafis argue that all diyah from killing (accidental, quasi-intentional, and intentional by a father) is mu'ajjal by shari'ah. They cite qiyas: valuation of a human by wealth is against qiyas, but shari'ah established it mu'ajjal, so we adhere.
They also reason that since the amount (100 camels) is not increased despite intentionality, the time factor should not be increased either.
4
Apply the usul principle
The Hanafi reasoning relies on the principle that when a shari'ah ruling comes contrary to qiyas, it is accepted as is, and any addition (like immediacy) requires proof.
Compare with the credit sale example: equality in value and genus still forbids credit due to suspicion of excess.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Under Hanafis, the father pays in installments over three years; under Shafi'is, he must pay immediately.
This affects whether the heirs receive the full amount at once or over time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا قتل الاب ابنه عمدا فالدية فى ماله فى ثلث سنين وقال الشافعى تجب حالة لان الاصل ان ما يجب بالاتلاف يجب حالا والتاجيل للتخفيف فى الخاطى وهذا عامد فلا يستحقه ولان المال وجب جبر لحقه وحقه فى نفسه حال فلا ينجبر بالمؤجل ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جب باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کو عمد قتل کر دیا تو دیت قاتل کے مال میں تین سال میں ہوگی ۔ اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ فی الحال واجب ہوگی اس لئے کہ اصل یہ ہے کہ جو مال اختلاف کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے وہ فی الحال واجب ہوگا اور خاطی کے اندرتا جیل ( مہلت) تخفیف کی غرض سے ہوتی ہے اور یہ عام ہے پس باپ ( عامد ) تخفیف کا مستحق نہ ہوگا اور اس لئے کہ مال بیٹے کے حق کو پورا کرنے کی غرض سے واجب ہوا ہے اور بیٹے کا حق اپنے نفس میں فی الحال ہے تو یہ حق نفس جو منجل ہے ) موجل کے ذریعہ پورا نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح جب باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کو قتل کر دیا تو قصاص نہیں بلکہ دیت واجب ہے پھر اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ یہ دیت مؤجل ہوگی یا معجل، ہمارا مذ ہب یہ ہے کہ مؤجل ہے جس کی ادائیگی تین سال میں کرنی پڑے گی۔ اور امام شاملی فرماتے ہیں کہ معجل ہے اور فی الحال واجب الادا ہے۔ امام شافعی نے یہ دلیل پیش کی ہے کہ جو مال کسی چیز کو تلف کرنے سے واجب ہوتا ہے وہ فی الحال واجب ہوا کرتا ہے۔ اور قتل خطاء میں بھی مال کا وجوب اتلاف نفس کی وجہ سے ہے لیکن اس کے خاطی ہونے کی وجہ سے اور معذور ہونے کی وجہ سے تخفیفاً تین سال میں ادائیگی کو واجب قراردیا گیا ہے مگر باپ یہاں خاطی نہیں ہے بلکہ عامد ہے لہذا عامد تخفیف کا مستحق نہ ہو گا۔ دوسری دلیل ان کی یہ ہے کہ مال اس لئے واجب ہوتا ہے تا کہ مقتول کا حق پورا ہو اور جب باپ نے اس کو فی الحال قتل کر دیا ہے تو مال کی ادائیگی بھی فی الحال ہونی چاہئے ورنہ حق منجل کی تلافی مؤجل کے ذریعہ نہ ہو گی۔ احناف کی دلیل ولنا انه مال واجب بالقتل فيكون مؤجلا كدية الخطا وشبه العمد وهذا لان القياس يأبى تقوم الآدمي بالمال لعدم التماثل والتقويم ثبت بالشرع وفد ورديه مؤجلا لا معجلا فلا يعدل عنه لا سيما الى زيادة ولما لم يجز التغليظ باعتبار العمدية قدرا لا يجوز وصفا ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ ایسا مال ہے جو قتل کی وجہ سے راجب ہوا ہے تو یہ مال مؤجل ہوگا خطاء اور شبہ عمد کی دیت کے مثل اور یہ اس لئے کہ قیاس انکار کرتا ہے آدمی کے تقوم کا مال کے ساتھ تماثل نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور تقویم شریعت سے ثابت ہوتی ہے اور تحقیق کہ شریعت وارد ہوئی ہے تقویم کے سلسلے میں مؤجل ہو کر نہ کہ بطریق مقتبل تو اس سے عدول نہیں کیا جائے گا خصوصا زیادتی کی جانب اور جب که باعتبار مقدار عمدیت کے اعتبار سے تغلیظ جائز نہ ہوئی تو وصف کے اعتبار سے بھی جائز نہ ہوگی۔ تشریح یہ حنفیہ کی دلیل ہے فرماتے ہیں کہ جو مال قتل کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے وہ مؤجل ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا اقتل خطاء اور شبہ عمد کی دیت اس کی شاہد ہے پھر انسان مالک ہے اور مال مملوک ہے اس لئے قیاس یہ چاہتا ہے کہ مال کے ذریعہ انسان کی قیمت نہ لگے کیونکہ مالک اور مملوک میں کوئی تماثل نہیں ہے ، مگر خطاء وغیرہ میں جو تقویم ثابت ہوئی ہے یہ خلاف قیاس ہے۔ لیکن شریعت سے ثابت ہے مگر یہ ثبوت بطریق تا جیل ہے نہ کہ تجمیلا تو ضروری ہوا کہ امر شرع سے عدول نہ ہو اس لئے ہم تاجیل کے قائل ہوئے ہیں۔ پھر متجل مؤجل کے مقابلہ میں زائد بھی ہے تو مورد شرع کے خلاف زیادتی کے اثبات کا کوئی تک نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ قدرو جنس میں سے ایک کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے برابری کے باوجود ادھار بیع حرام ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ شبۃ الفضل ہے۔ بہر حال جب باپ نے بیٹے کو قتل کیا تو دیت کی مقدار یہاں بھی سو اونٹ ہیں زیادہ نہیں ہیں تو اس کے عمد ا ہونے کی وجہ سے جب مقدار میں اضافہ نہیں ہوا تو وصف میں اضافہ بدرجہ اولی نہ ہوگا اور دیت کو معجل واجب نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
He (al-Quduri) said: When a father kills his son intentionally, the diyah is on his wealth over three years. Al-Shafi'i said: It becomes obligatory immediately because the principle is that wealth obligated due to destruction is immediate, and deferment is for leniency in accidental killing, and this is intentional so he does not deserve leniency, and because the wealth became obligatory to compensate his right, and his right is immediate, so it cannot be compensated by a deferred payment. Translation: Al-Quduri said: when a father kills his son intentionally, the diyah will be in the killer's wealth over three years. And al-Shafi'i said: it will be immediately obligatory because the principle is that any wealth that becomes obligatory due to destruction becomes obligatory immediately, and deferment in accidental killing is for the purpose of leniency, and this is intentional, so the father does not deserve leniency. And because the wealth became obligatory to fulfill the right of the son, and the son's right is immediate, so this immediate right of the self cannot be compensated through a deferred means. Explanation: When a father kills his son, retaliation is not performed; rather diyah is wajib. Then there is dispute whether this diyah is mu'ajjal or mu'ajjal. Our madhhab is that it is mu'ajjal, which must be paid over three years. And Imam Shafi'i says it is mu'ajjal and immediately due. Imam Shafi'i presented this proof: any wealth that becomes obligatory due to destruction of something, it is immediately due. In accidental killing too, the obligation of wealth is due to the destruction of the self, but because it is accidental and the killer is excused, leniently the payment over three years was made obligatory. But here the father is not accidental but intentional, so the intentional killer does not deserve leniency. Their second proof: wealth becomes obligatory so that the right of the killed is fulfilled. When the father killed him immediately, the payment of wealth should also be immediate, otherwise the immediate right cannot be compensated by a deferred right. And our proof: It is wealth obligatory due to killing, so it is mu'ajjal like the diyah of accidental and quasi-intentional killing. This is because qiyas rejects valuation of a human by wealth due to lack of similarity, and valuation is established by shari'ah, and verily it came mu'ajjal not mu'ajjal, so we will not deviate from it, especially towards increase. And since even with intentionality, the amount is not increased (it remains 100 camels), then the quality (time) should also not be increased. Translation: Our proof is that this is wealth obligated due to killing, so it will be mu'ajjal like the diyah of accidental and quasi-intentional. And because qiyas rejects valuation of a human by wealth due to lack of similarity, and valuation is established by shari'ah, and verily shari'ah came mu'ajjal in the matter of valuation, not mu'ajjal, so we will not deviate, especially towards increase. And since due to intentionality the amount is not increased, the quality should also not be increased. Explanation: This is the Hanafi proof. He says that any wealth obligatory due to killing is mu'ajjal. So the diyah of accidental and quasi-intentional is evidence. Then man is the owner and wealth is owned, so qiyas requires that a human not be valued by wealth because there is no similarity between owner and owned. But the valuation established in accidental etc. is contrary to qiyas. However, it is established by shari'ah, and this establishment is by way of ta'jil (deferral) not by ta'jil (immediate). So it is necessary that we do not deviate from the command of shari'ah, therefore we hold ta'jil. Moreover, the immediate is an increase over the deferred, so there is no proof for establishing an increase contrary to the shari'ah ruling. This is the reason why selling on credit becomes forbidden despite equality in value and genus because of the suspicion of excess. In any case, when the father killed the son, the amount of diyah here is also one hundred camels, not more. So when due to intentionality the amount has not increased, then increase in quality is even less likely, and the diyah will not be made immediate.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the timing of the diyah when a father intentionally kills his son. The Hanafi position, based on the statement of al-Quduri and the commentary of al-Hidayah, holds that the diyah is paid over three years (mu'ajjal). Imam al-Shafi'i argued that since the killing is intentional (amdan), the diyah should be immediate (hal) because deferment is only for accidental killing. The Hanafis respond by noting that all diyah due from killing, whether accidental, quasi-intentional, or intentional, is mu'ajjal by sharia, as the valuation of a human by wealth is contrary to qiyas but established by revelation. Since the amount of diyah is not increased due to intentionality, the payment term should not be increased either. The Hanafi proof includes analogy to accidental diyah and the principle that sharia came with deferment, so we adhere to it.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money, financial compensation paid by the killer or his aqilah for unlawful killing.
مؤجل (mu'ajjal): Deferred payment over a period of time, here three years.
خطأ (khata): Accidental killing where there was no intent.
شبه عمد (shibh amd): Quasi-intentional killing where there is intent but no weapon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, when a father intentionally kills his son, how is the diyah paid?
A) Immediately in a lump sum.
B) Over three years in installments.
C) The father pays nothing because he is the heir.
D) It is paid by the aqilah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that all diyah due from killing (except where qisas applies) is mu'ajjal over three years, and the intentionality of the father does not change this timing.

Diyat — Blood Money

Confession of Crime: Diyah on Criminal, Not on Aqilah
Ruling that a criminal's confession of injury places liability on his own wealth, not on the aqilah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a criminal's confession binds his own wealth and not the aqilah, and explain the hadith proof and legal reason.

Core Idea
Confession is binding only on the confessor, not on his aqilah, so the diyah falls on the criminal's own wealth.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a key distinction in diyah liability: when a criminal confesses to a crime, the aqilah (agnatic relatives) are not held responsible. Instead, the criminal must pay the diyah from his own wealth. The ruling is based on a hadith and the legal principle that confession does not extend beyond the confessor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a confession (iqrar) by the perpetrator of a crime that would normally require diyah on the aqilah (like accidental killing). The ruling is that the diyah is wajib on the criminal's own wealth, not on the aqilah.
The ruling applies only when the criminal confesses; if there is witness testimony or other proof, the aqilah may be liable.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is a hadith: 'Al-'awaqil la ta'mil al-'amda wa la as-sulha wa la i'tirafan' (The aqilah do not bear intentional, nor reconciliation, nor confession). This hadith is a Sunnah ahad.
The hadith is not quoted verbatim in the passage but is referenced as what 'we have narrated'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly excludes confession from the aqilah's liability. Therefore, any confession by the criminal cannot make the aqilah liable. The criminal alone bears the financial responsibility.
The exclusion is direct (mantuq) – the hadith says 'nor confession'.
4
Apply the usul principle
Additionally, the author gives a legal reason: confession (iqrar) is only effective against the confessor himself, not against others, because the confessor lacks authority (wilayah) over the aqilah. Thus, the confession does not 'appear' (yazhar) in favor of binding the aqilah.
This is a well-known rule: iqrar does not extend beyond the muqirr.
5
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
The ruling is presented as muttafaq alayh (unanimous) within the Hanafi school, and no intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab dispute is mentioned. The mufta bihi position is that the criminal pays from his own wealth.
The authority is Zahir al-Riwayah, specifically al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل جناية اعترف بها الجانى فهى فى ماله ولا يصدق على عاقلته لما روينا ولان الاقرار لا يتعدى المقر لقصور ولا يته عن غيره فلا يظهر فى حق العاقلة. ترجمہ اور ہر وہ جنایت جس کا جانی نے اعتراف کیا ہو تو وہ اس کے مال میں ہوگی اور اپنے عاقلہ کے اوپر اس کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی اسی حدیث کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں۔ اور اس لئے کہ اقرار مقر سے متعدی نہ ہوگا اس کی ولایت کے قصور کی وجہ سے اپنے غیر سے تو اقرار عاقلہ کے حق میں ظاہر نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح قتل خطاء کی دیت عاقلہ پر واجب ہوتی ہے لیکن اگر مجرم نے خود جنایت کا اقرار کیا ہو تو اس کا اقرار عاقلہ کے خلاف حجت نہ ہوگا تو یہ جرمانہ مقرا اپنے مال سے ادا کرے گا کیونکہ جو حدیث ابھی گزری تھی کہ عواقل عمد کا محل نہیں کرتے اس کے آخر میں ہے واصلحاً ولا اعترافاً ، لہذا حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اعتراف واقرار کا ضمان عاقلہ پر نہیں ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ مقر کو یہ ولایت نہیں کہ عاقلہ پر کوئی چیز لارم کردے لہذا اس کا اقرار حجبت لازمہ ہے حجت متعدیہ نہیں ہے۔ لہذا یہ اقرار عاقلہ کے حق میں ظاہر نہ ہوگا۔
And every injury for which the perpetrator confesses is on his own wealth, and he will not be believed against his aqilah due to what we have narrated, and because confession does not extend beyond the confessor due to deficiency, nor does it pass to others, so it does not appear against the aqilah. Translation: And every injury for which the perpetrator confessed, it is on his own wealth, and he will not be believed against his aqilah due to the hadith we have narrated. And because confession does not extend beyond the confessor due to deficiency of his authority over others, so the confession will not appear against the aqilah. Explanation: The diyah of accidental killing is wajib on the aqilah, but if the criminal himself confesses to the crime, his confession is not a proof against the aqilah. So this penalty will be paid from the confessor's own wealth. Because the hadith that passed earlier states that the aqilah do not bear intentional killing, nor reconciliation, nor confession. Therefore, from the hadith we learn that the guarantee of confession and acknowledgment is not on the aqilah. And because the confessor does not have the authority to make something obligatory on the aqilah, so his confession is a binding proof for himself, not a transitive proof. So this confession will not appear against the aqilah.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Hidayah that when a criminal confesses to a crime that would normally make the aqilah liable (such as accidental killing), his confession does not bind the aqilah. The diyah then becomes payable from the criminal's own wealth. The proof is a hadith indicating that the aqilah do not bear liability for intentional crimes, nor for confessions. Additionally, legal reasoning (usul) holds that a person's confession is only effective against himself, not against others, because he lacks authority over them. Therefore, the aqilah cannot be held liable based on the criminal's admission.

Key Terms
عاقلة (aqilah): The group of male agnatic relatives of the killer who are responsible for paying diyah in cases of accidental killing.
إقرار (iqrar): Confession or admission of guilt by the perpetrator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a criminal confesses to a crime that would normally make the aqilah liable, who pays the diyah?
A) The aqilah pays because confession is proof against them.
B) The criminal pays from his own wealth.
C) The state pays.
D) No one pays because confession is not accepted.

Key Takeaway
A confession of guilt places the diyah on the criminal's own wealth, not on his aqilah, due to the hadith and the legal principle that confession does not extend to others.

Diyat — Blood Money

Diyat for Father Killing Son: No Increase and Deferred
Explains Hanafi proof that diyat for father killing son is not increased and remains muajjal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyat when a father intentionally kills his son and explain the qiyas-based proof that the amount is not increased and remains deferred.

Core Idea
A father who kills his son pays the same deferred diyat as accidental killing—no increase, no immediacy.

This lesson examines a unique Hanafi ruling: when a father intentionally kills his son, the diyat (blood money) is not increased beyond the standard 100 camels, nor is it made immediate. The proof rests on analogy (qiyas) to the deferred diyat in accidental and quasi-intentional killings, and the principle that Shari'ah-established deferment cannot be overridden by mere intentionality. We will walk through the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
First, pinpoint the exact Hanafi ruling: diyat for father killing son is 100 camels, deferred (muajjal), not immediate and not increased. This is the conclusion the text defends.
2
Understand the proof structure
The text uses qiyas (analogy) to the diyat for khata (accidental) and shibh al-amd (quasi-intentional), which are deferred. The argument is that since Shari'ah established diyat as deferred, we cannot deviate towards increase or immediacy.
The proof is aqli (rational analogy), not naqli (textual).
3
Analyze the 'contrary to qiyas' point
Notice the text admits that valuing a human through wealth is contrary to qiyas (since human is malik and wealth is mamluk). Yet Shari'ah allowed it for khata etc., but only as deferred. So we stick to that deferment.
The text distinguishes between 'established contrary to qiyas' and 'then expanding it' – expansion (increase/immediacy) is not allowed.
4
Apply the principle to the father-son case
Even though the killing is intentional (amd), the amount and timing remain as in khata. The text argues that if quantity cannot be increased (because it's already set by Shari'ah for amd via qiyas?), then quality (immediacy) also cannot be increased.
The key is that the Shari'ah ruling for diyat is uniform for these cases; intentionality does not trigger increase.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah)
The thamarah al-khilaf: other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that intentional killing by a father requires increased diyat or immediate payment. Hanafi says no – the diyat remains standard and deferred.
This affects actual fiqh practice and fatwa.

شریعت وارد ہوئی ہے تقویم کے سلسلے میں مؤجل ہو کر نہ کہ بطریق مقتبل[؟] تو اس سے عدول نہیں کیا جائے گا خصوصا زیادتی کی جانب اور جب که باعتبار مقدار عمدیت کے اعتبار سے تغلیظ جائز نہ ہوئی تو وصف کے اعتبار سے بھی جائز نہ ہوگی۔ تشریح یہ حنفیہ کی دلیل ہے فرماتے ہیں کہ جو مال قتل کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے وہ مؤجل ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا اقتل خطاء اور شبہ عمد کی دیت اس کی شاہد ہے پھر انسان مالک ہے اور مال مملوک ہے اس لئے قیاس یہ چاہتا ہے کہ مال کے ذریعہ انسان کی قیمت نہ لگے کیونکہ مالک اور مملوک میں کوئی تماثل نہیں ہے ، مگر خطاء وغیرہ میں جو تقویم ثابت ہوئی ہے یہ خلاف قیاس ہے۔ لیکن شریعت سے ثابت ہے مگر یہ ثبوت بطریق تا جیل ہے نہ کہ تجميلا[؟] تو ضروری ہوا کہ امر شرع سے عدول نہ ہو اس لئے ہم تاجیل کے قائل ہوئے ہیں۔ پھر متجل[؟] مؤجل کے مقابلہ میں زائد بھی ہے تو مورد شرع کے خلاف زیادتی کے اثبات کا کوئی تک نہیں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ قدرو جنس میں سے ایک کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے برابری کے باوجود ادھار بیع حرام ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ شبۃ الفضل ہے۔ بہر حال جب باپ نے بیٹے کو قتل کیا تو دیت کی مقدار یہاں بھی سو اونٹ ہیں زیادہ نہیں ہیں تو اس کے عمد ا ہونے کی وجہ سے جب مقدار میں اضافہ نہیں ہوا تو وصف میں اضافہ بدرجہ اولی نہ ہوگا اور دیت کو معجل واجب نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
Shari'ah has come concerning valuation (taqwim) as deferred (muajjal), not as immediate (muajjal?), so it will not be deviated from, especially towards increase. And when, in terms of quantity, intensification is not permissible by virtue of being intentional, then in terms of quality also it will not be permissible. Explanation: This is the Hanafi proof. They say that wealth that becomes obligatory due to killing is deferred. Therefore, the diyah for accidental killing (khata) and quasi-intentional (shibh al-amd) is evidence of this. Then a human is a possessor (malik) and wealth is possessed (mamluk), so analogy (qiyas) demands that a human's value should not be fixed through wealth because there is no likeness between possessor and possessed. But valuation (taqwim) established in khata etc. is contrary to analogy. However, it is established from Shari'ah, but this establishment is by way of deferment (ta'jil), not by way of immediacy (ta'jil?). So it became necessary not to deviate from the command of Shari'ah, therefore we adopt deferment. Then, [something] being more than deferred is also an increase, so there is no way to establish an increase contrary to the subject of Shari'ah. This is the reason why deferred sale becomes prohibited despite equality due to the existence of one of value and type, because it contains suspicion of excess. In any case, when a father kills his son, the amount of diyah here is also one hundred camels, not more. So when due to its being intentional, there is no increase in quantity, then an increase in quality is even less likely, and the diyah will not be made obligatory as immediate (muajjal).
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi legal commentary (sharh) explaining the ruling on the diyah (blood money) when a father intentionally kills his son. The author presents the Hanafi position that the diyah remains the same as in cases of accidental killing (khata) — one hundred camels — and it is deferred (muajjal), not immediate (muajjal). The proof is based on analogy (qiyas) and the principle that Shari'ah rulings on diyah are established as deferred. The author argues that since the Shari'ah has set the diyah for khata as deferred, and the father-son case is treated similarly despite being intentional, there is no basis to increase the amount or make it immediate. The passage also draws an analogy to the prohibition of deferred sale (bay' al-ajal) where suspicion of riba arises, emphasizing that any addition beyond the Shari'ah-established ruling would be impermissible. The conclusion is clear: the diyah for a father who kills his son is one hundred camels, deferred, not increased or made immediate.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood money or compensation paid to the heirs of a homicide victim.
مؤجل (muajjal): Deferred payment; here, the diyah is not due immediately but can be paid over time (typically three years).
عمد (amd): Intentional killing with premeditation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the amount and payment term of diyah when a father intentionally kills his son?
A) 200 camels, immediate
B) 100 camels, deferred
C) 100 camels, immediate
D) 200 camels, deferred

Key Takeaway
For a father who kills his son, the Hanafi diyah remains 100 camels deferred, with no increase or immediacy, based on the Shari'ah's established deferment for blood money.

Confession Shifts Diyat from Aqila to Criminal's Wealth
Ruling with proof on diyat liability after confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who pays diyat when the criminal confesses, and explain the legal principle that prevents the aqila from being liable based on the killer's confession.

Core Idea
A confession binds only the confessor—diyat on confession is from the criminal's wealth, not the aqila.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a key question: when a criminal confesses to a crime, does the aqila (agnatic group) bear the diyat as they do in accidental killings? The Hanafi ruling is clear: the confession makes the diyat the criminal's personal responsibility. The reasoning draws on a hadith and the legal principle that iqrar (confession) is binding only on the confessor, not on third parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the criminal's confession to a crime. The ruling is that the diyat becomes wajib on the criminal's own wealth, not on the aqila.
This applies even if the crime would normally require diyat from the aqila (e.g., accidental killing).
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites a hadith narrated earlier: 'العواقل لا تحمل عمدا ولا صلحا ولا اعترافا' (the aqila do not bear responsibility for intentional killing, reconciliation, or confession).
The hadith is of ahad status but is accepted as proof in Hanafi law.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly excludes confession from the aqila's liability ('la i'tiraf'), so the diyat due on confession falls on the killer alone.
The exclusion is clear, making the dalala (indication) decisive.
4
Apply the usul principle
The principle is that iqrar (confession) is a hujjat laazima (binding proof) on the confessor but not a hujjat muta'addiya (transitive proof) against others. The confessor has no authority (wilaya) over the aqila to make them liable.
This is a fundamental rule in Hanafi jurisprudence.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Even if the confession is true, the aqila cannot be forced to pay. The criminal must pay from his own wealth, and if he cannot, the debt remains on him.
This differs from cases where diyat is proven by independent evidence (e.g., witnesses).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجرم اپنے جرم کا اقرار کر لے تو ہر لازم ہونے والی دیت اس پر لازم ہوگی یا عاقلہ پر
وكل جناية اعترف بها الجانى فهى فى ماله ولا يصدق على عاقلته لما روينا ولان الاقرار لا يتعدى المقر لقصور ولا يته عن غيره فلا يظهر فى حق العاقلة.
ترجمہ اور ہر وہ جنایت جس کا جانی نے اعتراف کیا ہو تو وہ اس کے مال میں ہوگی اور اپنے عاقلہ کے اوپر اس کی تصدیق نہیں کی جائے گی اسی حدیث کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں۔ اور اس لئے کہ اقرار مقر سے متعدی نہ ہوگا اس کی ولایت کے قصور کی وجہ سے اپنے غیر سے تو اقرار عاقلہ کے حق میں ظاہر نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح قتل خطاء کی دیت عاقلہ پر واجب ہوتی ہے لیکن اگر مجرم نے خود جنایت کا اقرار کیا ہو تو اس کا اقرار عاقلہ کے خلاف حجت نہ ہوگا تو یہ جرمانہ مقرا اپنے مال سے ادا کرے گا کیونکہ جو حدیث ابھی گزری تھی کہ عواقل عمد کا محل نہیں کرتے اس کے آخر میں ہے واصلحاً[؟] ولا اعترافاً ، لہذا حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اعتراف واقرار کا ضمان عاقلہ پر نہیں ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ مقر کو یہ ولایت نہیں کہ عاقلہ پر کوئی چیز لارم کردے لہذا اس کا اقرار حجبت[؟] لازمہ ہے حجت متعدیہ نہیں ہے۔ لہذا یہ اقرار عاقلہ کے حق میں ظاہر نہ ہوگا۔
If the criminal confesses to his crime, then every diyat that becomes obligatory will be on him or on the aqila? [Heading]
And every injury (jinaaya) which the perpetrator confesses to is in his wealth, and he is not believed against his aqila, due to what we have narrated, and because the confession does not extend beyond the confessor due to the deficiency of his authority (wilaya) over others, so it does not appear in the right of the aqila.
[Urdu translation:] And every injury which the perpetrator confesses to, then it is in his wealth, and his testimony against his aqila will not be accepted, due to the hadith which we have narrated. And because the confession does not extend from the confessor due to the deficiency of his authority over others, so the confession will not be apparent in the right of the aqila. Explanation: The diyah for accidental killing (khata) is obligatory on the aqila, but if the criminal himself confesses to the injury, then his confession is not a proof against the aqila, so this penalty will be paid from his own wealth, because in the hadith that passed that the aqila do not take responsibility for intentional (amd), in its end is 'and reconciliation and not confession', so from the hadith it is understood that the guarantee of confession and acknowledgment is not on the aqila. And because the confessor does not have the authority to make anything obligatory on the aqila, so his confession is a binding proof (hujjat laazima) but not a transitive proof (hujjat muta'addiya). Therefore this confession will not be apparent in the right of the aqila.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling (hukm) from the matn of Al-Quduri followed by a commentary. The ruling states that if a criminal confesses to a crime, the resulting diyat (blood money) is due from his own wealth, and his confession is not accepted against his aqila (the group of male agnates who normally pay diyah on behalf of a killer in accidental cases). The proof is from a hadith (narrated earlier) which indicates that the aqila do not bear responsibility for confession. The reasoning is that a confession (iqrar) is a legal admission that only binds the confessor himself, as he has no authority (wilaya) over others to make them liable. Therefore, the aqila cannot be held responsible based solely on the criminal's admission. This is an important principle in Hanafi law: the aqila's liability for diyah in khata cases is based on proof that establishes the killing, not on the killer's personal acknowledgment.

Key Terms
عاقلہ (aagila / aqila): A group of male agnates (relatives on the father's side) who are responsible for paying diyah on behalf of a killer in cases of accidental killing (khata).
اقرار (iqrar): A legal confession or admission by a party. Here, the criminal's own acknowledgment of the crime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The aqila (male agnates)
B) The killer himself from his own wealth
C) The state treasury (bayt al-mal)
D) The victim's family

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: on confession, diyat is from the criminal's wealth, not the aqila, because iqrar is binding only on the confessor.

Intentional Killing by Child or Insane Person: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on diyah for child/insane person's killing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on diyah for intentional killing by a child/insane person, identify the Shafi'i counter-argument, and apply the Hanafi tarjih to determine the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
A child or insane person's intentional killing is treated as khata, so diyah is on the aqila, not on the killer's wealth.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the legal classification of intentional killing by a child or an insane person. The passage from Al-Quduri's matn states the Hanafi position that such killing is treated as accidental (khata), placing diyah on the aqila. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that it is truly intentional (amd) except for qisas, so diyah should come from the killer's own wealth. Understanding the proofs each school uses clarifies the practical consequence: who pays the diyah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling as given in the matn: the intentional killing of a child or insane person is considered accidental (khata) and the diyah is on the aqila.
The mentally deficient (ma'tuh) receives the same ruling.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds this killing to be true intentional (amd), so diyah is from the killer's own wealth.
He also deduces kaffara and deprivation of inheritance.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the Shafi'i reasoning: the act is done with intent (qasd), which is the essence of amd. Qisas is dropped only because of lack of capacity, but other consequences remain.
He argues that the ruling of amd applies unless a specific impediment blocks it.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the two Hanafi proofs: (a) the practice of Ali (رض) who placed diyah of insane on aqila and said his amd and khata are equal; (b) qiyas: a sane accidental killer gets leniency (diyah on aqila), so a child/insane person who is more excusable deserves it more.
The Hanafi response emphasizes legal capacity as the decisive factor.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: in Hanafi fiqh, the aqila pays; in Shafi'i fiqh, the killer's wealth pays (if he has any).
Also, kaffara and inheritance effects differ between the schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بچے اور مجنون کا عمد بھی خطاء کے حکم سے ہے اور دیت عاقلہ پر ہے، اقوال فقہاء
قال و عمد الصبي والمجنون خطا و فيه الدية على العاقلة وكذالك لك جناية موجها خمس مائة فصاعد او المعتوه كالمجنون و قال الشافعی عمده عمد حتى تجب الدية فى ماله لانه عمد حقيقة اذالعمد هو القصد غير انه تخلف عنه أحد حكميه وهو القصاص فينسحب عليه حكمه الأخر وهو الوجوب في ماله ولهذا تجب الكفارة به و يحرم عن الميراث على اصله لانهما يتعلقان بالقتل
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور بچہ اور مجنون کا عمد خطاء ہے اور اس میں عاقلہ کے اوپر دیت ہے اور ایسے ہی ہر وہ جنایت جس کا موجب پانچ سو درہم ہو یا زیادہ ار معتوه مثل مجنون کے ہے اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اس کا عمد عد ہے یہاں تک کہ اس کے مال میں دیت واجب ہو گی۔ اس لئے کہ یہ حقیقۂ عمد ہے اس لئے کہ عمد وہ قصد وارادہ ہے علاوہ اس بات کے عمد سے اس کے دو حکموں میں سے ایک مختلف ہو گیا اور وہ قصاص ہے تو اس پر اس کا دوسرا حکم متفرع ہو گا اور وہ اس کے مال میں وجوب ہے اور اسی وجہ سے ( عمد ہونے کی وجہ سے ) اس قتل کی وجہ سے کفارہ واجب اور میراث سے محروم ہے شافعی کی اصل کے مطابق ۔ اس لئے کہ یہ دونوں قتل سے متعلق ہیں۔ تشریح قتل عمد میں اگر شبہ ہو جائے تو جو دنیت واجب ہوگی۔ وہ قاتل کے مال میں ہوگی۔ لیکن اگر بچہ یا مجنون یا معتوہ نے عمد اقتل کر دیا تو قصاص نہیں کیونکہ وہ غیر مکلف ہے اور اگر خطا قتل کیا ہو تو بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ لیکن اب سوال یہ ہے کہ یہ دیت بچہ اور مجنون کے مال میں ہوگی۔ یا عاقلہ پر، ہمارے نزدیک اس کا وجوب عاقلہ پر ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس کا وجوب قاتل کے مال میں ہے۔
ہم نے ان کے عد کو خطا ر قراردیا ہے اور خطاء کی دیت عاقلہ پر ہے لہذا یہاں بھی دیت عاقلہ پر واجب ہوگی۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ عد تو عمد ہی ہے لیکن بچہ یا مجنون ہونے کی وجہ سے ہم نے قصاص کو چھوڑ دیا جو کہ قتل عمد کا موجب تھا۔ اور اس کا دوسرا موجب یہ ہے کہ دیت کا وجوب قاتل کے مال میں ہو لہذا ہم نے ایک موجب کو چھوڑ دیا لیکن دوسرا باقی رکھا یعنی دیت کو بچہ کے مال میں واجب کی کیونکہ یہ فعل عمد ہے۔
اور یہی وجہ ہے کہ امام شافعی کے اصول کے مطابق بچہ اور مجنون پر اس کے عمد ہونے کی وجہ سے کفارہ بھی واجب ہے۔ اور اس کو میراث سے محروم بھی کیا جائے گا کیونکہ وجوب کفارہ اور ارث سے حرمان قتل کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور قتل یہاں موجود ہے۔ یہ امام شافعی کے دلائل ختم ہو گئے۔ احناف کی دلیل
ولنا ما روى عن على رضى الله عنه انه جعل عقل المجنون على عاقلته و قال عمده و خطأه سواء ولان الصبي مظنة المرحمة والعاقل الخاطى لما استحق التخفيف حتى وجبت الدية على العاقلة فالضبي وهو اعذر اولى بهذا التخفيف
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل وہ ہے جو علی سے مروی ہے کہ انہوں نے مجنون کی دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر قرار دی اور یوں فرمایا کہ اس کا عمد اور اس کی خطاء دونوں برابر ہیں اور اس لئے کہ بچہ محل ترحم ہے اور عاقل خاطی جب تخفیف کا مستحق ہو گیا یہاں تک کہ عاقلہ پر دیت واجب ہوئی تو بچہ حالانکہ وہ زیادہ معذور ہے ( عاقل خاطی سے ) اس تخفیف کا زیادہ مستحق ہے۔ تشریح ہماری دلیل اوّل فرمان حضرت علی کہ مجنون کا عمد اور خطاء دونوں برابر ہیں اور آپ نے عمل بھی یہی کیا کہ مجنون کی دیت عاقلہ پر واجب فرمائی۔ دوسری دلیل یہ بھی ہے کہ بچہ ترحم وشفقت کا مکمل ہے اور جب آپ نے عاقل خاطی پر اس کے معذور ہونے کی وجہ سے تخفیف کر کے دیت کو عاقلہ پر واجب کر دیا تو بچہ اس سے بھی زیادہ معذور ہے لہذا اس کو یہ تخفیف بدرجہ اولی ملنی چاہیئے ۔
[Heading] The intentional (amd) of a child and an insane person is considered accidental (khata), and the diyah is on the aqila. Statements of Jurists:
Al-Quduri said: The intentional killing of a child and an insane person is accidental, and the diyah for it is on the aqila, and likewise every injury whose liability is five hundred dirhams or more, and the mentally deficient (ma'tuh) is like the insane. Al-Shafi'i said: His intentional killing is true intentional (amd), so that the diyah becomes obligatory in his wealth, because it is truly intentional, for intentional is the intent and will, except that one of its two rulings (which is qisas) is omitted, so its other ruling applies, which is obligation in his wealth. And for this reason, expiation (kaffara) becomes obligatory for it, and he is deprived of inheritance according to his (Shafi'i's) principle, because both are related to killing.
[Urdu translation and commentary elaborate the positions and then present Hanafi evidence:] Our proof is what is narrated from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he placed the 'aql (diyah) of the insane on his aqila and said: His intentional and his accidental are equal. And because the child is deserving of mercy, and the sane accidental killer (al-aqil al-khati) when he deserved leniency such that the diyah was made obligatory on the aqila, then the child, who is even more excusable, is more deserving of this leniency.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents a clear inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the legal classification of intentional killing by a child or an insane person. The matn from Al-Quduri states the Hanafi position: such killing is treated as accidental (khata), so the diyah is upon the aqila (the male agnates). Imam al-Shafi'i argues that it is truly intentional (amd) because the act is done with intent, but qisas (retaliation) is dropped due to lack of legal capacity. Therefore, the other consequence of intentional killing applies: the diyah is in the killer's own wealth, and expiation (kaffara) is required, and the killer is deprived of inheritance. The Hanafi commentary rebuts this using two proofs: first, the practice of Caliph Ali (رضي الله عنه) who placed the diyah of an insane person on his aqila and stated that his intentional and accidental are equal. Second, an argument by analogy: since a sane accidental killer gets leniency (diyah on aqila rather than from his own wealth), a child who is even more deserving of mercy and excuse should certainly receive that leniency. Thus, the Hanafi position is that the diyah for a child or insane person's intentional killing is on the aqila, not on the killer's own wealth.

Key Terms
صبی (sabi): A child who has not reached puberty; not legally responsible (ghayr mukallaf).
مجنون (majnoon): An insane person lacking legal capacity due to mental illness.
معتوه (ma'tuh): A person with mental deficiency or insanity; treated like the insane in this ruling.
عاقلہ (aqila): Group of male agnates responsible for paying diyah in khata cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The child himself (from his own wealth)
B) The aqila (male agnates)
C) The state
D) No diyat is due

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school treats intentional killing by a child or insane person as accidental (khata) for liability, placing diyah on the aqila.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
12 min
Liability for Murder by a Child or Insane Person: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on diyat liability for child/insane killer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school treats the intentional killing by a child or insane person as khata and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A child or insane person's intentional act is not legally 'amd due to lack of intellect; thus diyat falls on the 'aqila.

This lesson examines a key dispute in Islamic criminal law: how to classify a killing committed intentionally by someone who lacks full legal capacity. The Hanafi school holds that such a killing is treated as khata (unintentional), shifting blood money to the 'aqila. Imam al-Shafi'i argues it remains 'amd, making the killer's own property liable. We will explore the proofs and the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the Hanafi ruling
The issue is whether the deliberate killing by a child or insane person is legally 'amd or khata. The Hanafi ruling: it is khata, so diyat is on the 'aqila.
The ruling applies to injuries with diyat of 500 dirhams or more.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its dalil
Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is 'amd because the act is intentional; the only dropped consequence is qisas due to lack of capacity. The other consequences (diyat on property, kaffarah, deprivation of inheritance) remain.
Shafi'i bases this on the reality of intent ('amd) as intent to kill.
3
Trace the Hanafi proof
Hanafi relies on (1) hadith of 'Ali (ra) that the insane's 'amd and khata are equal, placing diyat on 'aqila; (2) qiyas: if a rational adult who errs gets leniency (diyat on 'aqila), the child is even more excusable.
The qiyas uses the illa of the need for leniency and mercy.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
Hanafis deny that true 'amd exists: 'amd requires knowledge, which requires intellect; the insane lacks intellect, the child has deficient intellect, so their act is like that of a sleeper. Also, they are not subject to punishment (pen lifted) so no kaffarah or inheritance deprivation.
The response refutes the Shafi'i claim that the act is truly 'amd.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi → diyat on 'aqila, no kaffarah, normal inheritance. Shafi'i → diyat on killer's property, kaffarah wajib, deprived of inheritance from victim.
The dispute has significant financial and spiritual implications.

Source Text

Book of Blood Money. The translation of Quduri: And the intentional act of a child and an insane person is [treated as] unintentional (khata), and the blood money is upon the 'aqila. And similarly every injury the consequence of which is five hundred dirhams or more, and the insane like a madman. And al-Shafi'i said: That is intentional, even to the point that the blood money becomes obligatory on his own property. Because this is the reality of intentionality. Because intentionality is intent and volition. Aside from the fact that from intentionality one of its two rulings is different, and that is qisas, so its other ruling becomes derivative upon that, and that is obligation on his property. And for that same reason (due to being intentional), expiation (kaffarah) becomes obligatory due to this killing and he is deprived of inheritance, according to al-Shafi'i's principle. Because both of these are related to killing. Commentary: If there is doubt in intentional killing, the blood money that becomes obligatory will be on the killer's property. But if a child or an insane person (ma'tuh) intentionally kills, there is no qisas because he is not legally responsible (mukallaf). And if he killed unintentionally, the ruling is the same. But now the question is whether this blood money is on the property of the child and insane person, or on the 'aqila. According to us, its obligation is on the 'aqila. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, its obligation is on the killer's property. We have declared their intentional act as unintentional, and the blood money of unintentional (killing) is on the 'aqila, so here too the blood money is obligatory on the 'aqila. Imam al-Shafi'i said: The act is indeed intentional, but due to the child or insane person we abandon qisas which was the consequence of intentional killing; and its other consequence is that the blood money is obligatory on the killer's property. So we left one consequence but kept the other, i.e., the blood money is obligatory on the child's property because this act is intentional. And this is why according to Imam al-Shafi'i's principle, expiation is also obligatory on the child and insane person due to its being intentional. And he will also be deprived of inheritance, because the obligation of expiation and deprivation of inheritance are due to killing, and killing is present here. This ends the proofs of Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi proof: And our proof is what is narrated from 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) that he placed the blood money of the insane on his 'aqila, and said: His intentional and his unintentional are equal. And because a child is deserving of mercy, and when a rational person who errs (al-‘āqil al-khāṭi’) is entitled to leniency such that the blood money is made obligatory on the 'aqila, then the child – being more excused – is even more entitled to this leniency. Response to Imam al-Shafi'i's argument: And we do not concede the verification of intentionality, because it is contingent upon knowledge, and knowledge is by intellect. The insane lacks intellect, and the child has deficient intellect, so how can intent be realized from them? And each of them becomes like a sleeping person. And deprivation of inheritance is a punishment, and these two are not deserving of punishment. And expiation (kaffarah) – as its name suggests – is a covering, and there is no sin to cover, because the pen is lifted from them.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage presents a complete inter-madhhab dispute regarding the legal classification and liability of a killing committed by a child (under the age of puberty) or an insane person (including a ma'tuh, i.e., an insane person). The author states the ruling from the Matn (Quduri): such a killing is treated as khata (unintentional), and the diyat (blood money) is upon the 'aqila (the tribal group/family of the killer, not the killer's own property). This ruling applies to any injury whose maximum compensation is 500 dirhams or more. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that the act is truly intentional ('amd) because the kill is done with intent; the only reason one misses qisas is the lack of capacity, but the other consequence of intentional killing (diyah on the killer's property) remains. The Hanafis respond with two proofs: first, the hadith of 'Ali (ra) who said that the insane's intentional and unintentional are equal, and he placed the diyat on the 'aqila. Second, qiyas (analogy) with an adult who commits khata: since the adult who errs gets leniency (diyah on 'aqila), the child is even more deserving of leniency because he is more excusable. Then they refute al-Shafi'i's argument: they deny that true 'amd exists from such persons because 'amd requires knowledge, which in turn requires intellect; the insane has no intellect, the child has deficient intellect, so their act is like that of a sleeping person (no legal intent). Furthermore, deprivation of inheritance is a punishment, but these persons are not subject to punishment; similarly, kaffarah is a covering for sin, but there is no sin from them because the pen is lifted (they are not legally responsible). Thus the Hanafi position is that diyah is on the 'aqila, and no kaffarah or deprivation of inheritance applies.

Key Terms
عاقله ('āqila): The paternal relatives (tribal group) who are responsible for paying diyah on behalf of a killer who committed khata.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for killing or injuring, fixed by shari'ah.
عمد ('amd): Intentional killing or injury with the intent to cause harm.
خطاء (khaṭā'): Unintentional killing or injury, where there is no intent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) On the 'aqila (paternal relatives)
C) On the state treasury
D) No diyat is due

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies intentional killing by a child or insane person as khata, making the 'aqila liable for diyat, with no kaffarah or inheritance deprivation.

Diyah for Causing Miscarriage: The Ghurrah
Ruling on diyah for fetal death due to assault on mother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling (hukm) for causing a stillborn miscarriage, define the ghurrah, and explain why the ruling overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
The ghurrah of 500 dirhams is wajib for causing a stillborn miscarriage, fixed by hadith over qiyas.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on diyah for causing a woman to miscarry a stillborn child. We will explore the definition of the foetus (janeen), the fixed compensation known as ghurrah, and the interesting interplay between ruling and qiyas. Understanding this helps clarify how the Hanafi school sometimes bases rulings on specific evidence rather than pure analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is striking a pregnant woman causing a stillborn foetus. The ruling is a fixed compensation called ghurrah.
2
Define the ghurrah linguistically and legally
Ghurrah originally means a white mark on a horse's forehead; legally it is half a tenth of diyah (500 dirhams).
For both male and female foetuses, the amount is 500 dirhams.
3
Locate the implicit dalil
Though not quoted, the ruling derives from a well-known hadith where the Prophet ﷺ judged with a ghurrah. The school relies on this specific evidence.
The hadith is Sunnah ahad, transmitted by Abu Dawood and others.
4
Contrast with qiyas
The author notes that qiyas would require certainty of the foetus's life at the time of the blow, which is lacking. Thus, qiyas would suggest no compensation.
The ruling overrides qiyas because the specific hadith takes precedence.
5
Apply the ruling to male vs female foetus
For a male foetus, ghurrah is half a tenth of a man's diyah (500 dirhams); for a female, it is one tenth of a woman's diyah (500 dirhams). Both equal 500 dirhams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجنان
ترجمہ فصل ہے جنین کے بیان میں
تشریح جنین اس بچہ کو کہتے ہیں جو ابھی پیٹ میں ہے ، ج ، ن ہمارہ میں اخفاء کے معنی ہیں اور بچہ خفی ہوتا ہے اس وجہ سے اس کو جنین کہتے ہیں اس وجہ سے جن کو بھی جن کہتے ہیں کیونکہ وہ آدمی کی نظر سے پوشیدہ رہتے ہیں اور جنین قبل ولادت گویا اپنی ماں کا جز ہے اور اس کے بعض احکام مخصوص ہیں جن کو یہاں بیان کیا جا رہا ہے۔
عورت کے پیٹ پر مارا عورت نے جنین گراد یا اس میں رواج ہے ، غرہ کا مصداق
قال و اذا ضرب بطن امرأة فالقت جنينا ميتا ففيه غرة وهى نصف عشر الدية قال رضى الله عنه معناه دية الرجل وهذا فى الذكر و فى الانثى عشر دية المرأة وكل منهما خمس مائة درهم والقياس ان لا يجب شيء لانه لم يتيقن بحياته والظاهر لا يصلح حجة للاستحقاق
Section on the Foetus. Translation: A section on the description of the foetus. Explanation: The foetus (janeen) is the child that is still in the womb. From the root j-n-n meaning concealment, the child is hidden, so it is called janeen. Similarly, jinn are called jinn because they are hidden from sight. And the foetus before birth is as if part of its mother, and it has some specific rulings which are being explained here. He struck a woman's belly, she miscarried a [؟] foetus, it is common, the subject of ghurrah. He said: If one strikes a woman's belly and she miscarries a dead foetus, then there is a ghurrah, which is half of a tenth of the diyah. He (the author, may Allah be pleased with him) said: Its meaning is the diyah of a man. And this [is] for the male, and for the female [it is] a tenth of the diyah of a woman, and each of these is five hundred dirhams. And the analogy (qiyas) is that nothing is obligatory because his life is not certain, and the apparent circumstance is not a valid proof for entitlement.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage introduces a new section (fasl) on the rulings pertaining to the foetus (janeen). The author first defines janeen linguistically as the child hidden in the womb. Then the ruling is given: If someone strikes a pregnant woman's belly and she miscarries a stillborn foetus (i.e., delivered dead), the compensation is a ghurrah. Ghurrah is defined as half of a tenth of the full diyah. For a male foetus, it is half a tenth of the diyah of a man, and for a female foetus, it is a tenth of the diyah of a woman. In both cases, the amount is 500 dirhams (since full diyah of a man is 10,000 dirhams, half a tenth = 500; diyah of a woman is 5,000 dirhams, one tenth = 500). The author notes that the qiyas (analogy) would suggest nothing is due because the foetus's life at the time of the blow is not certain (there is no yqeen of life), and outward appearances (dhahir) are not sufficient for establishing entitlement. However, the ruling is given based on specific evidence (likely hadith), overriding qiyas. The Hanafi position is that this ghurrah is obligatory as a fixed amount, and it is paid by the offender's 'aqila (as per khata) or by the offender if it is intentional but without qisas. The passage sets the stage for further detail.

Key Terms
جنین (janīn): The foetus in the womb before birth.
غرة (ghurrah): A specific fixed compensation for causing miscarriage: half a tenth of full diyah (500 dirhams).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the amount of the ghurrah for causing an unborn male foetus to be stillborn?
A) Full diyah of a man (10,000 dirhams)
B) Half a tenth of the diyah of a man (500 dirhams)
C) One tenth of the diyah of a man (1,000 dirhams)
D) No compensation

Key Takeaway
The ghurrah of 500 dirhams is the fixed Hanafi compensation for a stillborn foetus, established by hadith despite qiyas to the contrary.
